# Portuguese Curriculum — MS Sequence (BP)

Generated from `docs/units/`. Filter: `variant in (bp, shared)` AND `status == published`. Ordered by `sequence_position` ascending.

**Total units:** 152

---

## Unit 1 — Identity Statements (Eu sou)

*Slug: `a1-ser-identity` · Sequence position: 1.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `self-introduction`, `ser-vs-estar`, `definite-articles`, `adjective-agreement`

### Outcomes

- Introduce themselves by name
- State their nationality
- State their profession
- State their marital status
- Understand gender agreement basics

### Vocabulary

1. Eu (I)
2. sou (am)
3. Articles: o (masculine), a (feminine)
4. Nationalities: brasileiro/brasileira, americano/americana, português/portuguesa
5. Professions: professor/professora, estudante, médico/médica, engenheiro/engenheira
6. Marital status: casado/casada, solteiro/solteira, divorciado/divorciada, viúvo/viúva

### Grammar

- First person singular: Eu sou
- Gender agreement for adjectives (o/a endings)
- Definite articles with names: o [masculine name], a [feminine name]

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu sou o João / Eu sou a Maria (name)
- Eu sou brasileiro / Eu sou brasileira (nationality)
- Eu sou americano / Eu sou americana
- Eu sou professor / Eu sou professora (profession)
- Eu sou estudante
- Eu sou casado / Eu sou casada (marital status)
- Eu sou solteiro / Eu sou solteira
- Eu sou divorciado / Eu sou divorciada

## Unit 2 — Origin with Contractions (Eu sou de)

*Slug: `a1-sou-de-contracoes` · Sequence position: 2.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `common-prepositions`, `preposition-article-contractions`

### Outcomes

- State where they're from using correct contractions
- Understand when articles are needed with place names
- Combine Units 1 & 2: "Eu sou brasileiro. Eu sou de São Paulo."

### Vocabulary

- de (from/of)
- Country/city names: Brasil, Estados Unidos, Portugal, São Paulo, Rio, etc.
- Articles: o, a, os, as (for contractions)

### Grammar

- Preposition "de" + origin
- Contractions: de + o = do, de + a = da, de + os = dos, de + as = das
- When to use contractions vs. plain "de"

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu sou de São Paulo
- Eu sou do Brasil
- Eu sou do Rio de Janeiro
- Eu sou da Bahia
- Eu sou dos Estados Unidos
- Eu sou da Inglaterra

## Unit 3 — Location/Residence (Eu moro em)

*Slug: `a1-moro-em` · Sequence position: 3.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `regular-ar-conjugation`, `common-prepositions`, `preposition-article-contractions`

### Outcomes

- State where they live using correct contractions
- Combine with previous units for full introduction
- Understand difference between "sou de" (origin) and "moro em" (residence)

### Vocabulary

- moro (I live) - first regular -AR verb introduced
- em (in/at/on)
- Place names: São Paulo, Rio, Brasil, Estados Unidos, etc.
- Articles: o, a, os, as (for contractions with em)

### Grammar

- First regular -AR verb: moro (I live)
- Preposition "em" + location
- Contractions: em + o = no, em + a = na, em + os = nos, em + as = nas
- When to use contractions vs. plain "em"

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu moro em São Paulo
- Eu moro no Brasil
- Eu moro no Rio de Janeiro
- Eu moro na Bahia
- Eu moro nos Estados Unidos
- Eu moro na Inglaterra

## Unit 4 — Street Address (Eu moro na rua/avenida)

*Slug: `a1-moro-rua-avenida` · Sequence position: 4.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `common-prepositions`, `preposition-article-contractions`

### Outcomes

- Give a complete address (city + street)
- Understand that street/avenue names don't take articles
- Provide increasingly specific location information

### Vocabulary

- rua (street) - feminine
- avenida (avenue) - feminine
- Street names: Paulista, Ipiranga, Copacabana, etc.

### Grammar

- Specific address with "na" (em + a = na)
- Both "rua" and "avenida" are feminine → always "na"
- No article before street names (na Rua Paulista, not na Rua da Paulista)

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu moro na Rua Paulista
- Eu moro na Avenida Copacabana
- Eu moro na Rua Augusta
- Eu moro em São Paulo, na Rua Consolação

## Unit 5 — Workplace (Eu trabalho em/no/na)

*Slug: `a1-trabalho-em` · Sequence position: 5.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `regular-ar-conjugation`, `common-prepositions`, `preposition-article-contractions`, `work-professions`

### Outcomes

- State where they work using correct contractions
- Distinguish between indefinite (em um/uma) and definite (no/na)
- Recognize gender of workplace nouns

### Vocabulary

- trabalho (I work) - second regular -AR verb
- Workplace locations:
  - hospital (masculine) → no hospital
  - escola (feminine) → na escola
  - universidade (feminine) → na universidade
  - banco (masculine) → no banco
  - restaurante (masculine) → no restaurante
  - loja (feminine) → na loja
  - empresa (feminine) → na empresa
  - escritório (masculine) → no escritório

### Grammar

- Second regular -AR verb: trabalho (I work)
- Reusing "em" contractions from Unit 3 (no/na/nos/nas)
- Gender awareness: which workplaces are masculine/feminine

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu trabalho em um hospital
- Eu trabalho no hospital São Lucas
- Eu trabalho na universidade
- Eu trabalho em um banco
- Eu trabalho na escola
- Eu trabalho em casa

## Unit 6 — Languages (Eu falo) + Conjunction e

*Slug: `a1-falo-linguas` · Sequence position: 6.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `regular-ar-conjugation`, `conjunctions`

### Outcomes

- State which languages they speak
- Use "um pouco de" for limited proficiency
- **Combine multiple items with "e"** - works across all previous units
- Add adverbs to describe proficiency level
- Create more natural, flowing sentences by combining information

### Vocabulary

- falo (I speak) - third regular -AR verb
- **e (and)** - KEY CONJUNCTION
- Languages:
  - português (Portuguese) - masculine
  - inglês (English) - masculine
  - espanhol (Spanish) - masculine
  - francês (French) - masculine
  - alemão (German) - masculine
  - italiano (Italian) - masculine
  - chinês (Chinese) - masculine
- um pouco de (a little bit of)
- bem (well)

### Grammar

- Third regular -AR verb: falo (I speak)
- Direct object (no preposition needed): "Eu falo português" (not "em português")
- **Conjunction "e" (and)** - combining items in a list
- Adverbs of degree: bem, um pouco
- Multiple uses of "e": languages, combining previous units

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu falo português
- Eu falo inglês
- Eu falo português e inglês
- Eu falo um pouco de espanhol
- Eu falo francês bem
- Eu sou brasileiro e professor (combining Unit 1)
- Eu moro e trabalho em São Paulo (combining Units 3 & 5)

## Unit 7 — Transportation (Eu ando de/a pé)

*Slug: `a1-ando-transportes` · Sequence position: 7.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `regular-ar-conjugation`, `ir-transportation`

### Outcomes

- Express how they get around
- Use fourth -AR verb (reinforcing the -o pattern)
- Distinguish "andar de" + transport vs "andar a pé"
- Talk about daily transportation

### Vocabulary

- ando (I walk/ride) - fourth regular -AR verb
- de (by/of) - used with transport
- a pé (on foot) - fixed expression
- Example transports:
  - ônibus (bus)
  - bicicleta (bicycle)
  - carro (car)

### Grammar

- Fourth regular -AR verb: ando (I walk/ride)
- "Ando de" + transport = ride/go by [transport]
- "Ando a pé" = walk (on foot) - fixed expression
- No articles with transport in "ando de" construction

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu ando de ônibus
- Eu ando de bicicleta
- Eu ando de carro
- Eu ando a pé
- Eu ando de ônibus todo dia (I take the bus every day)

## Unit 8 — Going by Transport (Eu vou de)

*Slug: `a1-vou-de-transporte` · Sequence position: 8.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `irregular-verb-conjugation`, `ir-transportation`

### Outcomes

- Express going by a method of transport
- Use the irregular verb vou
- Distinguish between "ando de" and "vou de"

### Vocabulary

- vou (I go) - **IRREGULAR** verb
- Same transports from Unit 7: ônibus, bicicleta, carro

### Grammar

- First irregular motion verb: vou (I go)
- "Vou de" + transport (I go by [transport])
- Parallel structure to Unit 7's "ando de"

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu vou de ônibus (I go by bus)
- Eu vou de bicicleta (I go by bicycle)
- Eu vou de carro (I go by car)
- Eu vou a pé (I go on foot)

## Unit 9 — Going to Places (Eu vou a/para)

*Slug: `a1-vou-a-para` · Sequence position: 9.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `irregular-verb-conjugation`, `common-prepositions`

### Outcomes

- Express WHERE they go (destinations)
- Combine with Unit 7: "Eu vou ao trabalho de ônibus" (where + how)
- Use contractions with "a" (ao/à)
- Distinguish between "a" and "para"

### Vocabulary

- a (to - direction)
- para (to/for - destination)
- Contractions: ao (a + o), à (a + a)
- Example destinations:
  - trabalho (work)
  - escola (school)
  - casa (home)

### Grammar

- "Vou a/ao/à" + place (going to a specific place)
- "Vou para" + place (going toward - often used with casa)
- Contractions: a + o = ao, a + a = à
- No contraction with para (always "para casa", never *paro)

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu vou ao trabalho (I go to work)
- Eu vou à escola (I go to school)
- Eu vou para casa (I go home)
- Eu vou ao banco (I go to the bank)
- Eu vou à universidade (I go to the university)
- Eu vou ao trabalho de ônibus (combining Units 7+8)

## Unit 10 — Multiple Languages with Varying Proficiency (e um pouco de)

*Slug: `a1-um-pouco-de` · Sequence position: 10.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `common-expressions`

### Outcomes

- Express multiple languages with different proficiency levels
- Combine fluent and partial language knowledge naturally
- Use comma + "e" for lists of three or more items
- Add nuance with "bem", "um pouco", "também"

### Vocabulary

- More languages (if needed)
- também (also)
- mas (but)

### Grammar

- Complex combinations: fluent language + "e" + partial language
- "e um pouco de" construction for adding languages with limited proficiency
- Natural sentence flow with multiple proficiency levels

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu falo português e inglês, e um pouco de espanhol
- Eu falo inglês bem, e um pouco de francês
- Eu falo português, inglês e um pouco de alemão
- Eu falo espanhol, e um pouco de italiano também
- Eu falo português, mas eu falo um pouco de inglês

## Unit 11 — Dropping the Pronoun Eu (Pro-drop)

*Slug: `a1-pro-drop` · Sequence position: 11.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `personal-pronouns`, `subject-identification`

### Outcomes

- Speak more naturally like native speakers
- Understand that verb endings indicate the subject
- Recognize both forms (with and without "eu")
- Choose when to include "eu" for emphasis

### Vocabulary

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

### Grammar

- Optional subject pronouns in Portuguese
- Verb endings carry the person/number information
- "-o" ending = I (eu), so "eu" becomes redundant
- More natural, flowing speech

## Unit 12 — Temporary States and Current Location (estou - irregular)

*Slug: `a1-estou-irregular` · Sequence position: 12.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `ser-vs-estar`, `irregular-verb-conjugation`

### Outcomes

- Express how they feel right now (temporary)
- Say where they are currently (not where they live - that's moro)
- Understand the ser vs estar distinction
- Distinguish permanent (sou) from temporary (estou)

### Vocabulary

- estou (I am) - **IRREGULAR** verb, second "to be" verb
- Temporary states/feelings:
  - cansado/cansada (tired)
  - feliz (happy)
  - triste (sad)
  - doente (sick)
  - ocupado/ocupada (busy)
  - com fome (hungry)
  - com sede (thirsty)
- Current location:
  - em casa (at home)
  - no trabalho (at work)
  - na escola (at school)
- agora (now), hoje (today)

### Grammar

- Second irregular verb: estou (I am - temporary/location)
- **Critical distinction: ser vs estar**
  - **ser (sou)** = permanent/inherent qualities, identity
  - **estar (estou)** = temporary states, current location, conditions
- Temporary states require estar, not ser
- Current location uses estar

### Exemplar sentences

- Estou cansado (I'm tired right now)
- Estou feliz hoje (I'm happy today)
- Estou em casa (I'm at home now)
- Estou no trabalho (I'm at work)
- Estou com fome (I'm hungry)
- Estou doente (I'm sick)

## Unit 13 — Location at Someone's House (na casa de)

*Slug: `a1-na-casa-de` · Sequence position: 13.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `preposition-article-contractions`

### Outcomes

- Distinguish "em casa" (my home) from "na casa de" (someone else's home)
- Express whose house they're at using correct contractions
- Combine multiple contraction rules naturally
- Use possessive "de" with people's names
- Master the triple contraction pattern

### Vocabulary

- casa de (house of)
- People's names: João, Maria, Pedro, Ana
- Family members: pai (father), mãe (mother), irmão (brother), irmã (sister), amigo/amiga (friend)
- Revisit: de + articles = do/da/dos/das

### Grammar

- Fixed expression: "em casa" (at home - NO article) = at MY home
- Location at someone else's house: "na casa de [person]"
- Triple contraction: **na casa do/da/dos/das**
- Combining contractions:
  - em + a = na (from Unit 3)
  - de + o/a/os/as = do/da/dos/das (from Unit 2)
  - Together: na casa + de + article = **na casa do/da/dos/das**
- Possessive with "de": na casa do João (João's house), na casa da Maria (Maria's house)

### Exemplar sentences

- Estou em casa (at my home)
- Estou na casa do João (at João's house)
- Estou na casa da Maria (at Maria's house)
- Estou na casa do Pedro (at Pedro's house)
- Estou na casa da Ana (at Ana's house)
- Vou à casa do meu amigo (I'm going to my friend's house)
- Ele está na casa da irmã (He's at his sister's house)

## Unit 14 — Possessive Adjectives: Meu/Minha (My)

*Slug: `a1-poss-meu` · Sequence position: 14.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `possessives`

### Outcomes

- **Talk about family members using meu/minha**
- **Understand gender agreement with possessives**
- Express relationships (my brother, my sister, my friend)
- Combine possessives with location (na casa do meu pai)
- Use possessives with verbs learned so far (meu pai mora, minha mãe trabalha)

### Vocabulary

- **meu/minha** (my - masculine/feminine singular) - **FIRST POSSESSIVE ADJECTIVES**
- Family members:
  - pai (father) - masculine
  - mãe (mother) - feminine
  - irmão (brother) - masculine
  - irmã (sister) - feminine
  - filho/filha (son/daughter)
  - avô/avó (grandfather/grandmother)
- amigo/amiga (friend - masculine/feminine)
- família (family) - feminine

### Grammar

- **Possessive adjectives: meu/minha (my) - FOUNDATIONAL CONCEPT**
  - **meu** = my (masculine singular): meu irmão, meu amigo, meu pai
  - **minha** = my (feminine singular): minha irmã, minha amiga, minha mãe
  - **CRITICAL RULE: possessive agrees with the THING POSSESSED, not the speaker**
- Position: possessive + noun (no article needed)
- Used primarily with people (family members, friends) and relationships
- Can combine with estar location: "Estou na casa do meu irmão"

### Exemplar sentences

- Meu pai mora no Rio (My father lives in Rio)
- Minha mãe trabalha na escola (My mother works at the school)
- Meu irmão fala português e inglês (My brother speaks Portuguese and English)
- Minha irmã é médica (My sister is a doctor)
- Meu amigo trabalha aqui (My friend works here)
- Minha amiga mora em São Paulo (My friend (f) lives in São Paulo)
- Minha família é brasileira (My family is Brazilian)
- Estou na casa do meu pai (I'm at my father's house)

## Unit 15 — Numbers 0-20 (Cardinal Numbers - Foundation)

*Slug: `a1-num-0-20` · Sequence position: 15.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `numbers`

### Outcomes

- Count from 0 to 20
- Express quantities up to 20
- Use correct gender agreement for um/uma and dois/duas
- Answer "quantos/quantas?" (how many?) questions
- Talk about quantities of family members, belongings, etc.

### Vocabulary

- **Numbers 0-20:**
  - 0: zero
  - 1: um/uma (masculine/feminine)
  - 2: dois/duas (masculine/feminine)
  - 3: três
  - 4: quatro
  - 5: cinco
  - 6: seis
  - 7: sete
  - 8: oito
  - 9: nove
  - 10: dez
  - 11: onze
  - 12: doze
  - 13: treze
  - 14: quatorze
  - 15: quinze
  - 16: dezesseis
  - 17: dezessete
  - 18: dezoito
  - 19: dezenove
  - 20: vinte

### Grammar

- Cardinal numbers 0-20 (foundational counting)
- **Gender agreement for 1 and 2 ONLY:**
  - **um** livro (one book - masculine) vs **uma** casa (one house - feminine)
  - **dois** livros (two books - masculine) vs **duas** casas (two houses - feminine)
- **Numbers 3-20:** no gender agreement (três, quatro, cinco... same for all nouns)
- Position: number + noun (um livro, dois carros, três casas)
- Numbers can stand alone: "Quantos? Três." (How many? Three.)

### Exemplar sentences

- Tenho um irmão (I have one brother)
- Tenho duas irmãs (I have two sisters)
- Há cinco pessoas na minha família (There are five people in my family)
- Tenho três amigos brasileiros (I have three Brazilian friends)
- Moro na Rua Paulista número dez (I live on Paulista Street number 10)
- Trabalho oito horas por dia (I work eight hours per day)
- Tenho quinze livros (I have fifteen books)

### Drills & artifacts

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

## Unit 16 — Numbers 21-100 (Extending the System)

*Slug: `a1-num-21-100` · Sequence position: 16.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `numbers`

### Outcomes

- Count from 0 to 100
- Express any quantity up to 100
- Combine tens and units correctly with "e"
- Use correct gender for compound numbers ending in um/dois
- Give street addresses with larger numbers
- Express ages up to 100 (full structure in Unit 17)

### Vocabulary

- **Tens:**
  - 30: trinta
  - 40: quarenta
  - 50: cinquenta
  - 60: sessenta
  - 70: setenta
  - 80: oitenta
  - 90: noventa
  - 100: cem (when alone) / cento (when in 101, 102, etc.)

### Grammar

- **Compound numbers:** tens + **e** + units
  - 21: vinte **e** um
  - 32: trinta **e** dois
  - 45: quarenta **e** cinco
  - 99: noventa **e** nove
- **"E" is REQUIRED** between tens and units (unlike Spanish)
- **Gender agreement still applies to um/dois:**
  - vinte e um anos (21 years - masculine)
  - vinte e uma pessoas (21 people - feminine)
  - trinta e dois livros (32 books - masculine)
  - trinta e duas chaves (32 keys - feminine)
- **Even tens:** 30, 40, 50... stand alone (no "e")

### Exemplar sentences

- Tenho trinta anos (I'm 30 years old)
- Moro no número cinquenta e três (I live at number 53)
- Há quarenta alunos na classe (There are 40 students in the class)
- Trabalho cinquenta horas por semana (I work 50 hours per week)
- Meu pai tem sessenta anos (My father is 60 years old)
- Custa noventa reais (It costs 90 reais - currency in next units)
- O ônibus é o número oitenta e sete (The bus is number 87)

### Drills & artifacts

### Traps

## Unit 17 — Age Expression (Tenho X anos)

*Slug: `a1-ter-idade` · Sequence position: 17.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `irregular-verb-conjugation`

### Outcomes

- Ask and state age correctly using TER
- Express age in present, past, and future
- Ask others' ages politely
- Talk about birthdays (fazer anos)
- Compare ages (older/younger)
- Avoid the critical mistake of using SER for age

### Vocabulary

- **anos** (years)
- **idade** (age)
- **quantos anos** (how many years - how old)
- **aniversário** (birthday)
- **fazer anos** (to have a birthday - literally "to make years")
- **jovem** (young)
- **velho/velha** (old - for people)
- **novo/nova** (young, new)
- **mais velho/mais novo** (older/younger)

### Grammar

- **Age in Portuguese uses TER (to have), NOT SER (to be):**
  - ✅ **Tenho** 25 anos (I am 25 years old - literally "I have 25 years")
  - ❌ **Sou** 25 anos (WRONG - never use ser for age!)
- **Question:** Quantos anos você tem? (How old are you? - literally "How many years do you have?")
- **Pattern:** subject + ter (conjugated) + number + anos
- **Past age:** Tinha X anos (I was X years old)
- **Future age:** Vou ter X anos (I'm going to be X years old)

### Exemplar sentences

- Tenho trinta anos (I'm 30 years old)
- Quantos anos você tem? (How old are you?)
- Meu irmão tem vinte e dois anos (My brother is 22 years old)
- Minha avó tem oitenta anos (My grandmother is 80 years old)
- Tinha quinze anos quando aprendi português (I was 15 years old when I learned Portuguese)
- Vou fazer trinta anos em dezembro (I'm going to turn 30 in December)
- Meu filho tem cinco anos (My son is 5 years old)
- Ele é mais velho que eu (He's older than me)

### Drills & artifacts

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

## Unit 18 — Negation (Não + verb)

*Slug: `a1-negacao` · Sequence position: 18.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `interrogatives`

### Outcomes

- **Create negative sentences with ANY verb** - major milestone!
- Express what they DON'T do, DON'T have, AREN'T, etc.
- Understand that negation is universal across all verbs
- Use "não" as the PRIMARY negation word in Portuguese
- Apply this pattern to all future verbs automatically

### Vocabulary

- **não** (not/no) - **CRITICAL UNIVERSAL CONCEPT**
- Review all verbs learned so far to apply negation

### Grammar

- **NEGATION: "Não" + verb** - UNIVERSAL PATTERN for negative sentences!
  - Pattern: **não + verb = negative**
  - Works with ALL verbs learned so far
  - Simple placement: não comes directly before the verb
- This is a FOUNDATIONAL concept that applies to EVERY verb in Portuguese

### Exemplar sentences

- Não sou americano (I'm not American)
- Não moro no Rio (I don't live in Rio)
- Não trabalho no banco (I don't work at the bank)
- Não falo espanhol (I don't speak Spanish)
- Não ando de carro (I don't go by car)
- Não vou de ônibus (I don't go by bus)
- Não estou cansado (I'm not tired)
- Não estou em casa (I'm not at home)

## Unit 19 — Possession (Tenho - Pets and Vehicles)

*Slug: `a1-ter-posse` · Sequence position: 19.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `irregular-verb-conjugation`

### Outcomes

- Express what they own/possess (pets, vehicles, belongings)
- Use third irregular verb (tenho)
- Distinguish um (masculine) vs uma (feminine)
- **Apply negation to tenho:** "Não tenho" (building on Unit 18)
- Talk about pets and vehicles
- Combine with "e" and "mas" for complex statements
- Connect possessions with possessive adjectives: "Meu cachorro" (from Unit 14)

### Vocabulary

- **tenho** (I have) - **THIRD IRREGULAR VERB** (not *tero)
- Pets:
  - cachorro (dog) - masculine
  - gato (cat) - masculine
  - pássaro (bird) - masculine
- Vehicles:
  - carro (car) - masculine
  - bicicleta (bicycle) - feminine
  - moto / motocicleta (motorcycle) - feminine
- Indefinite articles: **um** (masculine), **uma** (feminine)

### Grammar

- Third irregular verb: **tenho** (I have) - from "ter"
  - NOT regular: would be *tero (wrong)
  - Correct: tenho
- Possession: "Tenho um/uma [thing]"
- **Applying negation from Unit 15:** "Não tenho" (I don't have)
- Indefinite articles for expressing "a" or "one"
- Article omission in negative: "Não tenho carro" (no article after negative)

### Exemplar sentences

- Tenho um cachorro (I have a dog)
- Tenho um gato (I have a cat)
- Tenho um carro (I have a car)
- Tenho uma bicicleta (I have a bicycle)
- Tenho uma moto (I have a motorcycle)
- **Não tenho carro** (I don't have a car)
- **Não tenho cachorro** (I don't have a dog)
- Tenho uma bicicleta, mas não tenho carro (I have a bicycle, but I don't have a car)
- Tenho um gato e um cachorro (I have a cat and a dog)

## Unit 20 — Likes and Preferences (Gosto de)

*Slug: `a1-gosto-de` · Sequence position: 20.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `preposition-collocations`, `regular-ar-conjugation`

### Outcomes

- Express likes and dislikes (with nouns)
- **Apply negation pattern** learned in Unit 14 to preferences
- Add intensity with "muito"
- Combine with "e" and "também" for multiple preferences

### Vocabulary

- gosto (I like) - fifth regular -AR verb
- Common things to like:
  - café (coffee)
  - música (music)
  - futebol (soccer)
  - cinema (movies)
  - português (Portuguese language)
- muito (a lot, very much)
- também (also)

### Grammar

- Fifth regular -AR verb: gosto (I like)
- "Gosto de" construction (requires preposition "de")
- **Applying negation from Unit 14:** "Não gosto de" (I don't like)
- Intensity: "Gosto muito de"

### Exemplar sentences

- Gosto de café
- Gosto muito de música brasileira
- Não gosto de futebol
- Também gosto de cinema
- Gosto de português

## Unit 21 — Liking Activities (Gosto de + Infinitive)

*Slug: `a1-gosto-infinitivo` · Sequence position: 21.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `preposition-collocations`

### Outcomes

- Express what activities they like/dislike
- Use infinitive forms (no need to conjugate!)
- Expand vocabulary massively (can use any verb as infinitive)
- Combine multiple activities with "e"
- Apply negation to activities

### Vocabulary

- Verb infinitives as activities:
  - estudar (to study)
  - viajar (to travel)
  - cozinhar (to cook)
  - cantar (to sing)
  - dançar (to dance)
  - correr (to run)
  - nadar (to swim)
  - ler (to read)
  - escrever (to write)
  - assistir (to watch)
  - ouvir (to listen)
  - dormir (to sleep)
  - acordar (to wake up)

### Grammar

- Expanding "gosto de + infinitive" (introduced in Unit 18)
- Infinitive verbs as objects (no conjugation needed!)
- Students can now use verbs they haven't learned to conjugate yet
- Combining multiple activities: "Gosto de estudar e viajar"
- Negation with activities: "Não gosto de acordar cedo"

### Exemplar sentences

- Gosto de estudar português
- Gosto muito de viajar
- Não gosto de acordar cedo
- Gosto de cozinhar em casa
- Gosto de correr no parque
- Gosto de dançar e cantar
- Não gosto de nadar
- Gosto de ler livros
- Gosto de assistir filmes

## Unit 22 — -ER Verbs (como, bebo, corro)

*Slug: `a1-verbos-er` · Sequence position: 22.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `regular-er-conjugation`

### Outcomes

- Express eating, drinking, and running habits
- Recognize -ER verb pattern (same -o ending as -AR)
- Apply negation to -ER verbs
- Combine food/drink preferences with actions
- See that "-o" is universal for "I"

### Vocabulary

- como (I eat) - first -ER verb
- bebo (I drink) - second -ER verb
- corro (I run) - third -ER verb
- Food vocabulary:
  - arroz e feijão (rice and beans)
  - carne (meat)
  - peixe (fish)
  - salada (salad)
- Drink vocabulary:
  - café (coffee)
  - água (water)
  - suco (juice)
  - cerveja (beer)

### Grammar

- **-ER verb pattern: -ER → -o** (same ending as -AR verbs!)
- comer → como
- beber → bebo
- correr → corro
- **Key revelation: "-o = I" works for BOTH -AR and -ER verbs**
- Negation with -ER verbs: não como, não bebo, não corro

### Exemplar sentences

- Como arroz e feijão todo dia
- Como peixe, mas não como carne
- Bebo café de manhã
- Bebo água, mas não bebo cerveja
- Corro no parque
- Não corro, mas caminho (I don't run, but I walk)

## Unit 23 — Você (You) - Questions and Answers

*Slug: `a1-pron-voce-bp` · Sequence position: 23.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: bp*

**Concepts:** `personal-pronouns`

### Outcomes

- Ask questions using "você"
- Understand the difference between eu (-o) and você (-a/-e) verb forms
- Conduct basic conversations (asking and answering)
- Use question intonation and structure

### Vocabulary

- você (you - formal/neutral singular)
- Question words:
  - onde (where)
  - como (how - not the verb!)
  - o que (what)

### Grammar

- **MAJOR MILESTONE**: First pronoun other than "eu"
- **você** = you (singular, formal/neutral)
- **Question formation**: Você + verb + ?
- **Different verb endings for você**:
  - -AR verbs: você mora, trabalha, anda, fala, gosta (ending in -a)
  - -ER verbs: você come, bebe, corre (ending in -e)
  - **Irregular verbs (with accents!)**: você **é**, **está**, tem
    - Note the accent marks: é (from ser), está (from estar)
    - eu sou → você **é** (not *você sou)
    - eu estou → você **está** (not *você estou)
- Pattern recognition: você uses **third person singular** (not the -o ending)

### Exemplar sentences

- Você é brasileiro? (Are you Brazilian?)
- Você mora em São Paulo? (Do you live in São Paulo?)
- Onde você trabalha? (Where do you work?)
- Você fala português? (Do you speak Portuguese?)
- Você gosta de café? (Do you like coffee?)
- Você tem cachorro? (Do you have a dog?)
- Você está cansado? (Are you tired?)

## Unit 24 — Ele/Ela (He/She) - Talking About Others

*Slug: `a1-pron-ele-ela` · Sequence position: 24.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `personal-pronouns`

### Outcomes

- Talk about people not in the conversation (third person)
- Distinguish between ele (he) and ela (she) based on gender
- Recognize that você/ele/ela all share the same verb forms
- Ask and answer questions about other people

### Vocabulary

- ele (he)
- ela (she)
- o nome (the name)
- Common names and relationships (for practice examples)

### Grammar

- **ele** = he / **ela** = she (third person singular)
- **KEY INSIGHT: ele/ela use the SAME verb forms as você!**
- Gender distinction: ele (masculine) vs ela (feminine)
- Verb forms (identical to você):
  - -AR verbs: ele/ela mora, trabalha, anda, fala, gosta (ending in -a)
  - -ER verbs: ele/ela come, bebe, corre (ending in -e)
  - Irregular: ele/ela **é**, **está**, tem
- Talking about a third person (not present in the conversation)

### Exemplar sentences

- Ele é brasileiro. (He is Brazilian.)
- Ela mora em São Paulo. (She lives in São Paulo.)
- Ele trabalha na universidade. (He works at the university.)
- Ela fala português e inglês. (She speaks Portuguese and English.)
- Ele está cansado. (He is tired.)
- Ela tem um cachorro. (She has a dog.)
- Ele gosta de café. (He likes coffee.)

## Unit 25 — Nós (We) - First Person Plural

*Slug: `a1-pron-nos` · Sequence position: 25.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `personal-pronouns`

### Outcomes

- Talk about themselves + one or more others as a group
- Use first person plural verb forms
- Recognize the -amos/-emos pattern for nós
- Express collective actions and states

### Vocabulary

- nós (we)
- juntos/juntas (together)
- também (also - reinforcing from earlier)

### Grammar

- **nós** = we (first person plural)
- **NEW verb endings for nós**:
  - -AR verbs: nós moramos, trabalhamos, andamos, falamos, gostamos (ending in **-amos**)
  - -ER verbs: nós comemos, bebemos, corremos (ending in **-emos**)
  - Irregular: nós **somos**, **estamos**, **temos**
- Pattern: Add -mos to the infinitive stem (mostly regular!)

### Exemplar sentences

- Nós moramos em São Paulo. (We live in São Paulo.)
- Nós trabalhamos na mesma empresa. (We work at the same company.)
- Nós falamos português. (We speak Portuguese.)
- Nós somos brasileiros. (We are Brazilian.)
- Nós estamos cansados. (We are tired.)
- Nós temos um cachorro. (We have a dog.)
- Nós gostamos de café. (We like coffee.)
- Nós comemos arroz e feijão. (We eat rice and beans.)

## Unit 26 — Vocês (You Plural) - Talking to Groups

*Slug: `a1-pron-voces` · Sequence position: 26.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `personal-pronouns`

### Outcomes

- Address multiple people using "vocês"
- Ask questions to groups of people
- Understand the você → vocês pattern (singular → plural)
- Recognize that vocês verb forms end in -m (third person plural)
- Conduct conversations with groups

### Vocabulary

- vocês (you plural - both formal and informal)
- todos/todas (all, everyone)
- juntos/juntas (together - reinforcing from Unit 23)

### Grammar

- **vocês** = you (plural) - addressing multiple people
- **NEW verb endings for vocês**:
  - -AR verbs: vocês moram, trabalham, andam, falam, gostam (ending in **-am**)
  - -ER verbs: vocês comem, bebem, correm (ending in **-em**)
  - Irregular: vocês **são**, **estão**, **têm** (note: têm has circumflex accent to distinguish from tem)
- **KEY INSIGHT: vocês is the plural of você**
- Question formation with groups: "Vocês moram em São Paulo?"

### Exemplar sentences

- Vocês são brasileiros? (Are you [plural] Brazilian?)
- Vocês moram em São Paulo? (Do you all live in São Paulo?)
- Onde vocês trabalham? (Where do you all work?)
- Vocês falam português? (Do you [plural] speak Portuguese?)
- Vocês gostam de café? (Do you all like coffee?)
- Vocês estão cansados? (Are you all tired?)
- Vocês têm cachorro? (Do you all have a dog?)

## Unit 27 — Eles/Elas (They) - Talking About Groups

*Slug: `a1-pron-eles-elas` · Sequence position: 27.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `personal-pronouns`

### Outcomes

- Talk about groups of people not in the conversation
- Distinguish between eles (masculine/mixed) and elas (all feminine) based on gender
- Recognize that vocês/eles/elas all share the same verb forms
- Ask and answer questions about groups of people
- **Complete understanding of ALL Portuguese subject pronouns**

### Vocabulary

- eles (they - masculine or mixed group)
- elas (they - feminine group only)
- os amigos (the friends - masculine)
- as amigas (the friends - feminine)
- a família (the family)

### Grammar

- **eles** = they (masculine or mixed gender group)
- **elas** = they (all feminine group)
- **KEY INSIGHT: eles/elas use the SAME verb forms as vocês!**
- Gender distinction: eles (masculine/mixed) vs elas (all feminine)
- Talking about groups of people not present in the conversation
- Verb forms (identical to vocês):
  - -AR verbs: eles/elas moram, trabalham, andam, falam, gostam (ending in **-am**)
  - -ER verbs: eles/elas comem, bebem, correm (ending in **-em**)
  - Irregular: eles/elas **são**, **estão**, **têm**

### Exemplar sentences

- Eles são brasileiros. (They [masc/mixed] are Brazilian.)
- Elas moram em São Paulo. (They [fem] live in São Paulo.)
- Eles trabalham na universidade. (They work at the university.)
- Elas falam português e inglês. (They speak Portuguese and English.)
- Eles estão cansados. (They are tired.)
- Elas têm um cachorro. (They have a dog.)
- Eles gostam de café. (They like coffee.)

## Unit 28 — -IR Verbs (abro, parto, assisto)

*Slug: `a1-verbos-ir` · Sequence position: 28.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `regular-ir-conjugation`

### Outcomes

- Conjugate -IR verbs in present tense
- Recognize all three regular verb patterns (-AR, -ER, -IR)
- See that "-o" is truly universal for "I" across all verb types
- Apply negation to -IR verbs
- Connect back to Unit 16: "Gosto de assistir" + "Assisto filmes"

### Vocabulary

- abro (I open) - first -IR verb
- parto (I leave/depart) - second -IR verb
- assisto (I watch) - third -IR verb (infinitive already known from Unit 19)
- Common vocabulary:
  - a porta (the door)
  - a janela (the window)
  - a loja (the store)
  - cedo (early)
  - tarde (late)
  - filmes (movies/films)
  - séries (TV series)

### Grammar

- **-IR verb pattern: -IR → -o** (same ending as -AR and -ER verbs!)
- abrir → abro
- partir → parto
- assistir → assisto
- **REVELATION: "-o = I" works for ALL THREE verb types!**
- Complete regular verb system: -AR, -ER, -IR all use -o
- Negation with -IR verbs: não abro, não parto, não assisto

### Exemplar sentences

- Abro a porta (I open the door)
- Abro a janela de manhã (I open the window in the morning)
- Parto cedo (I leave early)
- Não parto tarde (I don't leave late)
- Assisto filmes brasileiros (I watch Brazilian films)
- Assisto séries em português (I watch series in Portuguese)
- Não assisto televisão (I don't watch television)

## Unit 29 — Future with Vou + Infinitive (Going to...)

*Slug: `a1-vou-infinitivo` · Sequence position: 29.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `future-immediate`

### Outcomes

- Express future plans and intentions
- Talk about what they're going to do (later today, tomorrow, next week, etc.)
- Use the full conjugation of "ir" + infinitive for all pronouns
- Apply time expressions to indicate when
- Distinguish between present actions (Unit 23: "Estudo") and future plans (Unit 24: "Vou estudar")

### Vocabulary

- amanhã (tomorrow)
- depois (later, after)
- hoje à noite (tonight)
- no fim de semana (on the weekend)
- na próxima semana (next week)
- no próximo mês (next month)
- Time expressions already known: agora (now), hoje (today), cedo (early), tarde (late)

### Grammar

- **Future construction: vou + infinitive** = "going to" (immediate/planned future)
- This combines two concepts students already know:
  - **vou** from Unit 8 (irregular verb "ir")
  - **infinitives** from Unit 19 (gosto de + infinitive)
- Pattern: subject + vou/vai/vamos/vão + infinitive verb
- Expressing future plans and intentions
- Time expressions to indicate when actions will happen

### Exemplar sentences

- Vou estudar português amanhã (I'm going to study Portuguese tomorrow)
- Vou trabalhar hoje à noite (I'm going to work tonight)
- Vou viajar no fim de semana (I'm going to travel on the weekend)
- Vou comer no restaurante depois (I'm going to eat at the restaurant later)
- Não vou assistir filmes hoje (I'm not going to watch movies today)
- Vou dormir cedo (I'm going to sleep early)

## Unit 30 — Progressive Tenses - Estar + Gerund (Estou Fazendo)

*Slug: `a2-estar-gerundio-bp` · Sequence position: 30.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: bp*

**Concepts:** `present-continuous`

### Outcomes

- Form the gerund for all verb types (-ando, -endo, -indo)
- Use progressive tense for actions in progress
- Ask "O que você está fazendo?" (What are you doing?)
- Describe ongoing actions
- Distinguish simple present from progressive

### Vocabulary

- **Progressive expressions:**
  - agora (now)
  - neste momento (at this moment)
  - agora mesmo (right now)
  - atualmente (currently)
  - no momento (at the moment)

### Grammar

- **Progressive tense: ESTAR + GERUND:**
  - Expresses actions in progress (ongoing right now)
  - "I am doing", "You are working", "We are eating"
  - Very common in Brazilian Portuguese

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu estou trabalhando. (I am working.)
- O que você está fazendo? (What are you doing?)
- Ela está cozinhando. (She is cooking.)
- Nós estamos estudando português. (We are studying Portuguese.)
- Eles estão assistindo TV. (They are watching TV.)
- Estou falando no telefone. (I'm talking on the phone.)
- Ele está dormindo agora. (He is sleeping now.)

## Unit 31 — Plural Possessives: Meus/Minhas (My - Plural)

*Slug: `a1-poss-meus` · Sequence position: 31.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `possessives`

### Outcomes

- **Complete the "my" possessive system:** meu/minha/meus/minhas
- Talk about family members in plural (meus irmãos, minhas irmãs, meus pais)
- Express possession of multiple items (meus livros, minhas chaves)
- Understand full gender AND number agreement for possessives
- Apply all four forms correctly based on the noun

### Vocabulary

- **meus/minhas** (my - masculine/feminine PLURAL) - extending Unit 14's meu/minha
- Plural family/friends:
  - irmãos/irmãs (brothers/sisters)
  - filhos/filhas (sons/daughters)
  - amigos/amigas (friends)
  - pais (parents - always masculine plural)
- Personal items (plural):
  - livros (books) - masculine plural
  - chaves (keys) - feminine plural
  - documentos (documents) - masculine plural
  - sapatos (shoes) - masculine plural

### Grammar

- **Extending Unit 14:** Adding PLURAL forms meus/minhas to complete "my" system
- **Four forms total for "my":**
  - Masculine singular: **meu** pai (from Unit 14)
  - Feminine singular: **minha** mãe (from Unit 14)
  - Masculine plural: **meus** irmãos (NEW!)
  - Feminine plural: **minhas** irmãs (NEW!)
- **Agreement rule (review from Unit 14):** Possessive agrees with the THING POSSESSED
- Position: possessive + noun (no article needed)

### Exemplar sentences

- Review: Meu pai é brasileiro (My father is Brazilian - from Unit 14)
- Review: Minha mãe trabalha no hospital (My mother works at the hospital - from Unit 14)
- **NEW:** Meus irmãos moram em São Paulo (My brothers live in São Paulo)
- **NEW:** Minhas irmãs falam inglês (My sisters speak English)
- **NEW:** Meus pais moram no Rio (My parents live in Rio)
- **NEW:** Meus amigos são brasileiros (My friends are Brazilian)
- **NEW:** Minhas chaves estão aqui (My keys are here)
- **NEW:** Meus livros são novos (My books are new)

## Unit 32 — Your/His/Her Possessives: Seu/Sua + Dele/Dela Construction

*Slug: `a1-poss-seu-dele` · Sequence position: 32.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `possessives`, `pronoun-contractions`

### Outcomes

- Use seu/sua/seus/suas possessives (but understand the ambiguity)
- **Use dele/dela/deles/delas construction for clarity** (PREFERRED in BP!)
- Distinguish "your" from "his/her" using context or dele/dela
- Understand why Brazilians prefer the dele/dela construction
- Express third-person possession clearly

### Vocabulary

- **seu/sua/seus/suas** (your/his/her - masculine/feminine, singular/plural) - **AMBIGUOUS!**
- **dele** (his - literally "of-him")
- **dela** (her - literally "of-her")
- **deles** (their - masculine/mixed group)
- **delas** (their - feminine group only)

### Grammar

- **Seu/sua/seus/suas possessives** - can mean YOUR, HIS, HER, or THEIR!
  - Four forms: seu (masc sing), sua (fem sing), seus (masc pl), suas (fem pl)
  - **CRITICAL PROBLEM:** Extremely ambiguous in Brazilian Portuguese
- **SOLUTION: Dele/Dela construction** (PREFERRED in colloquial BP!)
  - Structure: **article + noun + dele/dela/deles/delas**
  - o irmão dele (his brother), a casa dela (her house)
  - **REQUIRES article:** Cannot say just "irmão dele"
- Position:
  - Seu/sua: possessive + noun (like meu/minha)
  - Dele/dela: article + noun + dele/dela

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link drills, worksheets, lessons in Phase 3 -->

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

## Unit 33 — Our Possessives: Nosso/Nossa/Nossos/Nossas

*Slug: `a1-poss-nosso` · Sequence position: 33.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `possessives`

### Outcomes

- Express "our" possession with full gender/number agreement
- Use all four forms correctly (nosso/nossa/nossos/nossas)
- **Complete the possessive system:** my, your/his/her, our
- Talk about shared family, belongings, and experiences
- Combine with nós (we) for complete first-person plural expression

### Vocabulary

- **nosso/nossa/nossos/nossas** (our - masculine/feminine, singular/plural)
- Words commonly used with "our":
  - família (family) - feminine
  - casa (house) - feminine
  - país (country) - masculine
  - cidade (city) - feminine
  - trabalho (job/work) - masculine
  - projeto (project) - masculine

### Grammar

- **"Our" possessive adjectives: nosso/nossa/nossos/nossas**
  - Four forms based on gender/number of noun:
    - **nosso** = our (masculine singular): nosso pai
    - **nossa** = our (feminine singular): nossa mãe
    - **nossos** = our (masculine plural): nossos irmãos
    - **nossas** = our (feminine plural): nossas irmãs
- **Agreement rule (same as all possessives):** agrees with the THING POSSESSED
- Position: possessive + noun (no article needed)
- **No ambiguity!** - nosso/nossa ALWAYS means "our" (unlike seu/sua)

### Exemplar sentences

- Nossa casa é pequena (Our house is small)
- Nosso pai trabalha no banco (Our father works at the bank)
- Nossa mãe é professora (Our mother is a teacher)
- Nossos pais moram no Rio (Our parents live in Rio)
- Nossos irmãos falam inglês (Our brothers speak English)
- Nossas irmãs moram aqui (Our sisters live here)
- Nossos amigos são legais (Our friends are cool)
- Nossa cidade é bonita (Our city is beautiful)

## Unit 34 — Past Tense - Regular -AR Verbs (Preterite)

*Slug: `a2-pret-regular-ar` · Sequence position: 34.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `preterite-regular`

### Outcomes

- Talk about completed past actions with regular -AR verbs
- Use all -AR verbs learned so far in past tense
- Distinguish present from past using time expressions
- Notice that nós form is SAME in present and past (context determines meaning)
- Ask questions about past events

### Vocabulary

- **ontem** (yesterday)
- **na semana passada** (last week)
- **no mês passado** (last month)
- **no ano passado** (last year)
- **anteontem** (the day before yesterday)
- **há [time]** (ago) - há dois dias (two days ago)

### Grammar

- **Preterite tense for regular -AR verbs** (simple past - completed actions)
- Past tense endings for -AR verbs:
  - eu: -**ei** (morei, trabalhei, estudei)
  - você/ele/ela: -**ou** (morou, trabalhou, estudou)
  - nós: -**amos** (moramos, trabalhamos, estudamos) - **SAME as present!**
  - vocês/eles/elas: -**aram** (moraram, trabalharam, estudaram)
- Used for actions that happened at a specific time in the past and are complete
- Time expressions that signal past tense

### Exemplar sentences

- Morei no Brasil (I lived in Brazil)
- Trabalhei ontem (I worked yesterday)
- Estudei português na semana passada (I studied Portuguese last week)
- Ele morou em São Paulo (He lived in São Paulo)
- Nós trabalhamos ontem (We worked yesterday - same as present!)
- Eles falaram português (They spoke Portuguese)
- Você gostou do filme? (Did you like the movie?)
- Não gostei (I didn't like it)

## Unit 35 — Past Tense - Regular -ER/-IR Verbs (Preterite)

*Slug: `a2-pret-regular-er-ir` · Sequence position: 35.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `preterite-regular`

### Outcomes

- Talk about completed past actions with regular -ER and -IR verbs
- Use all -ER verbs from Unit 20 in past tense (comer, beber, correr)
- Use all -IR verbs from Unit 26 in past tense (abrir, partir, assistir)
- Recognize that -ER and -IR share past tense endings
- Notice that nós form is SAME as present (like -AR verbs)
- Combine with -AR past tense from Unit 29

### Vocabulary

- Time expressions (review from Unit 29): ontem, na semana passada, no mês passado
- Additional: de manhã (in the morning), à tarde (in the afternoon), à noite (at night)
- já (already), ainda não (not yet)

### Grammar

- **Preterite tense for regular -ER and -IR verbs**
- **KEY INSIGHT: -ER and -IR verbs share the SAME past tense endings!**
- Past tense endings for -ER/-IR verbs:
  - eu: -**i** (comi, bebi, corri, abri, parti, assisti)
  - você/ele/ela: -**eu/-iu** (comeu, bebeu, correu, abriu, partiu, assistiu)
  - nós: -**emos/-imos** (comemos/abrimos - same as present!)
  - vocês/eles/elas: -**eram/-iram** (comeram/abriram)
- Used for completed actions in the past (same as -AR verbs in Unit 29)

### Exemplar sentences

- Comi arroz e feijão ontem (I ate rice and beans yesterday)
- Bebi café de manhã (I drank coffee in the morning)
- Corri no parque na semana passada (I ran in the park last week)
- Abri a porta (I opened the door)
- Ele partiu cedo (He left early)
- Assistimos um filme (We watched a movie)
- Vocês comeram? (Did you all eat?)
- Não bebi cerveja (I didn't drink beer)

## Unit 36 — Past Tense - Essential Irregular Verbs (ser, ir, ter, estar)

*Slug: `a2-pret-essenciais` · Sequence position: 36.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `preterite-irregular`

### Outcomes

- Talk about past identity/professions (fui)
- Talk about where they went (fui)
- Distinguish ser/ir by context
- Talk about past possession (tive)
- Talk about past location/state (estive)
- Tell complete stories combining regular and irregular verbs

### Vocabulary

- Time expressions (review): ontem, na semana passada, no ano passado
- Additional time expressions:
  - no passado (in the past)
  - quando (when)
  - antes (before)

### Grammar

- **Preterite tense for the most essential irregular verbs**
- **AMAZING FACT: ser (to be) and ir (to go) share identical past tense forms!**
- Four essential irregulars:
  - **ser/ir**: fui, foi, fomos, foram
  - **ter**: tive, teve, tivemos, tiveram
  - **estar**: estive, esteve, estivemos, estiveram
- Context determines meaning for ser vs ir (both use fui, foi, etc.)
- These verbs don't follow regular patterns - must be memorized

### Exemplar sentences

- Fui professor no Brasil (I was a teacher in Brazil) - ser
- Fui ao cinema ontem (I went to the movies yesterday) - ir
- Ela foi brasileira (She was Brazilian) - doesn't work! Identity doesn't change
- Ele foi ao banco (He went to the bank) - ir
- Fomos ao restaurante (We went to the restaurant) - ir
- Tive um cachorro (I had a dog)
- Não tive tempo (I didn't have time)
- Estive em São Paulo (I was in São Paulo)
- Estivemos cansados (We were tired)

## Unit 37 — Past Tense - Common Irregular Verbs (fazer, ver, dar)

*Slug: `a2-pret-fazer-ver-dar` · Sequence position: 37.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `preterite-irregular`

### Outcomes

- Talk about what they did/made (fiz)
- Talk about what they saw/watched (vi)
- Talk about what they gave (dei)
- Answer "O que você fez?" (What did you do?) - one of the most common questions
- Combine with Units 26-28 for rich storytelling

### Vocabulary

- Vocabulary that pairs with these verbs:
  - perguntas (questions)
  - trabalho (work/task)
  - exercícios (exercises)
  - presente (gift/present)
  - dinheiro (money)
  - ajuda (help)

### Grammar

- **Three more essential irregular verbs in preterite**
- **fazer (to make/do)**: fiz, fez, fizemos, fizeram
- **ver (to see/watch)**: vi, viu, vimos, viram
- **dar (to give)**: dei, deu, demos, deram
- These verbs are extremely common in past tense conversations
- Each has its own irregular pattern - must be memorized

### Exemplar sentences

- Fiz exercícios de manhã (I did exercises in the morning)
- Fiz o trabalho ontem (I did the work yesterday)
- Fiz uma pergunta (I asked a question)
- Vi meus amigos (I saw my friends)
- Vi um filme ontem (I saw/watched a movie yesterday)
- Não vi nada (I didn't see anything)
- Dei um presente para ela (I gave her a gift)
- Dei dinheiro (I gave money)
- Ele me deu ajuda (He gave me help)

## Unit 38 — Question Words (Interrogatives)

*Slug: `a1-question-words` · Sequence position: 38.0 · CEFR: A1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `question-words`

### Outcomes

- Ask questions about any topic covered so far
- Use interrogatives with present, future, and past tenses
- Form information questions (not just yes/no questions)
- Understand that many question words they've seen informally are now systematic
- Conduct two-way conversations (not just answer, but also ask)

### Vocabulary

- **Question words (interrogatives):**
  - **o que / que** (what)
  - **quem** (who)
  - **onde** (where)
  - **quando** (when)
  - **como** (how)
  - **por que** (why)
  - **qual / quais** (which / which ones)
  - **quanto/a/os/as** (how much / how many)

### Grammar

- **Systematic introduction to interrogatives**
- Question formation with all tenses (present, future, past)
- Word order: interrogative + verb + subject (or just interrogative + verb with pro-drop)
- Using question words students have encountered informally since early units
- Questions can end with question mark but intonation is key

### Exemplar sentences

- O que você faz? (What do you do?)
- Quem é ela? (Who is she?)
- Onde você mora? (Where do you live?)
- Quando você vai viajar? (When are you going to travel?)
- Como você está? (How are you?)
- Por que você gosta de português? (Why do you like Portuguese?)
- Qual é seu nome? (What is your name? / literally: Which is your name?)
- Quanto custa? (How much does it cost?)
- Quantos irmãos você tem? (How many siblings do you have?)

## Unit 39 — Reflexive Verbs (me chamo, me levanto, me sinto)

*Slug: `a2-reflexivos-bp` · Sequence position: 39.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: bp*

**Concepts:** `reflexive-verbs`

### Outcomes

- Introduce themselves formally: "Me chamo [name]"
- Talk about daily routine (getting up, sitting down, going to bed)
- Express how they feel (me sinto bem/mal/cansado/feliz)
- Use reflexive verbs in all three tenses (present, future, past)
- Understand difference between reflexive and non-reflexive verbs
- Ask someone's name formally: "Como você se chama?"

### Vocabulary

- **Reflexive pronouns:**
  - **me** (myself)
  - **se** (yourself/himself/herself/themselves)
  - **nos** (ourselves)
- **Common reflexive verbs:**
  - chamar-se (to call oneself / to be named)
  - levantar-se (to get up)
  - sentar-se (to sit down)
  - sentir-se (to feel)
  - vestir-se (to get dressed)
  - deitar-se (to lie down / go to bed)
  - lembrar-se (to remember)
  - esquecer-se (to forget)
- **Daily routine vocabulary:**
  - de manhã (in the morning)
  - à tarde (in the afternoon)
  - à noite (at night)
  - cedo (early)
  - tarde (late)
  - bem (well)
  - mal (badly)
  - cansado/a (tired)
  - feliz (happy)

### Grammar

- **Reflexive verbs: action reflects back on the subject**
- **Reflexive pronouns in Brazilian Portuguese go BEFORE the conjugated verb**
- Pattern: subject + reflexive pronoun + conjugated verb
  - Eu **me** chamo Maria (I call myself Maria = My name is Maria)
  - Eu **me** levanto cedo (I get up early)
  - Eu **me** sinto bem (I feel well)
- Reflexive pronouns for each subject:
  - eu → **me** (myself)
  - você/ele/ela → **se** (yourself/himself/herself)
  - nós → **nos** (ourselves)
  - vocês/eles/elas → **se** (yourselves/themselves)
- Common use: **"Como você se chama?"** = "What's your name?" (literally: How do you call yourself?)
- Answer: **"Me chamo [name]"** or informal **"Meu nome é [name]"** (Unit 13)

### Exemplar sentences

- Me chamo Maria (My name is Maria)
- Me levanto às 7h (I get up at 7am)
- Me sinto bem (I feel well)
- Me sinto cansado (I feel tired)
- Não me sinto bem (I don't feel well)
- Me visto rápido de manhã (I get dressed quickly in the morning)
- Me sento aqui (I sit here)
- Me deito tarde (I go to bed late)
- Você se lembra? (Do you remember?)
- Não me lembro (I don't remember)
- Como você se chama? (What's your name?)

## Unit 40 — Direct Object Pronouns (me, te, o/a, nos, os/as)

*Slug: `a2-dop-bp` · Sequence position: 40.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: bp*

**Concepts:** `object-pronouns`

### Outcomes

- Replace direct objects with pronouns to sound more natural
- Avoid repetition: "Vejo João. João é meu amigo." → "Vejo João. O conheço bem."
- Use object pronouns with all three tenses
- Distinguish between reflexive pronouns (Unit 35) and direct object pronouns (Unit 36)
- Understand that me/nos can be reflexive OR object pronouns (context determines)
- Form more natural, fluent Portuguese sentences

### Vocabulary

- **Direct object pronouns:**
  - **me** (me - as object)
  - **te** (you - as object, informal)
  - **o / a** (him/it / her/it - masculine/feminine)
  - **nos** (us - as object)
  - **os / as** (them - masculine/feminine plural)
- **New verbs commonly used with direct objects:**
  - ver (to see - already learned in Unit 33)
  - conhecer (to know/meet - people/places)
  - amar (to love)
  - ajudar (to help)
  - esperar (to wait for / to hope)
  - ouvir (to hear/listen)
  - entender (to understand)
  - encontrar (to find / to meet)

### Grammar

- **Direct object pronouns: replace the direct object (the thing/person receiving the action)**
- **In Brazilian Portuguese, pronouns typically go BEFORE the verb (like reflexive pronouns)**
- Pattern: subject + object pronoun + verb
  - Ele **me** vê (He sees me)
  - Eu **te** amo (I love you)
  - Eu **o** conheço (I know him)
  - Ela **nos** ajuda (She helps us)
- Direct object answers "what?" or "whom?"
  - Vejo João → Vejo quem? João → **O** vejo (I see him)
  - Amo Maria → Amo quem? Maria → **A** amo (I love her)
  - Conhecemos as pessoas → **As** conhecemos (We know them)
- Gender and number agreement with o/a/os/as
  - **o** = him/it (masculine singular)
  - **a** = her/it (feminine singular)
  - **os** = them (masculine plural or mixed)
  - **as** = them (feminine plural)

### Exemplar sentences

- Ele me vê todos os dias (He sees me every day)
- Te amo (I love you)
- O conheço bem (I know him well)
- A vejo na escola (I see her at school)
- Ela nos ajuda (She helps us)
- Vocês os conhecem? (Do you all know them?)
- Não as vejo mais (I don't see them anymore - feminine)
- Me entendem? (Do you understand me?)
- Te espero aqui (I wait for you here / I'll wait for you here)

## Unit 41 — Past Tense - More Common Irregular Verbs (poder, querer, saber)

*Slug: `a2-pret-poder-querer-saber` · Sequence position: 41.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `preterite-irregular`

### Outcomes

- Talk about what they could or couldn't do (pude/não pude)
- Express past desires and intentions (quis/não quis)
- Talk about finding out information (soube)
- Understand the nuanced meaning shifts in the past tense
- Combine with other past tense verbs for richer storytelling

### Vocabulary

- **Three more essential irregular verbs in preterite:**
  - poder (to be able to / can)
  - querer (to want)
  - saber (to know - facts/information)
- **Additional vocabulary:**
  - nada (nothing)
  - tudo (everything)
  - a verdade (the truth)
  - a resposta (the answer)
  - a notícia (the news)
  - comprar (to buy - regular verb for examples)
  - vir (to come - for context, but conjugation comes later)

### Grammar

- **Preterite tense for poder, querer, and saber**
- These three verbs often change meaning slightly in the past:
  - **poder** (present: can/am able to) → (past: could/was able to/managed to)
  - **querer** (present: want) → (past: wanted/tried to)
  - **saber** (present: know) → (past: found out/learned)
- Conjugation patterns:
  - **poder**: pude, pôde, pudemos, puderam
  - **querer**: quis, quis, quisemos, quiseram
  - **saber**: soube, soube, soubemos, souberam
- All three are highly irregular with unique stems

### Exemplar sentences

- Pude ir (I was able to go / I managed to go)
- Não pude trabalhar ontem (I couldn't work yesterday)
- Quis viajar, mas não pude (I wanted to travel, but couldn't)
- Ele não quis comer (He didn't want to eat / He refused to eat)
- Soube a notícia hoje (I found out the news today)
- Quando você soube? (When did you find out?)
- Não soube a resposta (I didn't know the answer)
- Pudemos ver tudo (We were able to see everything)

## Unit 42 — Para vs Por (Two meanings of for)

*Slug: `a2-por-vs-para` · Sequence position: 42.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `por-vs-para`

### Outcomes

- Distinguish between the two main translations of "for" in Portuguese
- Express purpose with para + infinitive
- Express duration with por + time expression
- Talk about recipients with para
- Explain reasons with por
- Use fixed expressions like "por favor," "por exemplo," "por isso"
- Understand when to use each preposition correctly

### Vocabulary

- **Prepositions:**
  - **para** (for/to - purpose, destination, recipient, deadline)
  - **por** (for/by/through - reason, duration, agent, means)
- **Vocabulary for common uses:**
  - presente (gift/present)
  - razão (reason)
  - causa (cause)
  - através de (through - alternative to por)
  - durante (during - alternative to por)
  - motivo (reason/motive)
- **Time expressions with por:**
  - por uma hora (for an hour)
  - por dois dias (for two days)
  - por muito tempo (for a long time)
  - por enquanto (for now)
- **Common expressions:**
  - por favor (please - literally: for favor)
  - por exemplo (for example)
  - por que (why - literally: for what)
  - por isso (therefore/that's why - literally: for this)

### Grammar

- **PARA - purpose, destination, recipient, deadline:**
  1. **Purpose/goal** (in order to): Para estudar (in order to study)
  2. **Destination** (to/toward): Vou para casa (I go home/toward home)
  3. **Recipient** (for someone): É para você (It's for you)
  4. **Deadline** (by a time): Para amanhã (by tomorrow)
  5. **Opinion/perspective**: Para mim (for me/in my opinion)

- **POR - reason, duration, agent, means, location:**
  1. **Reason/cause** (because of): Por amor (for love/because of love)
  2. **Duration** (for a length of time): Por duas horas (for two hours)
  3. **Agent** (by someone - passive voice): Escrito por João (written by João)
  4. **Means/method** (by/through): Por email (by email)
  5. **Movement through**: Por aqui (through here)
  6. **Exchange**: Paguei 50 reais por isso (I paid 50 reais for this)

- **Key distinction:**
  - **PARA** = destination, goal, purpose, future-oriented
  - **POR** = reason, cause, duration, past-oriented

### Exemplar sentences

- Estudo para aprender português (I study to learn Portuguese) - purpose
- Isso é para você (This is for you) - recipient
- Vou para o Brasil (I'm going to Brazil) - destination
- Este projeto é para amanhã (This project is for tomorrow) - deadline (with SER)
- Preciso terminar até amanhã (I need to finish by tomorrow) - deadline (with ATÉ, not PARA)
- Trabalho por dinheiro (I work for money) - reason
- Fiz isso por amor (I did this for love) - reason
- Morei lá por três anos (I lived there for three years) - duration
- Mandei por email (I sent by email) - means
- Obrigado por tudo (Thank you for everything) - reason
- Por favor (Please) - fixed expression

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link drills, worksheets, lessons in Phase 3 -->

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

## Unit 43 — Past Tense - Additional Irregular Verbs (trazer, dizer, vir, pôr)

*Slug: `a2-pret-trazer-dizer-vir-por` · Sequence position: 43.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `preterite-irregular`

### Outcomes

- Talk about bringing things in the past (trouxe)
- Report what people said (disse)
- Talk about coming/arrival in the past (vim/veio)
- Talk about placing/putting things (pus/pôs)
- Combine with all other past tense verbs for richer storytelling
- Use 14 irregular past tense verbs total (Units 28, 29, 33, 35)

### Vocabulary

- **Four more essential irregular verbs in preterite:**
  - trazer (to bring)
  - dizer (to say/tell)
  - vir (to come)
  - pôr (to put/place)
- **Additional vocabulary:**
  - presente (gift/present)
  - mensagem (message)
  - notícia (news)
  - verdade (truth)
  - mentira (lie)
  - aqui (here)
  - lá (there)
  - mesa (table)
  - lugar (place)

### Grammar

- **Preterite tense for trazer, dizer, vir, and pôr**
- All four verbs are highly irregular with unique stems
- Conjugation patterns:
  - **trazer**: trouxe, trouxe, trouxemos, trouxeram
  - **dizer**: disse, disse, dissemos, disseram
  - **vir**: vim, veio, viemos, vieram
  - **pôr**: pus, pôs, pusemos, puseram

### Exemplar sentences

- Trouxe um presente para você (I brought a gift for you)
- Ela trouxe a comida (She brought the food)
- Ele disse que vai viajar (He said that he's going to travel)
- Dissemos a verdade (We told the truth)
- Vim de ônibus (I came by bus)
- Ele veio aqui ontem (He came here yesterday)
- Pus o livro na mesa (I put the book on the table)
- Ela pôs as chaves lá (She put the keys there)

## Unit 44 — Indirect Object Pronouns (lhe, lhes) + Review of me/te/nos

*Slug: `a2-iop-bp` · Sequence position: 44.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: bp*

**Concepts:** `object-pronouns`

### Outcomes

- Express to/for whom actions are directed
- Use verbs like dar, dizer, mostrar with indirect objects
- Distinguish between direct objects (Unit 36) and indirect objects (Unit 40)
- Understand that me/te/nos can be direct OR indirect (context determines)
- Form more sophisticated sentences with both direct and indirect objects

### Vocabulary

- **Indirect object pronouns:**
  - **lhe** (to/for him, to/for her, to/for you - formal)
  - **lhes** (to/for them, to/for you plural)
  - Review: **me** (to/for me), **te** (to/for you - informal), **nos** (to/for us)
- **Verbs commonly used with indirect objects:**
  - dar (to give - Unit 33)
  - dizer (to say/tell - Unit 39)
  - falar (to speak - Unit 1)
  - perguntar (to ask)
  - mostrar (to show)
  - contar (to tell/count)
  - explicar (to explain)
  - enviar (to send)
  - emprestar (to lend)
  - pedir (to ask for/request)
- **Additional vocabulary:**
  - ajuda (help)
  - favor (favor)
  - dinheiro (money)
  - livro (book)
  - telefone (phone/phone number)
  - endereço (address)
  - resposta (answer)

### Grammar

- **Indirect object pronouns: replace "to/for someone" (recipient of action)**
- **Key distinction from direct objects (Unit 36):**
  - **Direct object:** WHO/WHAT receives the action directly (no preposition)
  - **Indirect object:** TO/FOR WHOM the action is done (with preposition a/para)
- **In Brazilian Portuguese, pronouns go BEFORE the verb**
- Pattern: subject + indirect pronoun + verb + (direct object)
  - Eu **lhe** dei o livro (I gave the book to him/her)
  - Ele **me** disse a verdade (He told the truth to me = He told me the truth)
  - Ela **nos** mostrou as fotos (She showed the photos to us)
- Indirect object answers "to whom?" or "for whom?"
  - Dei o livro a Maria → Dei a quem? A Maria → **Lhe** dei o livro (I gave the book to her)
  - Falei com João → Falei com quem? Com João → **Lhe** falei (I spoke to him)

### Exemplar sentences

- Lhe dei o livro (I gave the book to him/her)
- Ele me disse a verdade (He told me the truth)
- Ela nos mostrou o caminho (She showed us the way)
- Vou lhe contar uma história (I'm going to tell a story to you/him/her)
- Eles me perguntaram tudo (They asked me everything)
- Lhe pedi ajuda (I asked him/her for help)
- Me empresta dinheiro? (Can you lend me money? / Will you lend money to me?)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link drills, worksheets, lessons in Phase 3 -->

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

## Unit 45 — Imperfect Tense - Regular Verbs (Ongoing/Habitual Past)

*Slug: `a2-imp-regular` · Sequence position: 45.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `preterite-imperfect`

### Outcomes

- Describe ongoing actions in the past (was doing)
- Talk about habitual actions in the past (used to do)
- Describe what things were like in the past
- Tell richer stories by combining preterite and imperfect
- Talk about childhood and past routines

### Vocabulary

- **Time expressions for habitual/repeated actions:**
  - sempre (always)
  - todos os dias (every day)
  - todas as semanas (every week)
  - frequentemente (frequently)
  - normalmente (normally)
  - geralmente (generally)
  - às vezes (sometimes)
  - nunca (never)
  - quando era criança (when I was a child)
  - naquela época (at that time/back then)
  - antes (before)
- **Additional vocabulary:**
  - criança (child)
  - jovem (young)
  - pequeno/a (small/little)

### Grammar

- **Imperfect tense (pretérito imperfeito): for ongoing, habitual, or descriptive past actions**
- **Key distinction from preterite (Units 26-29, 33, 35):**
  - **Preterite:** completed actions (I ate, I went, I did)
  - **Imperfect:** ongoing/habitual actions (I was eating, I used to go, I would do)
- **Regular conjugation patterns for imperfect:**
  - **-AR verbs:** -ava, -ava, -ávamos, -avam
  - **-ER verbs:** -ia, -ia, -íamos, -iam
  - **-IR verbs:** -ia, -ia, -íamos, -iam
- **Good news: -ER and -IR verbs share the SAME imperfect endings!**
- **Better news: Imperfect is VERY regular - almost no irregular verbs!**

### Exemplar sentences

- Morava em São Paulo (I used to live in São Paulo)
- Trabalhava no banco (I used to work at the bank / I was working at the bank)
- Comia muito (I used to eat a lot)
- Estudava português todos os dias (I used to study Portuguese every day)
- Quando era criança, brincava muito (When I was a child, I used to play a lot)
- Sempre gostava de viajar (I always used to like traveling)
- Naquela época, corríamos no parque (At that time, we used to run in the park)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link drills, worksheets, lessons in Phase 3 -->

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

## Unit 46 — Imperfect Tense - Irregular Verbs (ser, ter, vir)

*Slug: `a2-imp-irregular` · Sequence position: 46.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `preterite-imperfect`

### Outcomes

- Use all three irregular imperfect verbs (ser, ter, vir)
- Describe what people/things were like in the past (era)
- Talk about age in the past (tinha X anos)
- Talk about possession in the past (tinha um carro)
- Talk about habitual coming in the past (vinha)
- Combine with regular imperfect verbs for complete past descriptions
- Tell sophisticated stories with complete imperfect tense knowledge

### Vocabulary

- **Time/age expressions with imperfect:**
  - anos (years - for age)
  - idade (age)
  - jovem (young)
  - velho/a (old)
- **Additional descriptive vocabulary:**
  - pequeno/a (small/little)
  - grande (big/large)
  - rico/a (rich)
  - pobre (poor)
  - feliz (happy)
  - triste (sad)
  - forte (strong)
  - fraco/a (weak)

### Grammar

- **Only THREE irregular verbs in imperfect: ser, ter, vir**
- **ser (to be) - imperfect:**
  - eu **era**, você/ele/ela **era**, nós **éramos**, vocês/eles/elas **eram**
- **ter (to have) - imperfect:**
  - eu **tinha**, você/ele/ela **tinha**, nós **tínhamos**, vocês/eles/elas **tinham**
- **vir (to come) - imperfect:**
  - eu **vinha**, você/ele/ela **vinha**, nós **vínhamos**, vocês/eles/elas **vinham**
- **These are the ONLY irregular verbs in imperfect tense!**

### Exemplar sentences

- Era alto (I/he was tall)
- Eu era jovem (I was young)
- Quando era criança, era pequeno (When I was a child, I was small)
- A casa era grande (The house was big)
- Eles eram ricos (They were rich)
- Tinha 20 anos (I was 20 years old)
- Não tinha dinheiro (I didn't have money)
- Tínhamos uma casa (We had a house)
- Vinha aqui todos os dias (I used to come here every day)
- Eles vinham sempre (They always used to come)
- Vínhamos de ônibus (We used to come by bus)

### Drills & artifacts

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

- Preterite: completed, punctual actions
- Imperfect: ongoing, habitual, descriptive
- Using both in narrative (background vs foreground)
