## Unit 82 — School and Education (Escola e Educação)

*Slug: `a2-escola` · Sequence position: 75.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `common-expressions`

### Outcomes

- Name 12+ school subjects
- Name 10+ classroom items
- Talk about what they study
- Express preferences about subjects
- Describe school and classroom

### Vocabulary

- **School subjects:**
  - a matemática (mathematics)
  - o português (Portuguese)
  - a história (history)
  - a geografia (geography)
  - as ciências (science)
  - a física (physics)
  - a química (chemistry)
  - a biologia (biology)
  - a literatura (literature)
  - o inglês (English)
  - a educação física (physical education)
  - a arte (art)

- **Classroom items:**
  - o quadro (board/blackboard)
  - o giz (chalk)
  - o caderno (notebook)
  - o livro (book)
  - a caneta (pen)
  - o lápis (pencil)
  - a borracha (eraser)
  - a mochila (backpack)
  - a mesa (desk/table)
  - a cadeira (chair)

- **School vocabulary:**
  - a escola (school)
  - a universidade (university)
  - a aula (class/lesson)
  - o professor / a professora (teacher)
  - o aluno / a aluna (student)
  - a prova (test/exam)
  - o dever de casa (homework)

### Grammar

- **ESTUDAR (to study) + subject:**
  - Eu estudo **matemática**. (I study math.)
  - Ela estuda **português**. (She studies Portuguese.)
  - Use subject WITHOUT article after estudar

- **GOSTAR DE + subject:**
  - Eu gosto **de** matemática. (I like math.)
  - Ele gosta **de** história. (He likes history.)
  - Note: uses "de" as usual with gostar

- **TER aula (to have class):**
  - Eu tenho aula de português. (I have Portuguese class.)
  - Tenho aula às oito horas. (I have class at 8 o'clock.)

- **SER + adjective for subjects:**
  - Matemática é difícil. (Math is difficult.)
  - Português é fácil. (Portuguese is easy.)
  - Subject is singular even if "ciências" is plural

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu estudo matemática. (I study math.)
- Eu gosto de história. (I like history.)
- Tenho aula de português às nove. (I have Portuguese class at 9.)
- Matemática é difícil. (Math is difficult.)
- Eu preciso de um caderno. (I need a notebook.)
- O professor está no quadro. (The teacher is at the board.)
- Eu tenho muito dever de casa. (I have a lot of homework.)

## Unit 83 — Future Tense (Farei, Fará)

*Slug: `b1-fut-sintetico` · Sequence position: 76.0 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `future-tense`

### Outcomes

- Make formal predictions and talk about distant future
- Use future tense in formal writing
- Understand the difference between two future constructions
- Handle the 3 irregular future verbs (fazer, dizer, trazer)

### Vocabulary

- farei (I will do), fará (he/she will do)
- viajarei (I will travel), comerei (I will eat)
- serei (I will be), estarei (I will be - location/state)
- direi (I will say - irregular)
- trarei (I will bring - irregular)
- amanhã (tomorrow), próxima semana (next week), no futuro (in the future)

### Grammar

- **Future tense formation:** infinitive + -ei/-á/-emos/-ão
- Regular pattern: falar → falarei, falarás, falará, falaremos, falarão
- ONLY 3 irregulars: fazer → farei, dizer → direi, trazer → trarei
- All three drop the middle syllable: fa(ze)r → farei, di(ze)r → direi, tra(ze)r → trarei
- When to use future tense vs "vou + infinitive"

### Exemplar sentences

- Eu falarei com você amanhã. (I will speak with you tomorrow - formal)
- Eles viajarão para o Brasil no próximo ano. (They will travel to Brazil next year.)
- Você fará isso? (Will you do this?)
- Direi a verdade. (I will tell the truth - irregular)
- No futuro, morarei em Lisboa. (In the future, I'll live in Lisbon.)

## Unit 84 — Condicional simples — formas (âncora compartilhada)

*Slug: `b1-condicional` · Sequence position: 76.95 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `conditional-formation`

**Prereqs:** `a2-imp-regular`, `b1-fut-sintetico`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Form the **condicional simples** in BP and EP (regular and irregular stems)
- Recognize the parallel between condicional endings and imperfeito do indicativo endings (both share *-ia / -ias / -ia / -íamos / -iam*)
- Use the form productively in any reported-speech, hypothetical, or polite-request context — variant-specific usage is covered downstream

### Vocabulary

- **falar** → falar**ia**, falar**ias**, falar**ia**, falar**íamos**, falar**iam**
- **comer** → comer**ia**, comer**ias**, comer**ia**, comer**íamos**, comer**iam**
- **partir** → partir**ia**, partir**ias**, partir**ia**, partir**íamos**, partir**iam**

### Grammar

The condicional simples is built on the same stems as the synthetic future (`b1-fut-sintetico`), with personal endings shared with the imperfeito do indicativo.

### Form: infinitive + ending

| Pessoa | Ending | Example (falar) |
|---|---|---|
| eu | -ia | falaria |
| tu | -ias | falarias |
| você / ele / ela | -ia | falaria |
| nós | -íamos | falaríamos |
| vocês / eles / elas | -iam | falariam |

The full infinitive serves as the stem (no clipping), with endings appended directly. This is the same pattern as the futuro do indicativo (which uses *-ei / -ás / -á / -emos / -ão*).

### Irregular stems (3 verbs only)

| Verb | Stem | Example (eu form) |
|---|---|---|
| dizer | dir- | diria |
| fazer | far- | faria |
| trazer | trar- | traria |

These three verbs use clipped/altered stems for both the futuro do indicativo and the condicional. All other verbs use the full infinitive as the stem.

### Minimal exemplar set

- *Eu **gostaria** de viajar para Portugal.* — I'd like to travel to Portugal.
- *Tu **comerias** mais se tivesses fome?* — Would you eat more if you were hungry?
- *Ele **diria** a verdade se pudesse.* — He'd tell the truth if he could.
- *Nós **viajaríamos** mais cedo, mas não dá.* — We'd travel earlier, but it's not possible.
- *Eles **fariam** isso por nós.* — They'd do that for us.

### Drills & artifacts

This unit is a **shared form anchor** — its job is to be a clean prereq target for downstream shared units that touch condicional (reported speech, concessive/purpose clauses, argumentation register). Drill content lives in the variant-specific units.

For BP/EP usage detail and the imperfeito-cortesia substitution pattern, see [[b1-condicional-bp]] / [[b1-condicional-ep]].

### Traps

- **Don't confuse the endings with imperfeito do indicativo.** Condicional: *falaria*. Imperfeito: *falava*. Both share the *-ia/-ias/-ia/-íamos/-iam* PERSONAL endings, but the stem differs. Imperfeito clips the infinitive (*fal-ava*); condicional appends to the full infinitive (*falar-ia*).
- **Only 3 irregular stems.** *Dizer → diria, fazer → faria, trazer → traria*. Every other verb is regular (*ser → seria, ter → teria, vir → viria, ir → iria, pôr → poria, estar → estaria*).
- **This unit teaches form, not usage.** When to *use* condicional — for hypothetical Type 2 main clauses, for politeness, for reported-speech future-backshift — is variant-conditional and covered in `b1-condicional-bp` / `b1-condicional-ep` and downstream cluster units.
- **Spoken EP often substitutes imperfeito do indicativo for condicional in informal speech** (*Eu queria* vs *Eu quereria*). That's a usage choice, not a form gap; the form *quereria* exists and conjugates as expected. The substitution is documented in [[b1-condicional-ep]].

---

## Unit 85 — Conditional Tense (Faria, Gostaria)

*Slug: `b1-condicional-bp` · Sequence position: 77.0 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: bp*

**Concepts:** `conditional-formation`, `conditional-usage`

### Outcomes

- Make polite requests (gostaria de instead of quero)
- Express hypothetical situations
- Give advice using conditional
- Sound more formal and polite in Portuguese

### Vocabulary

- faria (I would do), gostaria (I would like)
- seria (I would be), estaria (I would be - location/state)
- poderia (I could), deveria (I should)
- comeria (I would eat), viajaria (I would travel)
- talvez (maybe), se eu fosse (if I were)

### Grammar

- **Conditional formation:** infinitive + -ia/-ia/-íamos/-iam
- Regular pattern: falar → falaria, falarias, falaria, falaríamos, falariam
- Same 3 irregulars as future: fazer → faria, dizer → diria, trazer → traria
- Note: All persons except nós use same ending (-ia)

### Exemplar sentences

- Gostaria de uma xícara de café. (I would like a cup of coffee - polite)
- Eu viajaria para o Brasil, mas não tenho dinheiro. (I would travel to Brazil, but I don't have money.)
- Você deveria estudar mais. (You should study more.)
- Seria interessante morar em Lisboa. (It would be interesting to live in Lisbon.)
- O que você faria? (What would you do?)

## Unit 86 — É que - Emphatic Questions

*Slug: `a2-e-que` · Sequence position: 78.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `e-que-questions`

### Outcomes

- Ask questions that sound more natural and conversational
- Understand this extremely common BP construction
- Add emphasis and flow to questions
- Sound more like a native BP speaker

### Vocabulary

- é que (emphatic marker)
- onde é que (where...?), o que é que (what...?)
- quando é que (when...?), como é que (how...?)
- por que é que (why...?), qual é que (which...?)
- quanto é que (how much...?)

### Grammar

- **É que construction:** [Question word] + é que + [rest of sentence]
- Makes questions more emphatic and conversational
- EXTREMELY common in Brazilian Portuguese speech
- Optional but very natural-sounding

### Exemplar sentences

- Onde é que você trabalha? (Where do you work?)
- O que é que você está fazendo? (What are you doing?)
- Quando é que você vai viajar? (When are you going to travel?)
- Como é que se faz isso? (How do you do this?)
- Por que é que você não foi? (Why didn't you go?)
- Qual é que é o seu? (Which one is yours?)

## Unit 87 — Crase (à, às)

*Slug: `b1-crase` · Sequence position: 79.0 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `crase`

### Outcomes

- Use crase correctly with feminine nouns
- Tell time with às + hours
- Use direction expressions (à esquerda/direita)
- Understand when crase is required

### Vocabulary

- à (to the - feminine singular)
- às (to the - feminine plural)
- à esquerda (to/on the left)
- à direita (to/on the right)
- às três horas (at 3 o'clock)
- ir à praia (go to the beach)
- à noite (at night)

### Grammar

- **Crase:** contraction of a (preposition) + a (article) = à
- Written with grave accent: à
- Plural form: às (a + as)
- ONLY occurs with feminine articles
- One of the trickiest aspects of Portuguese!

### Exemplar sentences

- Vou à praia. (I'm going to the beach.)
- Vire à direita. (Turn right.)
- Às três horas. (At 3 o'clock.)
- Vou à escola. (I'm going to school.)
- À noite, eu estudo. (At night, I study.)
- Às vezes, eu viajo. (Sometimes, I travel.)

## Unit 88 — Pronome relativo *que* — pronome relativo padrão

*Slug: `b1-relativo-que` · Sequence position: 79.5 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `relative-pronouns`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Use **que** as the default relative pronoun for both subject and object positions, with both human and non-human antecedents
- Distinguish **restrictive** relative clauses (no commas, defines the antecedent) from **non-restrictive** ones (with commas, adds info about an already-identified antecedent)
- Avoid English-style preposition stranding — Portuguese requires the preposition to precede the relative pronoun

### Vocabulary

- **que** — that / which / who (default relative)
- Common preposition + relative combinations (with *quem* for [+human], *que* otherwise — see `b1-relativo-quem`):
  - *com que / com quem* — with which / with whom
  - *de que / de quem* — of which / of whom
  - *em que* — in which
  - *a que / a quem* — to which / to whom

### Grammar

**Que** is the workhorse relative pronoun: invariable in form, usable for any antecedent (human, non-human, abstract), serving as either subject or direct object of the relative clause.

### Restrictive vs non-restrictive

| Type | Punctuation | Meaning |
|---|---|---|
| Restrictive | no commas | defines / restricts the antecedent (which X?) |
| Non-restrictive | with commas | adds info about an already-known antecedent |

- *O homem **que mora ao lado** é simpático.* — The man who lives next door is nice. (restrictive — *which* man)
- *O João, **que mora ao lado**, é simpático.* — João, who lives next door, is nice. (non-restrictive — adds info about a specific person)

### Subject vs object position in the relative clause

- *A pessoa **que veio** é minha amiga.* — The person who came is my friend. (que = subject of *veio*)
- *O livro **que comprei** está aqui.* — The book that I bought is here. (que = direct object of *comprei*)

Portuguese never drops the relative pronoun. English permits *"the book I bought"* (no relative); Portuguese requires *o livro **que** comprei*.

### Preposition placement

Portuguese **does not allow preposition stranding**. The preposition must come BEFORE the relative pronoun:

| Wrong (English-influenced) | Right (Portuguese) |
|---|---|
| *O homem que falei com.* | *O homem com quem falei.* (use quem after preposition for [+human]) |
| *A casa que moro em.* | *A casa em que moro.* / *A casa onde moro.* |
| *O assunto que falamos sobre.* | *O assunto sobre o qual falamos.* / *O assunto de que falamos.* |

For [+human] antecedents after a preposition, **quem** typically replaces que (see `b1-relativo-quem`). For non-human antecedents, *em que / de que / com que / por que* are common.

### Exemplar sentences

- *Conheço o autor **que escreveu** este livro.* — I know the author who wrote this book.
- *Os filmes **que vi** ontem eram interessantes.* — The films I saw yesterday were interesting.
- *A casa **em que moramos** é antiga.* — The house we live in is old.
- *A Maria, **que é minha vizinha**, vai mudar-se.* — Maria, who is my neighbor, is going to move.
- *Não gosto do café **que serviram**.* — I don't like the coffee they served.
- *O dia **em que nos conhecemos** foi inesquecível.* — The day we met was unforgettable.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a restrictive vs non-restrictive comma drill, plus a preposition-stranding correction drill (high-error pattern for English speakers). Pair with b1-relativo-quem for the [+human] split. -->

### Traps

- **Don't drop the relative pronoun.** English allows *"the book I bought"*; Portuguese requires *o livro que comprei*. The que is mandatory.
- **Don't strand prepositions.** *O homem que falei com* is wrong. The preposition must precede the relative pronoun.
- **Don't overuse o qual.** For most cases, simple *que* is the natural choice. *O qual* / *a qual* (see `b1-relativo-formal-locativo`) is reserved for formal contexts or disambiguation — pulling it out where *que* would suffice sounds bookish.
- **Restrictive vs non-restrictive comma matters semantically.** *Os meus irmãos que moram em Lisboa vêm visitar* (restrictive — only the brothers who live in Lisbon are visiting; implies others don't live there) vs *Os meus irmãos, que moram em Lisboa, vêm visitar* (non-restrictive — all brothers live in Lisbon and they're visiting).
- **Subject que vs object que looks identical.** Disambiguation is positional / semantic. *O homem que viu o João* (the man who saw João — que = subject) vs *O homem que o João viu* (the man whom João saw — que = object). The verb's argument structure tells you which.

---

## Unit 89 — Pronome relativo *quem* — antecedente humano após preposição

*Slug: `b1-relativo-quem` · Sequence position: 79.6 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `relative-pronouns`

**Prereqs:** `b1-relativo-que`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Use **quem** as the [+human] relative pronoun after a preposition (*de quem, com quem, para quem, sobre quem, a quem, em quem*)
- Recognize that quem WITHOUT a preposition is rare in modern Portuguese (use *que* instead, even for human antecedents)
- Avoid English-influenced "that I work with" constructions — Portuguese fronts the preposition

### Vocabulary

Common preposition + quem combinations:

- **a quem** — to whom
- **com quem** — with whom
- **de quem** — of whom / about whom
- **em quem** — in whom (trust, faith)
- **para quem** — for whom
- **por quem** — for whom (cause / sake)
- **sobre quem** — about whom

### Grammar

**Quem** is the [+human] relative pronoun, almost always used after a preposition. It's invariable in form but encodes the [+human] feature.

### When to use quem

| Context | Pronoun | Example |
|---|---|---|
| Subject of relative clause, [+human] | **que** | *A pessoa **que** veio…* |
| Direct object of relative clause, [+human] | **que** | *A pessoa **que** vi…* |
| After preposition, [+human] | **quem** | *A pessoa **com quem** falei…* |
| After preposition, [-human] | **que** | *A casa **em que** moro…* |

The preposition + quem combination is the canonical [+human] relative construction. Without a preposition, quem alone is essentially restricted to proverbs and fixed expressions (*Quem cala consente* — "Silence implies consent"; *Quem ri por último ri melhor* — "He who laughs last laughs best").

### Exemplar sentences

- *A pessoa **de quem** te falei mora em Coimbra.* — The person I told you about lives in Coimbra.
- *A mulher **com quem** trabalho é portuguesa.* — The woman I work with is Portuguese.
- *O amigo **para quem** comprei o presente já o recebeu.* — The friend I bought the gift for has already received it.
- *A criança **a quem** dei o livro adorou-o.* — The child I gave the book to loved it.
- *O candidato **em quem** voto sempre é honesto.* — The candidate I always vote for is honest.
- *A artista **sobre quem** escrevi a tese expôs em Lisboa.* — The artist I wrote my thesis about exhibited in Lisbon.

### Quem vs que after a preposition

For [+human] antecedents, both *com que* and *com quem* are sometimes possible — but **quem is the strong default**. Que after a preposition with a human antecedent sounds awkward or substandard:

- *A mulher com quem trabalho.* ← natural
- *A mulher com que trabalho.* ← marked / heavy

For [-human] antecedents, *que* dominates and *quem* is wrong:

- *A casa em que moro.* ← right
- *A casa em quem moro.* ← wrong (quem requires [+human])

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a [+human] / [-human] disambiguation drill — given an antecedent and a preposition, pick que vs quem. -->

### Traps

- **Don't use quem without a preposition for animate referents.** *A pessoa quem mora aqui* is wrong; use *A pessoa que mora aqui* (subject position takes que regardless of [+human]). Preposition is the trigger for quem.
- **Quem is invariable.** No gender or number agreement. *As pessoas com quem trabalho* (plural antecedent, quem stays singular form).
- **Preposition-stranding is wrong in Portuguese.** *A pessoa que falei com* — wrong. *A pessoa com quem falei* — right.
- **Standalone quem in modern usage is mostly fixed-expression territory.** *Quem viu, viu* (whoever saw, saw — proverb-like). Don't reach for standalone quem in normal sentence construction.
- **Don't confuse with interrogative quem.** Same word, different role. *Quem veio?* (interrogative — Who came?) vs *A pessoa de quem te falei* (relative — about whom). Both forms are pronounced and spelled identically; context disambiguates.

---

## Unit 90 — Pronome relativo *cujo* — possessivo (concorda com o possuído)

*Slug: `b1-relativo-cujo` · Sequence position: 79.7 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `relative-pronouns`, `possessives`

**Prereqs:** `b1-relativo-que`, `a1-poss-meu`, `a1-ser-identity`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Use **cujo / cuja / cujos / cujas** as the possessive relative pronoun ("whose")
- Apply the agreement rule that's counterintuitive for English speakers: **cujo agrees with the THING POSSESSED, not with the possessor**
- Avoid the common error of inserting an article between cujo and the noun (*cujo o nome* — wrong; *cujo nome* — right)
- Recognize cujo as semi-formal — common in writing, less common in casual speech

### Vocabulary

- **cujo** (m sg) — whose [m sg thing]
- **cuja** (f sg) — whose [f sg thing]
- **cujos** (m pl) — whose [m pl thing]
- **cujas** (f pl) — whose [f pl thing]

### Grammar

Cujo is the possessive relative pronoun. It links an antecedent (the possessor) to a possessed noun in the relative clause. The agreement is the high-leverage rule:

**Cujo agrees with the noun that follows it (the possessed thing), NOT with the antecedent (the possessor).**

This inverts English speakers' intuition, where "whose" is invariable and the agreement question doesn't arise.

### The agreement rule

- *A mulher **cujo nome** esqueci.* — The woman whose name I forgot.
  - *cujo* is masculine singular because **nome** (the possessed thing) is masc sg, NOT because *mulher* is feminine.
- *O homem **cuja casa** visitamos.* — The man whose house we visited.
  - *cuja* is feminine singular because **casa** is fem sg, NOT because *homem* is masc.
- *A escola **cujos alunos** foram premiados.* — The school whose students were awarded.
  - *cujos* is masculine plural because **alunos** is masc pl.
- *O livro **cujas páginas** estão rasgadas.* — The book whose pages are torn.
  - *cujas* is feminine plural because **páginas** is fem pl.

### No article between cujo and the noun

This is mandatory and a common error point:

| Wrong | Right |
|---|---|
| *A mulher cujo o nome esqueci.* | A mulher **cujo nome** esqueci. |
| *O homem cuja a casa visitamos.* | O homem **cuja casa** visitamos. |

Cujo absorbs the article function — adding *o/a* on top is ungrammatical.

### Cujo can follow a preposition

- *O autor **a cujo livro** me referi…* — The author whose book I referred to…
- *A empresa **em cujos escritórios** trabalho…* — The company in whose offices I work…

When a preposition combines with the article-bearing word in the noun phrase, contractions apply: *de* + *cujo* → *de cujo* (no contraction needed since cujo isn't an article); *em* + *cujos* → *em cujos*. The contractions students know from *de + o = do* don't apply to cujo itself.

### Exemplar sentences

- *Conheci um escritor **cuja obra** vou ler.* — I met a writer whose work I'll read.
- *A casa **cujo telhado** está partido precisa de obras.* — The house whose roof is broken needs repairs.
- *Contratámos a empresa **cujas referências** eram melhores.* — We hired the company whose references were better.
- *O cliente **cujo pedido** chegou primeiro será atendido primeiro.* — The customer whose order arrived first will be served first.
- *Estudei com professores **cujos métodos** ainda uso.* — I studied with professors whose methods I still use.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a cujo-agreement drill — given an antecedent + possessed-noun pair, pick the right cujo form. High-error pattern: students agree cujo with the antecedent. -->

### Traps

- **The agreement-with-possessed rule is the biggest trap.** English speakers default to agreeing cujo with the antecedent (*a mulher cuja nome* — wrong, because *nome* is masc not fem). Drill the rule explicitly: look at the noun AFTER cujo, not the noun before.
- **Don't insert an article.** *Cujo o nome* is wrong; *cujo nome* is right. Cujo replaces the article.
- **Register: semi-formal.** Cujo is standard in writing and educated speech. In very casual conversation, speakers sometimes work around it: *A mulher que esqueci o nome dela* (with anaphoric *dela*) — substandard but heard. Teach cujo as the target form; don't endorse the workaround.
- **Cujo doesn't combine with quem.** *A pessoa cujo livro li* is right (the person whose book I read). *A pessoa de quem o livro li* is awkward — when possession is the relation, use cujo.
- **Don't confuse possession with restrictive description.** *A pessoa cujo carro avariou* (the person whose car broke down) vs *A pessoa que tem o carro vermelho* (the person who has the red car). Cujo specifically marks possession-of-X-by-Y; *que tem* is just description.

---

## Unit 91 — Pronomes relativos *o qual* (formal) e *onde* (locativo)

*Slug: `b1-relativo-formal-locativo` · Sequence position: 79.8 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `relative-pronouns`

**Prereqs:** `b1-relativo-que`, `b1-relativo-quem`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Use **o qual / a qual / os quais / as quais** as a formal alternative to *que*, especially after prepositions and in disambiguation contexts
- Use **onde** as the locative relative pronoun for static location (and *aonde / de onde / por onde* with motion verbs)
- Recognize that o qual is register-marked (formal/written) while onde is unmarked
- Avoid the dialectal extension of onde to temporal contexts (*o dia onde* — nonstandard)

### Vocabulary

**O qual family** (formal alternative to *que*):

- **o qual** (m sg) — which
- **a qual** (f sg) — which
- **os quais** (m pl) — which (plural)
- **as quais** (f pl) — which (plural)

These agree with their antecedent (unlike cujo, which agrees with the possessed thing).

**Onde** — locative:

- **onde** — where (static location)
- **aonde** — to where (with motion verbs: ir, chegar)
- **de onde** — from where
- **por onde** — through where / by which way

### Grammar

### O qual / a qual — when to choose over *que*

Three contexts where *o qual* is preferred or required:

**1. After a preposition, for clarification.** When the relative clause has a complex preposition or when *que* could be ambiguous:

- *Trabalho num projeto **sobre o qual** escrevi um artigo.* (formal) — I work on a project I wrote an article about.
- Less formal alternative: *Trabalho num projeto **sobre que** escrevi um artigo.* (acceptable but heavier)
- *A casa **dentro da qual** vivemos está velha.* — The house we live inside of is old. (with *dentro de* + relative)

**2. To disambiguate when *que* could refer to multiple antecedents.**

- *A irmã do João, **a qual** mora em Faro, vai casar-se.* — João's sister, who lives in Faro, is getting married. (*a qual* = the sister, not João — disambiguation)
- *A irmã do João, **que mora em Faro**, vai casar-se.* — Same sentence with *que*: ambiguous, could be sister or João.

**3. In formal/written register.** Newspapers, academic prose, legal documents reach for *o qual* more freely than spoken Portuguese.

For most everyday cases, **simple *que* is the natural choice** — *o qual* can sound bookish if used where *que* would suffice.

### Onde — locative relative

Onde is the locative relative pronoun for **static location**:

- *A casa **onde moro** é antiga.* — The house where I live is old.
- *O lugar **onde nos conhecemos** está fechado agora.* — The place where we met is closed now.
- *Visitámos a aldeia **onde nasceu o meu avô**.* — We visited the village where my grandfather was born.

With **motion verbs**, the directional preposition combines with onde:

- *Vamos para a praia **aonde** o João foi ontem.* — We're going to the beach (to) where João went yesterday.
- *Esta é a cidade **de onde** sou.* — This is the city I'm from.
- *O caminho **por onde** passámos era estreito.* — The path we passed through was narrow.

Onde can usually be replaced by *em que* in static-location contexts:

- *A casa **onde moro** = A casa **em que moro***.

### Exemplar sentences

- *O acordo **ao qual** chegámos foi satisfatório.* — The agreement we reached was satisfactory. (formal)
- *A universidade **na qual** estudei é em Coimbra.* — The university I studied at is in Coimbra. (alt: *em que*)
- *A época **em que vivemos** é incerta.* — The time we live in is uncertain. (NOT *onde vivemos* — temporal, not locative)
- *O parque **onde brincava** quando era criança ainda existe.* — The park where I played as a child still exists.
- *Não conheço o autor **do qual** falaste.* — I don't know the author you spoke of. (formal alt: *de quem*, since the antecedent is human)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a register-switching drill (que vs o qual in the same sentence frame, identify which fits each register). Build a static-vs-motion onde drill (onde vs aonde vs de onde). -->

### Traps

- **Don't use onde for time.** *O dia onde nos conhecemos* is dialectal/nonstandard. Use *o dia em que nos conhecemos*. Onde is strictly locative in standard Portuguese.
- **Don't overuse o qual.** Where simple *que* works, prefer *que*. *O qual* sounds heavy in casual contexts. Reserve it for genuine clarification needs or formal writing.
- **O qual agrees with the antecedent (unlike cujo, which agrees with the possessed thing).** *A casa na qual moro* (a qual fem because casa is fem). *Os livros sobre os quais falámos* (os quais masc pl because livros is masc pl).
- **Aonde vs onde.** *Aonde* (= a + onde) is for motion-toward. *Onde* alone is for static location. *Vou aonde queres* (motion); *Estou onde combinámos* (static). Some speakers conflate them; the distinction is prescriptively required and the standard target.
- **Don't double-mark with relative + clitic.** *A casa onde moro nela* — wrong (the *nela* duplicates the locative reference). Just *A casa onde moro*.
- **Em + o qual = no qual / na qual; de + o qual = do qual / da qual.** Standard preposition-article contractions apply (the *o/a* in *o qual* behaves like a definite article for contraction purposes).

---

## Unit 92 — Todo vs Tudo

*Slug: `a2-todo-tudo` · Sequence position: 80.0 · CEFR: A2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `todo-vs-tudo`

### Outcomes

- Distinguish between todo (adjective) and tudo (pronoun)
- Use common expressions with todo/tudo correctly
- Use "todo mundo" for "everyone"
- Greet with "Tudo bem?"

### Vocabulary

- todo/toda (all, every - adjective)
- todos/todas (all - plural)
- tudo (everything - pronoun)
- todo o/toda a (the whole)
- todos os dias (every day)
- todo mundo (everyone)
- Tudo bem? (Everything okay?)

### Grammar

- **Todo/toda:** adjective that agrees with noun (all, every, whole)
- **Tudo:** invariable pronoun meaning "everything"
- Never confuse them - different parts of speech!

### Exemplar sentences

- Todo dia eu estudo. (Every day I study.)
- Todos os alunos estão aqui. (All the students are here.)
- Tudo bem? (Everything okay? / How are you?)
- Eu fiz tudo. (I did everything.)
- Todo mundo gosta de música. (Everyone likes music.)
- Ela trabalha toda semana. (She works every week.)

### Drills & artifacts

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

## Unit 93 — Voz passiva analítica (ser + particípio)

*Slug: `b1-passiva-ser` · Sequence position: 80.5 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `passive-voice`

**Prereqs:** `a1-ser-identity`, `b1-mais-que-perfeito-ind`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Transform active sentences into the analytic passive (**ser + particípio**) preserving tense, person, and agreement
- Introduce the agent with **por / pela / pelo / pelos / pelas** when needed, or omit it when irrelevant
- Apply past-participle agreement with the grammatical subject (gender + number)
- Choose between active and passive based on whether the speaker wants to foreground the agent or the affected entity

### Vocabulary

- **ser** — auxiliary for the analytic passive (conjugates in any tense)
- **por / pela / pelo / pelos / pelas** — agent introducer (*por* + article contractions)
- Past participles — review the irregular set: *dito, feito, posto, visto, escrito, aberto, ganho, gasto, aceito/aceitado, eleito/elegido*

### Grammar

The analytic passive transforms an active sentence by:
1. Promoting the direct object to grammatical subject
2. Conjugating *ser* in the corresponding tense
3. Adding the past participle of the main verb (agreeing in gender + number with the new subject)
4. Optionally introducing the original subject as agent with *por*

### Active → passive transformation

| Active | Passive |
|---|---|
| A Ana fez o bolo. | O bolo foi feito (pela Ana). |
| Os engenheiros construíram a ponte. | A ponte foi construída (pelos engenheiros). |
| O autor escreveu estas cartas. | Estas cartas foram escritas (pelo autor). |

### Tense correspondence

The auxiliary *ser* takes whichever tense the active verb had:

| Active tense | Passive form |
|---|---|
| Presente: *escreve* | é escrito/a |
| Pretérito: *escreveu* | foi escrito/a |
| Imperfeito: *escrevia* | era escrito/a |
| Futuro: *escreverá* | será escrito/a |
| Condicional: *escreveria* | seria escrito/a |
| Pretérito composto: *tem escrito* | tem sido escrito/a |
| Subjuntivo presente: *(que) escreva* | (que) seja escrito/a |
| Subjuntivo imperfeito: *(se) escrevesse* | (se) fosse escrito/a |

### Participle agreement

The participle agrees with the **grammatical subject** of the passive sentence (the promoted object):

- *O livro foi **escrito** pela Ana.* — masc sg
- *A carta foi **escrita** pela Ana.* — fem sg
- *Os livros foram **escritos** pela Ana.* — masc pl
- *As cartas foram **escritas** pela Ana.* — fem pl

### Agent introduction

Use *por* + article contractions for the agent:

- *por + o = pelo*
- *por + a = pela*
- *por + os = pelos*
- *por + as = pelas*

Examples:
- *O bolo foi comprado **pelo** padeiro.*
- *A casa foi construída **pela** empresa.*
- *Os documentos foram assinados **pelos** advogados.*
- *As fotos foram tiradas **pela** Maria.*

The agent is **optional**. Omit it when irrelevant or unknown:

- *O livro foi publicado em 2020.* — agent unmentioned
- *As janelas foram partidas durante a tempestade.* — agent unmentioned

### Exemplar sentences

- *Esta canção **foi composta** em 1978.* — This song was composed in 1978.
- *Os documentos **serão entregues** amanhã.* — The documents will be delivered tomorrow.
- *O presidente **foi eleito** em outubro.* — The president was elected in October.
- *As decisões **são tomadas** pela direção.* — The decisions are made by management.
- *A obra **tinha sido feita** antes do incêndio.* — The work had been done before the fire.
- *É importante que a verdade **seja dita**.* — It's important that the truth be told. (subjuntivo presente)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build an active → passive transformation drill across multiple tenses, with and without agent. Pair with b1-passiva-se for construction-choice practice. -->

### Traps

- **Forgetting participle agreement is the most common error.** *O livro foi feita* (wrong — *feito* should be masc sg). The participle's gender/number tracks the grammatical subject, not the agent.
- **Por vs pelo/pela/pelos/pelas.** *Por João* is wrong if João takes an article (*O João foi visto*). *Pelo João foi feito o trabalho* — pelo because *o João* contracts. Apply normal *por +* article contractions.
- **Don't overuse passive in casual Portuguese.** Spoken Portuguese (BP and EP both) prefers active constructions much more than English does. *O livro foi escrito por ele* sounds heavy compared to *Ele escreveu o livro*. Reserve passive for when the agent really doesn't matter or when the affected entity is the topic.
- **Don't conflate ser-passive with estar-passive (estar + particípio).** *O livro foi escrito* (action: someone wrote it) vs *O livro está escrito* (state: it's currently in written form). Different aspects entirely. The unit covers ser-passive only; estar + particípio is a separate construction.
- **Double participles matter here.** Some verbs have both regular and irregular participles, and the passive uses the irregular one: *aceitar → aceito* (passive: *foi aceito*, NOT *foi aceitado*). Same with *eleger → eleito* (passive: *foi eleito*, NOT *foi elegido*). The unit `b2-participios-duplos` (Phase 2 placeholder, future enrichment) catalogs the full pair list.
- **Particípios irregulares anchor here.** This unit assumes participle forms from prior compound-tense exposure (`b1-mais-que-perfeito-ind`, `b1-pret-perfeito-composto-bp/ep`). A dedicated participle-introduction unit doesn't yet exist in the corpus — backlog item.

---

## Unit 94 — Passiva sintética / impessoal (verbo + se)

*Slug: `b1-passiva-se` · Sequence position: 80.6 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `passive-se`

**Prereqs:** `b1-passiva-ser`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Use the **passive-se** construction for generic statements, instructions, commercial signs, and impersonal contexts where no agent is mentioned
- Apply the prescriptive verb-agreement rule (verb agrees in number with the promoted object) and recognize the colloquial-usage exception (singular verb regardless of object number)
- Distinguish passive-se from reflexive-se from reciprocal-se from impersonal-se — same clitic, four functions
- Choose between ser-passive and passive-se based on register and whether the agent is even potentially mentionable

### Vocabulary

- **se** — clitic marking passive/impersonal use (same form as reflexive *se*, distinct function)
- Common passive-se verbs: *vender, alugar, comprar, procurar, falar, fazer, escrever, dizer, viver*

### Grammar

The passive-se construction promotes a direct object to the position of grammatical subject and uses the clitic *se* in place of an agent-marked passive auxiliary. The agent is **never expressible** in this construction — that's its core distinguishing feature.

### Pattern

`verbo-conjugado + se + objeto-direto-promovido`

- *Vendem-se livros.* — Books are sold (here / by us, no agent mentionable).
- *Aluga-se apartamento.* — Apartment for rent.
- *Procura-se programador.* — Programmer wanted.

### Verb agreement — prescriptive vs colloquial

Prescriptive grammar: verb agrees in number with the promoted object.

| Object number | Prescriptive verb form |
|---|---|
| Singular | *Vende-se casa.* |
| Plural | *Vendem-se casas.* |

Colloquial usage (heard in BP and EP both): verb stays singular regardless of object number.

| Colloquial form | Status |
|---|---|
| *Vende-se casas.* | Heard frequently; considered substandard by traditional grammars |
| *Aluga-se apartamentos.* | Same — substandard but common |

The prescriptive form is what to teach for production; the colloquial form is what students will encounter on real shop signs and news headlines.

### Common contexts

| Context | Example |
|---|---|
| Commercial signs | *Vende-se / Aluga-se / Trespassa-se* |
| Job ads | *Procura-se cozinheiro com experiência.* |
| Generic statements | *Aqui se fala português.* / *Não se fuma na escola.* |
| News headlines | *Discutiu-se a proposta no parlamento.* |
| Instructions | *Misturam-se os ingredientes lentamente.* |
| Impersonal generalizations | *Vive-se bem em Lisboa.* (impersonal-se, often grouped with passive-se) |

### Passive-se vs ser-passive — when to choose which

| Use ser-passive when… | Use passive-se when… |
|---|---|
| Agent matters or might be mentioned | Agent is irrelevant or unknown |
| Formal / written register | Generic / commercial / instruction context |
| Specific affected entity in focus | Generic / class-of-things in focus |

Examples:

- *O livro foi escrito **por ela**.* (ser-passive — agent named) → can't switch to passive-se without losing the agent.
- *Vendem-se livros usados.* (passive-se — generic, no agent) → switching to ser-passive (*Livros usados são vendidos*) sounds odd; the passive-se carries the commercial-sign register.

### Exemplar sentences

- *Vendem-se livros usados.* — Used books for sale.
- *Aluga-se quarto a estudantes.* — Room for rent for students.
- *Procura-se cozinheiro experiente.* — Experienced cook wanted.
- *Aqui se fala português, espanhol e inglês.* — Portuguese, Spanish, and English spoken here.
- *Não se permite fumar nesta sala.* — Smoking is not permitted in this room.
- *Discutiram-se vários assuntos na reunião.* — Several matters were discussed at the meeting.
- *Vive-se bem nesta cidade.* — One lives well in this city. / Life is good in this city. (impersonal-se reading)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a passive-se vs reflexive-se disambiguation drill (same clitic form, different functions). Build a register-choice drill: passive-se vs ser-passive given a context cue. -->

### Traps

- **Don't confuse passive-se with reflexive-se.** Same clitic form, different function. Reflexive: *Ela se chama Maria* / *Chama-se Maria* (the subject acts on themselves). Passive: *Vendem-se livros* (no subject acts; the verb describes what happens to the object). Context disambiguates.
- **Don't try to add an agent.** *Vende-se a casa pelo proprietário* is wrong — the construction structurally excludes agents. If you want to mention the agent, use ser-passive: *A casa é vendida pelo proprietário*.
- **Verb agreement is variable in real usage but prescriptive in classroom Portuguese.** Drill the prescriptive form (*vendem-se livros*) for production; recognize the colloquial form (*vende-se livros*) for comprehension. On exam-grade writing, always agree.
- **Clitic placement applies to the *se* per variant rules.** BP often uses proclisis with passive-se (*Aqui se fala português*); EP defaults to enclisis (*Fala-se português aqui*). Both forms exist in both variants depending on triggers — see [[a2-reflexivos-bp]] / [[a2-reflexivos-ep]] for the full clitic-placement rules. The *se* in passive-se follows those same rules.
- **Some verbs resist passive-se.** Intransitive verbs can't take it. Verbs whose direct object is a person typically prefer ser-passive (*Foi visto pelo polícia* > *Viu-se ele*). The construction is most natural with concrete-noun direct objects (*livros, casas, carros, apartamentos*).
- **Impersonal-se reading.** When the verb has no direct object, *se* makes the construction impersonal: *Vive-se bem aqui* (one lives well here / life is good here). Some grammars classify this separately; pedagogically it sits naturally with passive-se as part of the same agentless-construction family.

---

## Unit 95 — Discurso direto vs discurso indireto (declarativo)

*Slug: `b1-discurso-direto-indireto` · Sequence position: 80.7 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `reported-speech`, `tense-backshift`

**Prereqs:** `a2-pret-vs-imp`, `b1-mais-que-perfeito-ind`, `b1-condicional`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Transform direct quotations into reported (indirect) speech using verbs of saying (*dizer, comentar, afirmar, contar, responder*)
- Apply **tense backshift** when the reporting verb is in a past tense (presente → imperfeito, pretérito → mais-que-perfeito, futuro → condicional)
- Adjust pronouns and time/place adverbials to match the reporter's perspective
- Recognize when backshift is NOT needed (reporting verb in present, current relevance preserved)

### Vocabulary

Reporting verbs:

- **dizer** — to say (default reporting verb)
- **comentar** — to comment
- **afirmar** — to affirm / state
- **contar** — to tell (a story / fact)
- **responder** — to reply
- **explicar** — to explain
- **declarar** — to declare (formal)

Connector:

- **que** — that (mandatory between reporting verb and the reported clause)

### Grammar

Reported speech transforms a direct quotation into a subordinate `que`-clause attached to a verb of saying. Three things may shift:

1. **Tense** of the reported verb (backshift, when reporting verb is past)
2. **Pronouns** (1st-person typically becomes 3rd-person)
3. **Time and place adverbials** (deictic shift)

### Tense backshift table

When the reporting verb is in a **past tense** (most common), the reported verb shifts:

| Direct (in quotation) | Reported (after past reporting verb) |
|---|---|
| Presente: *"Vou ao cinema."* | Imperfeito: *Disse que ia ao cinema.* |
| Pretérito: *"Comi a pizza."* | Mais-que-perfeito: *Disse que tinha comido a pizza.* |
| Imperfeito: *"Estava cansado."* | Imperfeito (no shift): *Disse que estava cansado.* |
| Futuro: *"Vou viajar."* | Condicional: *Disse que viajaria.* |
| Condicional: *"Iria, mas não posso."* | Condicional (no shift): *Disse que iria, mas não podia.* |
| Subjuntivo presente: *"Talvez chova."* | Imperfeito subjuntivo: *Disse que talvez chovesse.* |

The future-backshift use of condicional is the reason this unit prereqs `b1-condicional`.

### When the reporting verb is in present — no backshift

If the reporting verb is in present (or present perfect with current relevance), tenses are typically preserved:

- Direct: *"Vou ao cinema."* → Reported: *Ele diz que vai ao cinema.* (no shift)
- Direct: *"Comi a pizza."* → Reported: *Ele diz que comeu a pizza.* (no shift)

This is common in news headlines, live commentary, or reports of recent statements.

### Pronoun adjustment

Pronouns shift to match the reporter's perspective:

- Direct: *"Eu vou ao cinema com a minha irmã."*
- Reported: *Ele disse que ele ia ao cinema com a irmã dele.* (or naturally: *Ele disse que ia ao cinema com a irmã.*)

The 1st-person reference in the original becomes a 3rd-person reference, and possessives shift accordingly.

### Time and place adverbials

Deictic adverbs shift to match the new temporal/spatial frame:

| Direct | Reported (past frame) |
|---|---|
| hoje | naquele dia |
| amanhã | no dia seguinte |
| ontem | no dia anterior / na véspera |
| agora | naquele momento |
| aqui | ali / lá |
| este | aquele |

These shifts apply when the reporting context is clearly displaced from the original utterance. In live or near-live reports, they may not apply.

### Exemplar transformations

| Direct | Reported (past) |
|---|---|
| *"Eu estudo português."* | Disse que estudava português. |
| *"Vamos ao restaurante hoje."* | Disse que iam ao restaurante naquele dia. |
| *"Já terminei o trabalho."* | Disse que já tinha terminado o trabalho. |
| *"Vou comprar um carro novo."* | Disse que ia comprar um carro novo. (or: que compraria) |
| *"Talvez chegue tarde."* | Disse que talvez chegasse tarde. |
| *"Comprei o presente ontem."* | Disse que tinha comprado o presente no dia anterior. |

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a backshift-table drill (given a Direct sentence, produce the Reported version with the right tense shift). Build a pronoun-adjustment drill separately. Pair with b1-perguntas-indiretas for full reported-speech coverage. -->

### Traps

- **Forgetting backshift in spoken usage.** Casual BP often skips backshift: *Ele disse que vai ao cinema* (no shift, common in spoken BP) instead of *Ele disse que ia ao cinema*. Teach backshift as the target form for production; recognize the no-shift form as a real spoken pattern.
- **Over-applying backshift when reporting verb is in present.** *Ele diz que ia ao cinema* is wrong if the original was "Vou ao cinema" — present reporting verb keeps present in the reported clause. *Ele diz que vai* is right.
- **Pronoun confusion in nested reports.** "He said that I told him I'd go" — chains of reporters create ambiguity. Be explicit about who *eu* refers to in each layer.
- **Don't drop the connector *que*.** English allows *"He said he'd go"*; Portuguese requires *Ele disse **que** ia*. The *que* is mandatory.
- **Time-adverb shift is context-dependent.** *Ele disse que vinha hoje* can be correct if the reporting and the original utterance are on the same day. The shift to *naquele dia* applies when the reporting frame is clearly displaced.
- **Subjuntivo-leaning EP usage.** EP slightly more often retains subjuntivo in reported clauses where BP allows indicative: *Disse-me que viesse* (EP, subj — a request being reported) vs *Disse-me que vinha* (BP, indicative — a statement being reported). Both forms are correct; the choice tracks whether the original utterance was a directive (subj) or assertion (indic).

---

## Unit 96 — Perguntas indiretas (yes/no com *se*, conteúdo com wh-words)

*Slug: `b1-perguntas-indiretas` · Sequence position: 80.8 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `reported-speech`, `indirect-questions`, `tense-backshift`

**Prereqs:** `b1-discurso-direto-indireto`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Convert direct yes/no questions into indirect questions using **se** (whether)
- Convert direct content questions into indirect questions retaining the **wh-word** (*onde, quando, como, por que, quem, o que*)
- Apply non-inversion in indirect questions — word order reverts to declarative even though the meaning is interrogative
- Inherit tense backshift rules from `b1-discurso-direto-indireto` when the reporting verb is past

### Vocabulary

Reporting verbs for questions:

- **perguntar** — to ask (default reporting verb for questions)
- **questionar** — to question (more formal)
- **querer saber** — to want to know (= "asked whether")

Question-clause connectors:

- **se** — whether / if (yes/no questions)
- **onde** — where
- **quando** — when
- **como** — how
- **por que / porquê** — why
- **quem** — who
- **o que / o quê** — what
- **qual / quais** — which

### Grammar

Indirect questions are subordinate clauses introduced by *se* (for yes/no questions) or a wh-word (for content questions). The most distinctive feature is **non-inversion**: the subordinate clause uses declarative word order, even though the meaning is a question.

### Yes/no questions — *se*

Direct yes/no question → *se*-clause:

| Direct | Indirect |
|---|---|
| *"Você quer ir?"* | *Ele perguntou **se** eu queria ir.* |
| *"Está pronto?"* | *Ela quis saber **se** estava pronto.* |
| *"Vens amanhã?"* | *Perguntei **se** vinhas no dia seguinte.* |

The *se* in this construction is **the conjunction "whether"**, not the conditional "if." Functionally similar but syntactically distinct from the *se* in conditional sentences.

### Content questions — wh-word retained

Direct content question → wh-word + declarative-order clause:

| Direct | Indirect |
|---|---|
| *"Onde ele mora?"* | *Ele perguntou **onde** eu morava.* |
| *"Quando vais voltar?"* | *Ela quis saber **quando** voltaria.* |
| *"Como você descobriu?"* | *Perguntou **como** eu tinha descoberto.* |
| *"Por que ela saiu?"* | *Não disse **por que** tinha saído.* |
| *"Quem te chamou?"* | *Perguntou **quem** me tinha chamado.* |
| *"O que aconteceu?"* | *Quis saber **o que** tinha acontecido.* |

### Non-inversion is the key rule

Direct questions in Portuguese can use inversion or intonation:

- *"Onde mora ele?"* (inverted, somewhat formal)
- *"Onde é que ele mora?"* (with *é que*, common)
- *"Onde ele mora?"* (no inversion, intonation only — most common in spoken use)

Indirect questions **always use declarative word order** — subject before verb:

- *Perguntou onde **ele mora**.* ← right (subj-verb order)
- *Perguntou onde **mora ele**.* ← wrong (inversion in indirect question)

### Tense backshift inherits from declarative reported speech

The same backshift rules from `b1-discurso-direto-indireto` apply:

| Direct (present-time question) | Indirect (past reporting) |
|---|---|
| *"Como você está?"* | *Perguntou como eu estava.* |
| *"Onde estavas?"* | *Perguntou onde eu tinha estado.* |
| *"Vais sair amanhã?"* | *Perguntou se eu ia sair no dia seguinte.* |

### Exemplar set

- *Ele perguntou se eu queria um café.* — He asked if I wanted a coffee.
- *Ela quis saber onde eu morava.* — She wanted to know where I lived.
- *Não sei se ele vem.* — I don't know whether he's coming.
- *Pergunto-me como ela conseguiu.* — I wonder how she managed.
- *Perguntei o que ele queria.* — I asked what he wanted.
- *Diz-me quando posso ir.* — Tell me when I can go.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a yes/no-vs-content classification drill (pick *se* or wh-word). Build a non-inversion drill separately (correct word-order errors). Pair with b1-discurso-direto-indireto for the tense-backshift inheritance. -->

### Traps

- **Don't keep direct-question word order in indirect questions.** *Perguntou onde mora ele* — wrong (inverted). *Perguntou onde ele mora* — right (declarative order).
- **Don't drop *se* in yes/no questions.** *Ele perguntou eu queria ir* — wrong (no connector). *Ele perguntou se eu queria ir* — right.
- **Don't confuse the conjunction *se* with the conditional *se*.** Same word, two functions: *Pergunto-me **se** ele vem* (whether — indirect question) vs *Se ele vem, eu fico* (if — conditional). Disambiguation comes from the matrix verb (*perguntar / saber* → conjunction; without matrix verb of inquiry → conditional).
- **Por que vs por quê vs porque vs porquê.** All four exist in Portuguese, with subtle distinctions:
  - *por que* — interrogative (used in direct and indirect questions): *Por que saíste? / Perguntou por que saíste.*
  - *por quê* — sentence-final or before punctuation: *Saíste por quê?*
  - *porque* — conjunction "because": *Saí porque estava cansado.*
  - *porquê* — noun "the reason": *O porquê ainda é desconhecido.*
  EP often writes *porquê* where BP would write *por quê* — register variation.
- **Wh-word retention can mask backshift.** *Perguntou quando ele vem* (no shift) vs *Perguntou quando ele vinha* (shift). The wh-word stays the same; only the embedded verb tense shifts. Don't lose the backshift just because the question word is preserved.
- **Don't double-mark with both wh-word and *se*.** *Perguntou se onde ele mora* — wrong. Pick one connector based on question type.

---

## Unit 97 — Introduction to Subjunctive Mood

*Slug: `b1-subj-introducao` · Sequence position: 81.0 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-broad`

### Outcomes

- Understand the concept of grammatical mood
- Recognize when subjunctive is needed (triggers)
- Differentiate between facts (indicative) and wishes/doubts (subjunctive)
- Prepare for learning subjunctive conjugations in Units 82-85

### Vocabulary

- modo indicativo (indicative mood - facts)
- modo subjunctivo (subjunctive mood - wishes, doubts, hypotheticals)
- que (that - introduces subjunctive clauses)
- espero que (I hope that), quero que (I want that)
- duvido que (I doubt that), talvez (maybe)
- é importante que (it's important that)

### Grammar

- **Mood concept:** indicative vs subjunctive
- **Indicative:** states facts, certainty, reality
  - Ele **fala** português. (He speaks Portuguese - fact)
- **Subjunctive:** expresses wishes, doubts, emotions, hypotheticals, commands
  - Espero que ele **fale** português. (I hope he speaks Portuguese - wish)
- **When subjunctive is triggered:** certain verbs and expressions require it

### Drills & artifacts

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

## Unit 98 — Present Subjunctive - Regular Verbs

*Slug: `b1-subj-pres-regular` · Sequence position: 82.0 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-present`

### Outcomes

- Form present subjunctive of all regular verbs
- Use subjunctive after common triggers
- Express wishes, doubts, and emotions correctly
- Apply the "opposite vowel" rule

### Vocabulary

- que eu fale (that I speak), que você coma (that you eat)
- que nós falemos (that we speak), que eles partam (that they leave)
- espero que (I hope that), é importante que (it's important that)
- talvez (maybe), antes que (before), para que (so that)

### Grammar

- **Present subjunctive formation - Regular verbs:**
  - **-AR verbs:** Change -o to -e
    - falo → fale, fales, fale, falemos, falem
  - **-ER/-IR verbs:** Change -o to -a
    - como → coma, comas, coma, comamos, comam
    - parto → parta, partas, parta, partamos, partam

### Exemplar sentences

- Espero que você fale português. (I hope you speak Portuguese.)
- É bom que nós estudemos juntos. (It's good that we study together.)
- Talvez ela coma aqui. (Maybe she'll eat here.)
- Quero que eles venham. (I want them to come.) [vir is irregular - Unit 83]
- É importante que você descanse. (It's important that you rest.)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link drills, worksheets, lessons in Phase 3 -->

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

## Unit 99 — Present Subjunctive - Irregular Verbs

*Slug: `b1-subj-pres-irregular` · Sequence position: 83.0 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-present`

### Outcomes

- Use present subjunctive of all major irregular verbs
- Express complex wishes and doubts with common verbs
- Handle ser/estar/ter/ir in subjunctive contexts
- Combine with triggers from Unit 81-82

### Vocabulary

- que eu seja (that I be), que você esteja (that you be - location)
- que ele tenha (that he has), que nós vamos (that we go)
- que eles deem (that they give), que eu saiba (that I know)
- que você possa (that you can), que ele queira (that he wants)

### Grammar

- **Present subjunctive - Irregular verbs**
- Most common irregular verbs have unpredictable subjunctive forms
- Must memorize these key verbs

### Exemplar sentences

- Espero que você esteja bem. (I hope you are well.)
- É importante que nós sejamos honestos. (It's important that we be honest.)
- Talvez ele tenha razão. (Maybe he's right.)
- Quero que vocês vão comigo. (I want you all to go with me.)
- Duvido que ela saiba a resposta. (I doubt she knows the answer.)
- É bom que você possa vir. (It's good that you can come.)

### Drills & artifacts

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

## Unit 100 — Pôr e seus derivados (compor, propor, expor, dispor...)

*Slug: `b1-por-derivados` · Sequence position: 83.5 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `por-derivatives`, `irregular-verb-conjugation`

**Prereqs:** `a2-pret-trazer-dizer-vir-por`, `b1-subj-pres-irregular`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Conjugate any verb derived from **pôr** by inheriting the parent's irregular paradigm — present, preterite, imperfeito, futuro, condicional, subjuntivo
- Use the most frequent derivatives in context (*propor, expor, dispor, compor, supor*)
- Recognize less-frequent / formal derivatives (*depor, opor, impor, repor, transpor, pressupor*) without forcing production

### Vocabulary

The pôr family — derivatives are formed by attaching a Latinate prefix to the parent verb. All inherit pôr's full irregular paradigm.

| Verb | Meaning | Frequency / register |
|---|---|---|
| **pôr** | to put, place | foundational |
| **propor** | to propose | high — daily use |
| **expor** | to expose, present | high — daily + formal |
| **compor** | to compose | medium — music/text/figurative |
| **dispor** | to dispose, arrange; to have at one's disposal | medium |
| **supor** | to suppose | medium |
| **impor** | to impose | medium |
| **opor** | to oppose | medium — often as *opor-se* |
| **repor** | to replace, replenish | medium |
| **depor** | to depose; to give testimony (legal) | low — formal/legal |
| **transpor** | to transpose, cross over | low — formal/literary |
| **pressupor** | to presuppose | low — formal/written |
| **antepor** | to place before | rare |
| **contrapor** | to counterpose | rare |

Reflexive forms also exist: *compor-se* (to compose oneself), *dispor-se* (to be willing), *opor-se* (to oppose), *impor-se* (to impose oneself / dominate).

### Grammar

The inheritance rule is total: **every derivative conjugates exactly like pôr in every tense and mood**, with the prefix attached unchanged.

### Pôr paradigm (parent — must know cold)

| Tense | eu | tu | você/ele/ela | nós | vocês/eles/elas |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Presente | ponho | pões | põe | pomos | põem |
| Pretérito | pus | puseste | pôs | pusemos | puseram |
| Imperfeito | punha | punhas | punha | púnhamos | punham |
| Futuro | porei | porás | porá | poremos | porão |
| Condicional | poria | porias | poria | poríamos | poriam |
| Pres. subj. | ponha | ponhas | ponha | ponhamos | ponham |
| Imp. subj. | pusesse | pusesses | pusesse | puséssemos | pusessem |
| Fut. subj. | puser | puseres | puser | pusermos | puserem |
| Particípio | posto | | | | |

### Derivative inheritance — example: propor

Just attach the prefix *pro-* to every form:

| Tense | eu form | 3sg form |
|---|---|---|
| Presente | proponho | propõe |
| Pretérito | propus | propôs |
| Imperfeito | propunha | propunha |
| Futuro | proporei | proporá |
| Pres. subj. | proponha | proponha |
| Imp. subj. | propusesse | propusesse |
| Particípio | proposto | |

The same rule applies to all derivatives — *componho, expomos, dispus, supôs, impuseram, oporia, transpunha, pressuposto*.

### Exemplar sentences

- *O comitê **propôs** uma nova solução.* — The committee proposed a new solution.
- *Eles **expuseram** o problema na reunião.* — They presented the problem at the meeting.
- *A música foi **composta** em 1978.* — The song was composed in 1978.
- *Eu **disponho** de pouco tempo hoje.* — I have little time available today.
- *Ele **se opôs** à proposta.* — He opposed the proposal.
- *A polícia **deteve** o suspeito enquanto a testemunha **depunha**.* — The police detained the suspect while the witness was giving testimony. (deter from ter family + depor from pôr family)
- *Não suponha que ele virá.* — Don't suppose he'll come. (negative imperative = subjuntivo)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a propor / compor / expor conjugation drill across present + preterite. Pair with b2-pret-trazer-dizer-vir-por for the preterite anchor. -->

### Traps

- **Don't regularize the derivatives.** Students who haven't internalized pôr's irregularity often try *proponhei* or *exponhei* (using -AR endings on the eu-preterite). The correct form is *propus*, *expus* — same irregular pus/puseste/pôs paradigm as the parent.
- **Particípio is *posto*, not *ponhido* or *posto*.** Compounds: *proposto, exposto, composto, disposto, suposto, imposto, oposto, deposto, reposto*. The irregular *posto* form propagates through all derivatives.
- **3sg preterite carries the circumflex.** *Pôs* (he put) — accent distinguishes it from *pos-* prefix. Same for *propôs, compôs, expôs, dispôs, supôs, impôs, opôs, depôs, repôs, transpôs*.
- **Some derivatives are register-restricted.** *Transpor*, *pressupor*, *contrapor* are formal/literary — recognize but don't force production. *Propor* and *expor* are daily-use.
- **Pôr family vs ter family — don't cross-conjugate.** *Compor* uses pôr's pattern (*compus, compôs*). *Conter* uses ter's pattern (*contive, conteve*). Keep the families separate; the prefixes look similar but the parent verbs differ entirely.

---

## Unit 101 — Ter e seus derivados (manter, conter, obter, deter, reter, abster-se)

*Slug: `b1-ter-derivados` · Sequence position: 83.6 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `ter-derivatives`, `irregular-verb-conjugation`

**Prereqs:** `a1-ter-idade`, `a2-pret-essenciais`, `b1-subj-pres-irregular`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Conjugate any verb derived from **ter** by inheriting the parent's irregular paradigm
- Apply the **3sg / 3pl accent rule** that affects all ter-derivatives in the present indicative (acute on 3sg, circumflex on 3pl)
- Use the most frequent derivatives in context (*manter, conter, obter, deter*)

### Vocabulary

The ter family — derivatives are formed by attaching a Latinate prefix to the parent verb. All inherit ter's full irregular paradigm.

| Verb | Meaning | Frequency |
|---|---|---|
| **ter** | to have | foundational |
| **manter** | to maintain, keep | high |
| **conter** | to contain, hold | high |
| **obter** | to obtain, get | high |
| **deter** | to detain, stop, hold | medium — formal/news |
| **reter** | to retain, hold back | medium |
| **entreter** | to entertain | medium |
| **abster-se** | to abstain (always reflexive) | medium — voting/dietary contexts |
| **deter-se** | to stop oneself, pause | medium — reflexive |

### Grammar

The inheritance rule is total: every derivative conjugates exactly like ter. **The critical pattern to memorize is the 3sg/3pl accent shift in the present indicative**, which appears in every derivative and is the highest-error point.

### Ter paradigm (parent — must know cold)

| Tense | eu | tu | você/ele/ela | nós | vocês/eles/elas |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Presente | tenho | tens | tem | temos | têm |
| Pretérito | tive | tiveste | teve | tivemos | tiveram |
| Imperfeito | tinha | tinhas | tinha | tínhamos | tinham |
| Futuro | terei | terás | terá | teremos | terão |
| Condicional | teria | terias | teria | teríamos | teriam |
| Pres. subj. | tenha | tenhas | tenha | tenhamos | tenham |
| Imp. subj. | tivesse | tivesses | tivesse | tivéssemos | tivessem |
| Particípio | tido | | | | |

### Derivative inheritance — example: manter

Just attach the prefix *man-* to every form, with **accent shift in 3sg/3pl present**:

| Tense | eu form | 3sg form | 3pl form |
|---|---|---|---|
| Presente | mantenho | **mantém** | **mantêm** |
| Pretérito | mantive | manteve | mantiveram |
| Imperfeito | mantinha | mantinha | mantinham |
| Futuro | manterei | manterá | manterão |
| Pres. subj. | mantenha | mantenha | mantenham |
| Imp. subj. | mantivesse | mantivesse | mantivessem |
| Particípio | mantido | | |

### The 3sg / 3pl accent shift in present

When ter takes a prefix, the stress of the 3sg form shifts to the prefixed-final syllable, and an **acute accent** marks it. The 3pl form takes a **circumflex accent**:

| Verb | 3sg present (acute) | 3pl present (circumflex) |
|---|---|---|
| ter | tem (no accent — monosyllabic) | têm (circumflex) |
| conter | **contém** | **contêm** |
| manter | **mantém** | **mantêm** |
| obter | **obtém** | **obtêm** |
| reter | **retém** | **retêm** |
| deter | **detém** | **detêm** |
| entreter | **entretém** | **entretêm** |

This accent pattern is the **single highest-error point** for ter-derivatives.

### Exemplar sentences

- *A caixa **contém** vinte livros.* — The box contains twenty books.
- *Os museus **contêm** muitas obras raras.* — The museums contain many rare works.
- *Eles **mantiveram** a casa limpa durante a viagem.* — They kept the house clean during the trip.
- *Nós **obtivemos** os resultados ontem.* — We got the results yesterday.
- *A polícia **deteve** o suspeito.* — The police detained the suspect.
- *Por favor, **retenha** os documentos até segunda-feira.* — Please hold the documents until Monday.
- *Ele **se absteve** de votar.* — He abstained from voting.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a 3sg/3pl present accent drill — high-error pattern that benefits from focused practice. -->

### Traps

- **Forgetting the 3sg acute / 3pl circumflex accent in present is THE big mistake.** *Contem*, *mantem*, *obtem* without the accent are wrong; the acute on 3sg and circumflex on 3pl are mandatory. Worksheets and drills must check this explicitly.
- **Don't regularize the eu-preterite.** *Mantive* (not *manteu*), *contive* (not *contei*), *obtive* (not *obtei*). Same tive/tiveste/teve paradigm as the parent.
- **Abster-se is always reflexive.** No non-reflexive *abster*. *Eu me abstenho de votar* (BP) / *Eu abstenho-me de votar* (EP). The se-pronoun is mandatory.
- **Deter has two meanings.** *Deter* = to detain (police context, *a polícia deteve*); *deter-se* (reflexive) = to stop oneself, pause. Different syntax.
- **Compound ter (auxiliary in compound tenses)** is the parent ter, not a derivative: *Tenho falado, tinha visto, terei feito*. Don't confuse compound auxiliary use with ter-derivative use.
- **Particípio is *tido*, not *tenido*.** Compounds: *mantido, contido, obtido, detido, retido, entretido, abstido*.

---

## Unit 102 — Vir e seus derivados (intervir, convir, provir, advir, sobrevir)

*Slug: `b1-vir-derivados` · Sequence position: 83.7 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `vir-derivatives`, `irregular-verb-conjugation`

**Prereqs:** `a2-pret-trazer-dizer-vir-por`, `a2-imp-irregular`, `b1-subj-pres-irregular`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Conjugate any verb derived from **vir** by inheriting the parent's irregular paradigm
- Apply the **3sg / 3pl accent rule** that affects vir-derivatives in the present indicative (acute on 3sg, circumflex on 3pl) — same pattern as ter-derivatives
- Use *intervir* and *convir* (the two productively used derivatives) in context
- Recognize *advir, provir, sobrevir* (formal/literary) without forcing production

### Vocabulary

The vir family is the smallest of the three derivative families. Most members are formal or restricted-context.

| Verb | Meaning | Frequency / register |
|---|---|---|
| **vir** | to come | foundational |
| **intervir** | to intervene | medium — daily + news |
| **convir** | to be appropriate, suit, be fitting | medium — mostly impersonal *convém que* |
| **provir** | to come from, originate from | low — formal/written |
| **advir** | to come from, derive, ensue | low — formal/literary |
| **sobrevir** | to come over, befall, occur unexpectedly | low — literary |

### Grammar

The inheritance rule is total: every derivative conjugates exactly like vir, with **the same 3sg-acute / 3pl-circumflex pattern** seen in the ter family.

### Vir paradigm (parent — must know cold)

| Tense | eu | tu | você/ele/ela | nós | vocês/eles/elas |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Presente | venho | vens | vem | vimos | vêm |
| Pretérito | vim | vieste | veio | viemos | vieram |
| Imperfeito | vinha | vinhas | vinha | vínhamos | vinham |
| Futuro | virei | virás | virá | viremos | virão |
| Condicional | viria | virias | viria | viríamos | viriam |
| Pres. subj. | venha | venhas | venha | venhamos | venham |
| Imp. subj. | viesse | viesses | viesse | viéssemos | viessem |
| Particípio | vindo | | | | |

### The 3sg / 3pl accent shift in present

When vir takes a prefix, the same accent rule from the ter family applies:

| Verb | 3sg present (acute) | 3pl present (circumflex) |
|---|---|---|
| vir | vem (no accent — monosyllabic) | vêm (circumflex) |
| convir | **convém** | **convêm** |
| intervir | **intervém** | **intervêm** |
| provir | **provém** | **provêm** |
| advir | **advém** | **advêm** |
| sobrevir | **sobrevém** | **sobrevêm** |

### Derivative inheritance — example: intervir

| Tense | eu form | 3sg form |
|---|---|---|
| Presente | intervenho | **intervém** |
| Pretérito | intervim | interveio |
| Imperfeito | intervinha | intervinha |
| Futuro | intervirei | intervirá |
| Pres. subj. | intervenha | intervenha |
| Particípio | intervindo | |

### Convir is mostly impersonal

The most common form of convir in modern Portuguese is the impersonal *convém que* + subjuntivo:

- *Convém que tu **venhas** cedo.* — It's advisable for you to come early.
- *Não convém que ele **saiba** disso.* — He shouldn't know about this.
- *Convém-lhe ficar em casa.* — It suits him to stay home. (clitic + impersonal)

Other personal forms (*convenho, convéns, convimos*) are rare in conversation.

### Exemplar sentences

- *O jornalista **interveio** na discussão.* — The journalist intervened in the discussion.
- *O dinheiro **provém** do governo.* — The money comes from the government.
- *Esse problema **adveio** de um mal-entendido.* — This problem arose from a misunderstanding. (formal)
- *Sobreveio uma tempestade durante a viagem.* — A storm came over during the trip. (literary)
- *Convém que vocês **cheguem** cedo.* — It's advisable that you arrive early.
- *O presidente **interveio** para resolver o impasse.* — The president intervened to resolve the deadlock.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: drill the 3sg/3pl accent pattern paired with ter-derivatives — same rule, two families, high-error overlap. -->

### Traps

- **Forgetting the 3sg acute / 3pl circumflex accent.** *Convem, intervem, provem* without the accent are wrong. Same rule as ter family — drill them together.
- **Convir is mostly used impersonally in modern Portuguese.** Don't drill the full personal paradigm as primary content; the impersonal *convém que* + subjuntivo is the productive form.
- **Sobrevir, advir are formal/literary.** Recognize when reading; don't force into production. *Sobreveio* in a casual conversation sounds bookish.
- **Particípio is *vindo*, not *vido*.** Compounds: *intervindo, convindo, provindo, advindo, sobrevindo*. Note that *vindo* doubles as both particípio of vir AND gerúndio of vir — context disambiguates.
- **Don't confuse with vir-itself in compound tenses.** *Tenho vindo* (I've been coming) uses ter as auxiliary + vir's particípio (*vindo*). Vir-derivatives in compound tenses use the same pattern: *Tenho intervindo, tinha convindo*.
- **Vir family vs ver family.** Both look similar: *vir* (to come) vs *ver* (to see). Conjugations diverge entirely (vens vs vês, vim vs vi, vinha vs via, venha vs veja). The vir family takes derivatives; the ver family doesn't form a parallel derivative system.

---

## Unit 103 — Imperfect Subjunctive

*Slug: `b1-subj-imperfeito` · Sequence position: 84.0 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-imperfect`

### Outcomes

- Express hypothetical situations in past or present
- Use "se" (if) clauses correctly
- Make polite suggestions
- Express wishes about impossible or contrary-to-fact situations

### Vocabulary

- se eu fosse (if I were), se você tivesse (if you had)
- se ele pudesse (if he could), se nós soubéssemos (if we knew)
- seria (would be), faria (would do)
- eu gostaria que (I would like that), eu quisera (I wished)

### Grammar

- **Imperfect subjunctive formation:**
  - Take preterite 3rd person plural: eles falaram
  - Remove -ram: fala-
  - Add -sse endings: -sse, -sses, -sse, -ssemos, -ssem

### Exemplar sentences

- Se eu fosse você, eu aceitaria. (If I were you, I would accept.)
- Se ele soubesse a verdade, ele entenderia. (If he knew the truth, he would understand.)
- Eu queria que você viesse à festa. (I wanted you to come to the party.)
- Se nós tivéssemos tempo, nós viajaríamos. (If we had time, we would travel.)
- Era importante que eles estudassem. (It was important that they studied.)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link drills, worksheets, lessons in Phase 3 -->

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->
