## Unit 104 — Subjuntivo após verbos de desejo e vontade

*Slug: `b1-subj-trigger-desejo` · Sequence position: 84.1 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-triggers`, `subjunctive-present`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-pres-regular`, `b1-subj-pres-irregular`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Recognize the verbs of desire/wish/volition that trigger subjuntivo presente in a subordinate `que`-clause
- Distinguish *eu quero ir* (same subject → infinitive) from *eu quero que você vá* (different subjects → subjuntivo)
- Form polite requests and indirect commands using *pedir que*, *exigir que*

### Vocabulary

Trigger verbs (ranked roughly by frequency):

- **querer que** — to want (someone) to
- **esperar que** — to hope that / expect that
- **desejar que** — to wish that (more formal than *querer*)
- **preferir que** — to prefer that
- **pedir que** — to ask that (indirect request)
- **exigir que** — to demand that
- **insistir (em) que** — to insist that
- **proibir que** — to forbid

### Grammar

Pattern: **[verb of desire] + que + sujeito + verbo no subjuntivo**.

The subjunctive is triggered because the speaker is projecting a desired state, not asserting a fact. The clause introduces what the speaker *wants*, not what *is*.

### Same-subject vs different-subject

When the subject of the desire and the desired action is the same, use the infinitive — no `que`, no subjunctive:

- *Eu quero **ir** ao cinema.* — I want to go to the movies.
- *Eu quero que você **vá** ao cinema.* — I want you to go to the movies.

### Exemplar sentences

- *Quero que você **venha** à festa.* — I want you to come to the party.
- *Espero que tudo **dê** certo.* — I hope everything works out.
- *Prefiro que ele **fique** em casa hoje.* — I'd rather he stay home today.
- *Peço que você me **ajude** com isso.* — I'm asking you to help me with this.
- *O chefe exigiu que entregássemos o relatório hoje.* — The boss demanded we hand in the report today. (imperfeito subj because triggering verb is past)
- *Insisto em que você **prove** o brigadeiro.* — I insist you try the brigadeiro.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link existing subjuntivo presente drills; pair with the polite-request reading covered in b1-querer-aspect-bp. -->

### Traps

- **Same-subject check.** *Eu quero que eu vá* is a beginner overgeneralization — same subject takes the infinitive: *eu quero ir*.
- **BP indicative drift.** In casual BP speech, indicative sometimes appears where the prescriptive rule wants subjuntivo: *quero que você vem* is heard but considered substandard. Teach subjuntivo as the target form; recognize the indicative form when the student hears it in the wild.
- *Pedir que* takes subjuntivo, not infinitive: *peço que você venha*, not *peço você vir*.

---

## Unit 105 — Subjuntivo após verbos de emoção

*Slug: `b1-subj-trigger-emocao` · Sequence position: 84.2 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-triggers`, `subjunctive-present`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-pres-regular`, `b1-subj-pres-irregular`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Recognize emotion verbs and adjectival expressions of emotion that trigger subjuntivo presente
- Express positive and negative reactions to a situation or another person's actions
- Distinguish *fico feliz porque você veio* (factual cause → indicative) from *fico feliz que você venha* (emotional reaction → subjuntivo)

### Vocabulary

Trigger expressions:

- **gostar que** — to be glad / like that
- **lamentar que** — to regret / be sorry that
- **sentir que** — to be sorry that / regret
- **ter medo (de) que** — to be afraid that
- **temer que** — to fear that (more formal)
- **ficar feliz/triste/contente que** — to be glad/sad/happy that
- **alegrar-se que** — to rejoice that
- **estranhar que** — to find it strange that
- **surpreender-se que** — to be surprised that

### Grammar

Pattern: **[expression of emotion] + que + sujeito + verbo no subjuntivo**.

The subjunctive is triggered because the speaker is reacting emotionally to a state of affairs, not just asserting it as fact. The `que`-clause carries the trigger, not standalone reactions.

### Exemplar sentences

- *Gosto que você **venha** sempre aos domingos.* — I like that you always come on Sundays.
- *Lamento que ela não **possa** estar conosco.* — I'm sorry she can't be with us.
- *Tenho medo que ele **se machuque** na bicicleta.* — I'm afraid he'll hurt himself on the bike.
- *Fico feliz que vocês **estejam** aqui.* — I'm happy you're here.
- *É uma pena que o restaurante **feche** cedo.* — It's a pity the restaurant closes early.
- *Estranho que ele ainda não **tenha** chegado.* — I find it strange he hasn't arrived yet.

### Causal vs emotional contrast

When the emotion is followed by a *cause* (with *porque*), the verb is indicative — that's an assertion, not a reaction:

- *Fico feliz **que você venha**.* — I'm happy you're coming. (reaction → subjuntivo)
- *Fico feliz **porque você veio**.* — I'm happy because you came. (assertion of cause → indicative)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link existing subjuntivo presente drills. -->

### Traps

- **BP indicative drift is strongest with emotion verbs.** Native BP speech often uses indicative — *fico feliz que você está aqui* is widely heard. Teach subjuntivo as the target; recognize indicative as common in spontaneous speech.
- *Ter medo que* and *ter medo de que* both occur. The *de* is grammatically preferred but optional in practice. Don't penalize either.
- *Sentir que* in the emotion sense (= "be sorry") triggers subjuntivo. *Sentir que* in the perception sense (= "feel that, sense that") triggers indicative: *sinto que você está cansado* — same form, different reading.

---

## Unit 106 — Subjuntivo após expressões impessoais

*Slug: `b1-subj-trigger-impessoal` · Sequence position: 84.3 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-triggers`, `subjunctive-present`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-pres-regular`, `b1-subj-pres-irregular`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Use impersonal expressions of necessity, possibility, advice, and judgment with subjuntivo presente
- Distinguish impersonals that take subjuntivo (necessity, possibility, judgment) from those that take indicative (assertion of fact)
- Construct generalized claims and recommendations without naming a subject

### Vocabulary

Triggers subjuntivo (uncertainty, necessity, judgment):

- **é importante que** — it's important that
- **é necessário / é preciso que** — it's necessary that
- **é bom que** — it's good that
- **é melhor que** — it's better that
- **é possível que** — it's possible that
- **é provável que** — it's likely that
- **é pena que** — it's a pity that
- **convém que** — it's advisable that
- **basta que** — it's enough that
- **pode ser que** — it might be that

Triggers indicative (assertion of fact — *do not* take subjuntivo):

- **é certo que** — it's certain that
- **é evidente que** — it's evident that
- **é claro que** — it's clear that
- **é óbvio que** — it's obvious that
- **é verdade que** — it's true that

### Grammar

Pattern: **é + adjetivo / substantivo + que + sujeito + verbo no subjuntivo**.

The subjunctive is triggered when the impersonal expression introduces a *judgment, necessity, possibility, or evaluation* — not when it asserts a fact. The form `é certo que ele vem` (assertion) takes indicative; `é possível que ele venha` (possibility) takes subjuntivo.

### Exemplar sentences

- *É importante que você **estude** todos os dias.* — It's important you study every day.
- *É preciso que ele **venha** logo.* — He needs to come soon.
- *É melhor que nós **fiquemos** em casa.* — It's better if we stay home.
- *É possível que **chova** amanhã.* — It might rain tomorrow.
- *É pena que ela não **possa** vir.* — It's a pity she can't come.
- *Pode ser que **dê** certo.* — It might work out.
- *Basta que vocês **avisem** com antecedência.* — All you need to do is let us know in advance.

### Indicative contrast

- *É possível que ele **esteja** cansado.* — He might be tired. (subjuntivo: possibility)
- *É evidente que ele **está** cansado.* — He's clearly tired. (indicative: assertion)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link existing subjuntivo drills; pair with conditional system in Cluster 3. -->

### Traps

- **Watch the truth-claiming impersonals.** *É verdade que*, *é certo que*, *é evidente que* trigger indicative because they assert. Default-applying subjuntivo to every "é + adj + que" frame is wrong.
- **Negation flips the indicative ones.** *É verdade que ele vem* (indicative). *Não é verdade que ele venha* (subjuntivo, because negated assertion).
- **BP indicative drift.** Casual BP often says *é importante que você estuda* instead of *estude*. Teach subjuntivo as the target.
- *Pode ser que* always takes subjuntivo: *pode ser que sim*, *pode ser que dê certo*.

---

## Unit 107 — Subjuntivo após verbos e expressões de dúvida

*Slug: `b1-subj-trigger-duvida` · Sequence position: 84.4 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-triggers`, `subjunctive-present`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-pres-regular`, `b1-subj-pres-irregular`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Use verbs of doubt and uncertainty (*duvidar, não acreditar, não pensar*) with subjuntivo presente
- Apply the **negation flip**: *acho que* (indicative, asserts a belief) → *não acho que* (subjuntivo, asserts the absence of belief)
- Use *talvez*, *é possível que*, *é provável que* and similar uncertainty markers correctly

### Vocabulary

Trigger expressions:

- **duvidar que** — to doubt that
- **não acreditar que** — to not believe that
- **não pensar / não achar que** — to not think that (negation flips trigger)
- **negar que** — to deny that
- **talvez** — maybe (no `que`)
- **é possível que** — it's possible that
- **é provável que** — it's likely that
- **pode ser que** — it might be that

### Grammar

Pattern: **[doubt expression] + (que) + sujeito + verbo no subjuntivo**.

The subjunctive marks that the speaker is *not committed* to the truth of the proposition. With *talvez*, no `que` appears — the subjunctive sits directly after the adverb.

### The negation flip

*Achar que* and *pensar que* are the most subtle case. In the affirmative, they assert a belief, so they take indicative. Negating them removes the assertion — the speaker is now denying belief, so subjuntivo:

- *Acho que ele **vem** amanhã.* — I think he's coming tomorrow. (assertion → indicative)
- *Não acho que ele **venha** amanhã.* — I don't think he's coming tomorrow. (denied assertion → subjuntivo)

The same flip applies to *acreditar que*, *crer que*, *parecer que* in the literal-perception sense.

### Exemplar sentences

- *Duvido que ele **chegue** a tempo.* — I doubt he'll arrive on time.
- *Não acredito que isso **seja** verdade.* — I don't believe that's true.
- *Talvez **chova** amanhã.* — Maybe it'll rain tomorrow.
- *É provável que ele **esteja** dormindo.* — He's probably sleeping.
- *Pode ser que **dê** tudo certo.* — Everything might work out.
- *O réu negou que **tivesse** participado.* — The defendant denied having taken part. (imperfeito subj because triggering verb is past)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link existing subjuntivo drills. The negation-flip is high-leverage and may warrant a dedicated drill. -->

### Traps

- **The negation flip is the single highest-frequency error.** Many students learn *acho que ele vem* (correct, indicative) and then say *não acho que ele vem* — wrong; it should be *não acho que ele venha*. Drill this contrast explicitly.
- *Talvez* takes subjuntivo when it precedes the verb. After the verb, indicative is fine: *Ele vem talvez amanhã* (indicative, *talvez* is just a side adverb).
- **BP indicative drift.** Casual BP sometimes uses indicative after *talvez*: *talvez ele vem*. Teach subjuntivo as the target.
- *Duvidar que* always takes subjuntivo, even when negated. *Não duvido que ele venha* — still subjuntivo, because the lexical content is "doubt." (Some grammars accept indicative for *não duvido*, but subjuntivo is safer.)

---

## Unit 108 — Subjuntivo após conjunções subordinativas

*Slug: `b1-subj-trigger-conjuncoes` · Sequence position: 84.5 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-triggers`, `subjunctive-present`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-pres-regular`, `b1-subj-pres-irregular`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Recognize the conjunctions that always take subjuntivo, regardless of the main clause
- Use these to construct purpose clauses (*para que*), concessive clauses (*embora*), conditional clauses (*a menos que*, *contanto que*), and time clauses (*antes que*, *até que*)
- Distinguish always-subjuntivo conjunctions from conjunctions that take indicative or both

### Vocabulary

Conjunctions that **always** take subjuntivo:

- **para que** — so that, in order that
- **a fim de que** — so that (more formal)
- **antes que** — before (in time)
- **sem que** — without (someone doing something)
- **embora** — although, even though
- **ainda que** — even if
- **mesmo que** — even if
- **a menos que** — unless
- **a não ser que** — unless
- **contanto que** — provided that
- **caso** — in case (alternative to *se* + subj)
- **por mais que** — no matter how much

### Grammar

Pattern: **[conjunction] + sujeito + verbo no subjuntivo**.

These conjunctions trigger subjuntivo categorically — there is no contrast with indicative. The subjuntivo expresses the projected, hypothetical, or contrary-to-fact nature of the subordinate clause.

### Exemplar sentences

- *Vou estudar **para que eu passe** no exame.* — I'll study so I pass the exam.
- *Saiu **antes que pudéssemos** despedir-nos.* — He left before we could say goodbye. (imperfeito subj because main is preterite)
- *Ela ajudou **sem que eu pedisse**.* — She helped without my asking.
- *Embora **chova**, vou sair.* — Even though it's raining, I'm going out.
- *Mesmo que ele **venha**, não vou ficar.* — Even if he comes, I won't stay.
- *A menos que você **mude** de ideia, fica decidido.* — Unless you change your mind, it's decided.
- *Contanto que vocês **avisem**, podemos remarcar.* — Provided you let us know, we can reschedule.
- *Caso **chova**, levo guarda-chuva.* — In case it rains, I'll take an umbrella.

### Tense agreement

When the main clause is in the past, the subordinate uses imperfeito subjuntivo:

- *Eu estudei **para que passasse** no exame.* — I studied so I would pass the exam.
- *Ela ajudou **sem que eu pedisse**.* — She helped without my asking.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: drill the conjunction list directly; this is high-volume vocabulary recognition. -->

### Traps

- **Para que vs para + infinitivo.** Same subject across both clauses → infinitive (*estudei **para passar** no exame*). Different subjects → *para que* + subjuntivo (*ele estudou **para que eu passasse**, dando o exemplo*). The infinitive form is far more common in BP for same-subject cases.
- **Embora ≠ porque.** *Embora chova* (subjuntivo, even though). *Porque chove* (indicative, because). Easy to confuse the structures.
- *Antes que* triggers subjuntivo; *depois que* triggers indicative (factual sequence): *antes que ele chegue, vou sair* vs *depois que ele chegou, saí*.
- **BP register.** Several of these conjunctions (*a fim de que*, *ainda que*) sound formal/written. Spoken BP often substitutes *para*, *mesmo se*, etc. Teach the full set; flag register.

---

## Unit 109 — Subjuntivo em construções hipotéticas (se + imperfeito subjuntivo)

*Slug: `b1-subj-trigger-hipotetico` · Sequence position: 84.6 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-triggers`, `subjunctive-imperfect`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-pres-regular`, `b1-subj-pres-irregular`, `b1-subj-imperfeito`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Form hypothetical conditions of the *Type 2* shape: **se + imperfeito subjuntivo + condicional**
- Distinguish hypothetical *se* (imagined situation → subjuntivo) from real-conditional *se* (factual → indicative or futuro do subjuntivo)
- Use this construction to express imagined preferences, plans, and unrealized situations

### Vocabulary

Trigger: **se** + imperfeito subjuntivo, paired with the conditional in the main clause.

Common imperfeito subjuntivo forms (review from `b1-subj-imperfeito`):

- ser → fosse, fosses, fosse, fôssemos, fossem
- ter → tivesse
- estar → estivesse
- fazer → fizesse
- poder → pudesse
- saber → soubesse

### Grammar

Pattern: **se + imperfeito subjuntivo, [main clause em condicional]**.

The hypothetical is unreal or contrary-to-fact at the moment of speaking. *Se eu fosse rico* doesn't claim wealth — it imagines an alternative state.

### Exemplar sentences

- *Se eu **fosse** rico, **viajaria** pelo mundo.* — If I were rich, I'd travel the world.
- *Se ela **soubesse** a verdade, **me contaria**.* — If she knew the truth, she'd tell me.
- *Se **chovesse** amanhã, eu **ficaria** em casa.* — If it rained tomorrow, I'd stay home.
- *Se você **estivesse** aqui, **veria** com seus próprios olhos.* — If you were here, you'd see with your own eyes.
- *O que você **faria** se **ganhasse** na loteria?* — What would you do if you won the lottery?

### Real conditional contrast

When the *se*-clause describes a real or future-likely event, **not** a hypothetical, BP uses **futuro do subjuntivo** (covered in `b2-subj-futuro`) — not imperfeito subjuntivo:

- *Se **chover** amanhã, fico em casa.* — If it rains tomorrow, I'll stay home. (real future condition: futuro do subjuntivo)
- *Se **chovesse** amanhã, ficaria em casa.* — If it rained tomorrow, I'd stay home. (hypothetical: imperfeito subjuntivo)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: this unit overlaps strongly with the conditional system (Cluster 3, b2-cond-irreal-bp). Coordinate the drill set so they share examples without duplicating. -->

### Traps

- **Don't use indicative after hypothetical *se*.** *Se eu **era** rico, viajaria* is wrong. Hypothetical = subjuntivo always.
- **The two conditional types collapse for English speakers.** English "if I were rich" and "if it rains" both use "if" + present, leaving the modality to the main clause. Portuguese splits them: hypothetical → imperfeito subj, real → futuro do subj. Drill both side-by-side.
- **EP polite-request overlap.** EP often uses imperfeito subjuntivo where BP uses imperfeito (*se pudesses, vinhas comigo* in EP vs *se você pudesse, vinha comigo* in BP). Phase 5 EP twin will revisit.
- **The main-clause verb defaults to condicional**, not future. *Se eu fosse rico, vou viajar* is wrong; the hypothetical chains to *viajaria*.

---

## Unit 110 — Subjuntivo em orações relativas com antecedente indefinido ou inexistente

*Slug: `b1-subj-trigger-relativo` · Sequence position: 84.7 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-triggers`, `subjunctive-present`, `relative-pronouns`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-pres-regular`, `b1-subj-pres-irregular`, `b1-relativo-que`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Distinguish definite-antecedent relative clauses (indicative) from indefinite or non-existent antecedent clauses (subjuntivo)
- Use *procuro alguém que…*, *quero comprar algo que…*, *não há nada que…* with the correct mood
- Recognize that the subjuntivo here marks the antecedent's hypothetical or non-existent status, not a triggering verb

### Vocabulary

Common antecedents that push toward subjuntivo:

- **alguém que** — someone who (indefinite)
- **alguma coisa / algo que** — something that (indefinite)
- **nada que** — nothing that (non-existent)
- **ninguém que** — nobody who (non-existent)
- **um/uma + noun + que** — a/an [noun] that (when not specific)
- **qualquer + noun + que** — any [noun] that
- **o/a + noun + que** + superlative — the [noun] that... (sometimes)

### Grammar

Pattern: **[antecedente] + que + verbo no subjuntivo** when the antecedent is hypothetical, indefinite, or non-existent.

The same relative pronoun (*que*) takes indicative when the antecedent is real and specific. The mood signals existence / specificity:

- *Procuro alguém que **fale** francês.* — I'm looking for someone who speaks French. (indefinite — anyone qualifying)
- *Conheço alguém que **fala** francês.* — I know someone who speaks French. (definite — a specific person)

### Exemplar sentences

- *Procuro alguém que **possa** me ajudar.* — I'm looking for someone who can help me. (any qualifying person)
- *Quero comprar um carro que **seja** barato e econômico.* — I want to buy a car that's cheap and fuel-efficient. (any car meeting criteria)
- *Não há nada que **sirva** para isso.* — There's nothing that fits for this. (non-existent referent)
- *Não conheço ninguém que **saiba** consertar isso.* — I don't know anyone who knows how to fix this. (non-existent within speaker's circle)
- *Preciso de alguém que **fale** português fluentemente.* — I need someone who speaks Portuguese fluently.
- *Diga-me qualquer coisa que **funcione**.* — Tell me anything that works.

### Specific vs non-specific contrast

- *Comprei um carro que **é** barato.* — I bought a car that's cheap. (specific car, exists, indicative)
- *Quero comprar um carro que **seja** barato.* — I want to buy a car that's cheap. (no specific car yet, hypothetical, subjuntivo)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: cross-link with the relative-pronoun cluster (b1-relativo-que, b1-relativo-quem, b1-relativo-cujo, b1-relativo-formal-locativo). The mood-distinction drill belongs here; the pronoun-form drills belong in those units. -->

### Traps

- **Don't apply subjuntivo to definite-antecedent clauses.** *O homem que **mora** ao lado é simpático* — indicative, because the man is real and specific. *Subjuntivo* is wrong here.
- **Negation often forces subjuntivo.** *Não há ninguém que entenda* (subjuntivo, because no one is being asserted to exist). *Há alguém que entende* (could be either, depending on whether the speaker means a specific person).
- **Procurar + alguém que** — almost always subjuntivo, because *procurar* implies the person isn't yet identified. *Encontrei alguém que entende* — indicative, because the person is now identified.
- **Relative-pronoun foundation.** This unit assumes the student knows the basic relative-pronoun system: `b1-relativo-que` (default), `b1-relativo-quem` ([+human] post-preposition), `b1-relativo-cujo` (possessive), `b1-relativo-formal-locativo` (*o qual* / *onde*). The mood-distinction taught here builds on those forms.

---

## Unit 111 — Condicional Tipo 1 — Real / provável (se + indicativo)

*Slug: `b1-cond-real-bp` · Sequence position: 84.8 · CEFR: B1 · Variant: bp*

**Concepts:** `conditional-sentences`

**Prereqs:** `b1-condicional-bp`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Construct **Type 1 (real / likely)** conditional sentences in BP using the indicative pair: `se + presente indicativo + presente / futuro indicativo`
- Distinguish habitual conditionals (general truths) from specific-future real conditionals
- Recognize that Type 1 does NOT use subjuntivo — that's Type 2 (irreal) and Type 3 (counterfactual past)

### Vocabulary

- **se** — if
- Common temporal anchors: *agora, sempre, normalmente, todo dia, amanhã, na próxima semana*

### Grammar

Type 1 covers conditions the speaker treats as **real, likely, or habitual** — the situation may or may not happen, but isn't being imagined as contrary to fact.

Two main BP patterns:

### Pattern 1a — Habitual / general

`se + presente indicativo + presente indicativo`

- *Se chove, eu fico em casa.* — If it rains, I stay home. (general / habitual)
- *Se ele liga, eu atendo.* — If he calls, I answer.
- *Se você estuda, você passa.* — If you study, you pass. (timeless truth)

### Pattern 1b — Specific future (real)

`se + futuro do subjuntivo + presente / futuro indicativo`

In BP, the *se*-clause for specific future events takes **futuro do subjuntivo** (covered in `b2-subj-futuro` — for regular verbs the form is identical to the infinitive, which is why this often *looks* like indicative):

- *Se chover amanhã, vou ficar em casa.* — If it rains tomorrow, I'll stay home.
- *Se ele ligar, eu atendo.* — If he calls, I'll answer.
- *Se você estudar, você passa no exame.* — If you study, you'll pass the exam.

The main clause uses presente indicativo (informal future) or futuro indicativo (more formal).

### Exemplar set

- *Se eu tenho tempo, eu cozinho.* — If I have time, I cook. (habitual)
- *Se eu tiver tempo amanhã, eu cozinho.* — If I have time tomorrow, I'll cook. (specific future — `tiver` is futuro do subj of *ter*)
- *Se chove, fico em casa.* — If it rains, I stay home. (general)
- *Se chover, fico em casa.* — If it rains, I'll stay home. (this specific occasion)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link existing presente-indicativo drills; pair with b2-subj-futuro for the Pattern 1b version. Cross-link b1-subj-trigger-hipotetico (which contrasts with this unit on the Type 2 side). -->

### Traps

- **Don't use subjuntivo presente in Type 1.** *Se ele venha, eu ajudo* — wrong (subjuntivo presente). Type 1 takes indicative or futuro do subjuntivo. The hypothetical/wish reading would be Type 2: *Se ele viesse, eu ajudaria*.
- **Pattern 1a vs 1b is a tense-of-the-se-clause distinction.** Habitual takes presente indicativo; specific-future takes futuro do subjuntivo. The forms can look identical for regular verbs (chover → chove vs chover → chover) but differ for irregulars (ter → tem vs ter → tiver).
- **EP overlap question.** EP also uses futuro do subjuntivo for specific-future Type 1, so Pattern 1b is largely shared. Pattern 1a differs less between variants. The EP twin (Cluster 5+) will refine.
- **Type 1 is NOT the place for "se eu fosse rico".** That's Type 2 (irreal). Type 1 is "se eu sou / se eu for", indicative-only.

---

## Unit 112 — Future Subjunctive

*Slug: `b2-subj-futuro` · Sequence position: 85.0 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-future`

### Outcomes

- Use future subjunctive after quando, se, and time conjunctions
- Express future conditions and possibilities correctly
- Understand this unique Portuguese grammar feature
- Distinguish between future possibilities (future subj.) and hypotheticals (imperf. subj.)

### Vocabulary

- quando eu falar (when I speak), se você tiver (if you have)
- quando ele vier (when he comes), se nós formos (if we go)
- assim que (as soon as), logo que (as soon as)
- enquanto (while), caso (in case)

### Grammar

- **Future subjunctive formation:**
  - Take preterite 3rd person plural: eles falaram
  - Remove -ram: fala-
  - Add -r endings: -r, -res, -r, -rmos, -rem

### Exemplar sentences

- Quando eu for ao Brasil, vou visitar você. (When I go to Brazil, I'll visit you.)
- Se você tiver dúvidas, me pergunte. (If you have doubts, ask me.)
- Assim que eu chegar em casa, vou ligar. (As soon as I arrive home, I'll call.)
- Enquanto você estiver aqui, aproveite. (While you're here, enjoy.)
- Quando nós formos, te avisamos. (When we go, we'll let you know.)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: link drills, worksheets, lessons in Phase 3 -->

### Traps

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

---

## Unit 113 — Mais-que-perfeito do subjuntivo (tivesse falado)

*Slug: `b2-mais-que-perfeito-subj` · Sequence position: 85.1 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `compound-tenses`, `subjunctive-imperfect`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-imperfeito`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Form the mais-que-perfeito do subjuntivo (tivesse/tivesses/tivesse/tivéssemos/tivessem + particípio)
- Use it as the *se*-clause in counterfactual past conditionals (Type 3 — see `b2-cond-contra-bp`)
- Use it after subjuntivo triggers in past time (e.g., *queria que ele tivesse vindo*)
- Use it after concessive/conditional conjunctions in past contexts (*embora tivesse, mesmo que tivesse*)

### Vocabulary

- **tivesse / tivesses / tivesse / tivéssemos / tivessem + particípio** — auxiliary + past participle
- **houvesse + particípio** — formal/literary alternative; rare in spoken use, common in written prose

### Grammar

Form: imperfeito do subjuntivo of *ter* (or *haver*) + particípio passado.

| Pessoa | Auxiliar | + particípio |
|---|---|---|
| eu | tivesse | falado |
| você / ele / ela | tivesse | falado |
| nós | tivéssemos | falado |
| vocês / eles / elas | tivessem | falado |

The form expresses a hypothetical, counterfactual, or wished-for past event. It marks the *se*-clause of Type 3 conditionals and appears under any subjuntivo trigger when the action is anchored in the past.

### Three primary uses

**1. Counterfactual past conditionals (Type 3) — see `b2-cond-contra-bp`**

- *Se eu **tivesse estudado** mais, teria passado.* — If I had studied more, I would have passed.
- *Se ela **tivesse vindo** ontem, teríamos comemorado.* — If she had come yesterday, we would have celebrated.

**2. After subjuntivo triggers in past contexts**

- *Eu queria que ele **tivesse vindo**.* — I wished he had come.
- *Era importante que vocês **tivessem chegado** a tempo.* — It was important you had arrived on time.
- *Duvidava que ele **tivesse feito** isso.* — I doubted he had done that.

**3. After concessive / conditional conjunctions in past time**

- *Embora **tivesse chovido**, saímos.* — Even though it had rained, we went out.
- *Mesmo que **tivessem avisado**, eu não teria ido.* — Even if they had warned me, I wouldn't have gone.

### Houvesse vs tivesse

Both forms are grammatical and interchangeable. *Tivesse* dominates in spoken usage and most modern writing. *Houvesse* appears in formal/literary register and legal/bureaucratic text:

- *Se eu **tivesse** sabido…* — natural in any register
- *Se eu **houvesse** sabido…* — formal, literary

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a Type 3 conditional drill that pairs this form with condicional composto. Cross-link b2-cond-contra-bp (Cluster 3) and b2-condicional-composto-bp once both are stable. -->

### Traps

- **Don't substitute mais-que-perfeito do indicativo (tinha falado) in subjuntivo contexts.** *Se eu tinha estudado, teria passado* is wrong — the *se*-clause requires subjuntivo. (EP allows *tinha* in spoken usage as a substitute, but the prescriptive form and the BP norm is *tivesse*.)
- **Don't use simple imperfeito do subjuntivo where a past anchor exists.** *Se eu estudasse, teria passado* mixes Type 2's *se*-clause with Type 3's main clause — confusing. For counterfactual past, use *tivesse estudado*; for irreal present/future, use *estudasse*.
- **Particípios irregulares.** *Tivesse dito, tivesse feito, tivesse posto, tivesse visto, tivesse aberto* — review the irregular set before drilling.
- **Reclassified to shared in Cluster 4.** This unit was originally tagged `variant: bp` as a Cluster 3 placeholder for prereq resolution. The form is identical in BP and EP, and the subjuntivo usage is symmetric, so it's now shared. Earlier prereq references (e.g., from `b2-cond-contra-bp`) updated to the new slug.

---

## Unit 114 — Condicional composto (teria falado)

*Slug: `b2-condicional-composto-bp` · Sequence position: 85.2 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: bp*

**Concepts:** `compound-tenses`, `conditional-formation`

**Prereqs:** `b1-condicional-bp`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Form the condicional composto (teria/terias/teria/teríamos/teriam + particípio) in BP
- Use it as the main-clause verb in counterfactual past conditionals (Type 3 — see `b2-cond-contra-bp`)
- Express past hypothetical consequences ("would have done") and future-in-the-past in reported speech
- Recognize that EP often substitutes mais-que-perfeito do indicativo (tinha falado) for the same meaning — a real BP/EP divergence

### Vocabulary

- **teria / terias / teria / teríamos / teriam + particípio** — auxiliary + past participle
- **haveria + particípio** — exists but essentially literary; use *teria* in BP

### Grammar

Form: condicional simples of *ter* + particípio passado.

| Pessoa | Auxiliar | + particípio |
|---|---|---|
| eu | teria | falado |
| você / ele / ela | teria | falado |
| nós | teríamos | falado |
| vocês / eles / elas | teriam | falado |

The form expresses a hypothetical past consequence — what *would have* happened *if* something had been different. It also appears in reported speech as the future-in-the-past.

### Three primary uses

**1. Main clause of Type 3 conditional — see `b2-cond-contra-bp`**

- *Se eu tivesse estudado mais, **teria passado**.* — If I had studied more, I would have passed.
- *Se ela tivesse vindo, **teríamos comemorado** juntos.* — If she had come, we would have celebrated together.

**2. Past hypothetical consequence (no explicit *se*-clause)**

- *Eu **teria ido** à festa, mas estava doente.* — I would have gone to the party, but I was sick.
- *Você **teria feito** o mesmo no meu lugar?* — Would you have done the same in my place?
- *Nós **teríamos comprado** a casa, mas o preço subiu.* — We would have bought the house, but the price went up.

**3. Future-in-the-past in reported speech**

- *Ele disse que **teria terminado** até hoje.* — He said he would have finished by today.
- *Ela prometeu que **teria respondido** logo.* — She promised she would have answered soon.

### BP/EP divergence

This is one of the sharpest BP/EP variant points covered in the curriculum:

| Variant | Form for "I would have gone" |
|---|---|
| BP | *Eu **teria ido**.* (condicional composto) |
| EP (spoken) | *Eu **tinha ido**.* (mais-que-perfeito do indicativo as substitute) |
| EP (formal) | *Eu **teria ido**.* (also acceptable) |

EP students learn this divergence in their twin unit (Cluster 5 backlog). BP students should produce *teria* exclusively and recognize the EP *tinha* substitution when listening or reading.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: pair drills with b2-mais-que-perfeito-subj for the Type 3 conditional pair (tivesse + teria). Cross-link b2-cond-contra-bp (Cluster 3). -->

### Traps

- **Don't substitute *tinha* for *teria* in BP main clauses.** *Se eu tivesse estudado, tinha passado* sounds EP-flavored to BP ears. BP keeps *teria passado*.
- **Distinguish from condicional simples (faria vs teria feito).** *Eu faria* = I would do (hypothetical present/future). *Eu teria feito* = I would have done (counterfactual past). Different time anchors.
- **Don't use it for unrealized future plans.** *Vou ter feito* (future perfect with *ir*) or *terei feito* (futuro composto, see `b2-futuro-composto-ind`) — those are forward-looking. *Teria feito* is backward-looking, counterfactual.
- **Particípios irregulares.** *Teria dito, teria feito, teria posto, teria visto* — same set as the other compounds.
- **Stays variant: bp.** The form *teria* is grammatically available in EP but practically substituted by *tinha* in spoken EP — the EP twin (Cluster 5 backlog) will document the substitution pattern.

---

## Unit 115 — Futuro composto do indicativo (terei falado) — future perfect

*Slug: `b2-futuro-composto-ind` · Sequence position: 85.3 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `compound-tenses`, `future-tense`

**Prereqs:** `b1-fut-sintetico`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Form the futuro composto do indicativo (terei/terás/terá/teremos/terão + particípio) — the **future perfect**
- Express an action that **will be completed before** another future point or action
- Recognize that this form is mostly written/formal in spoken BP, frequently replaced by *vou ter feito* in conversation

### Vocabulary

- **terei / terás / terá / teremos / terão + particípio** — auxiliary + past participle
- Common temporal anchors: *até* (by [time]), *antes de* (before), *quando* (when, anchoring future)

### Grammar

Form: futuro do indicativo of *ter* + particípio passado.

| Pessoa | Auxiliar | + particípio |
|---|---|---|
| eu | terei | falado |
| você / ele / ela | terá | falado |
| nós | teremos | falado |
| vocês / eles / elas | terão | falado |

The form expresses an action **completed before** a future reference point. The reference point may be explicit (*até o fim do ano*) or implicit (*quando você chegar*).

### Exemplar sentences

- *Até o fim do ano, eu **terei publicado** o livro.* — By the end of the year, I'll have published the book.
- *Quando você chegar, eu já **terei terminado**.* — When you arrive, I'll have already finished.
- *Em 2030, ela **terá se aposentado**.* — In 2030, she'll have retired.
- *Antes do casamento, eles **terão se mudado** para a nova casa.* — Before the wedding, they'll have moved to the new house.
- *Você **terá visto** o filme antes de eu chegar?* — Will you have seen the movie before I arrive?
- *Nós **teremos discutido** todos os pontos até o final da reunião.* — We'll have discussed all the points by the end of the meeting.

### Spoken vs written register

In spoken BP, this form is uncommon. The natural alternatives are:

| Register | Form | Example |
|---|---|---|
| Formal / written | futuro composto | *Terei terminado até sexta-feira.* |
| Spoken / informal | *vou ter* + particípio | *Vou ter terminado até sexta-feira.* |
| Spoken / informal | simple future + anchor | *Termino até sexta-feira.* |

EP usage is similar but slightly more comfortable with the synthetic form in writing.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a register-switching drill — same meaning, three forms (terei feito / vou ter feito / faço até [time]). -->

### Traps

- **Don't confuse with futuro próximo (vou fazer).** *Vou fazer* = will do (intent). *Terei feito* = will have done (completion before a future point). Different aspects entirely.
- **The form is rare in spoken BP.** Don't drill it as the default future expression — it's a register-specific form for written/formal contexts. For spoken BP, *vou ter feito* is the natural compound future.
- **Particípios irregulares apply.** *Terei dito, terei feito, terei posto* — same set as the other compound tenses.
- **Cluster 4 form unit; downstream from b2-futuro-composto-subj.** The indicative future-perfect appears in main clauses; the subjunctive future-perfect appears after temporal conjunctions (*quando, assim que, depois que*) — see `b2-futuro-composto-subj`.

---

## Unit 116 — Futuro composto do subjuntivo (tiver falado) — future perfect subjunctive

*Slug: `b2-futuro-composto-subj` · Sequence position: 85.4 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `compound-tenses`, `subjunctive-future`

**Prereqs:** `b2-subj-futuro`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Form the futuro composto do subjuntivo (tiver/tiveres/tiver/tivermos/tiverem + particípio)
- Use it after temporal and conditional conjunctions (*quando, assim que, depois que, se*) to mark **a completed action in the future**
- Distinguish it from the simple futuro do subjuntivo (which marks a future action without completion focus)

### Vocabulary

- **tiver / tiveres / tiver / tivermos / tiverem + particípio** — auxiliary + past participle
- Triggering conjunctions:
  - *quando* — when
  - *assim que / logo que* — as soon as
  - *depois que* — after
  - *se* — if (real conditional with completion reading)

### Grammar

Form: futuro do subjuntivo of *ter* + particípio passado.

| Pessoa | Auxiliar | + particípio |
|---|---|---|
| eu | tiver | falado |
| você / ele / ela | tiver | falado |
| nós | tivermos | falado |
| vocês / eles / elas | tiverem | falado |

The form is triggered by certain conjunctions that take futuro do subjuntivo (covered in `b2-subj-futuro`). The compound version adds the meaning of **completion** — the subordinate action will have been finished by the time of the main action.

### Exemplar sentences

- *Quando você **tiver acabado**, me chame.* — When you've finished, call me.
- *Assim que ele **tiver chegado**, começamos a reunião.* — As soon as he's arrived, we start the meeting.
- *Depois que vocês **tiverem terminado**, podemos ir.* — After you've finished, we can go.
- *Se você **tiver lido** o livro, podemos discutir.* — If you've read the book, we can discuss it.
- *Logo que eu **tiver feito** as compras, te ligo.* — As soon as I've done the shopping, I'll call you.
- *Quando ela **tiver respondido** o e-mail, te aviso.* — When she's answered the email, I'll let you know.

### Simple vs compound future subjunctive

| Form | Reading |
|---|---|
| *Quando você **chegar**, te ligo.* | When you arrive — single future action |
| *Quando você **tiver chegado**, te ligo.* | When you've arrived — completion focus |

Both are correct after *quando*; the compound emphasizes completion before the main action. In casual speech, the simple form often suffices; the compound is precision-marking.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: pair drills with b2-subj-futuro (the simple version) for completion-vs-action contrast practice. -->

### Traps

- **Don't use indicativo after *quando, assim que, depois que* in future contexts.** *Quando eu terei terminado* — wrong; subjuntivo required after these conjunctions when pointing to a future event. *Quando eu tiver terminado* — correct.
- **Distinguish from simple futuro do subjuntivo.** *Tiver* (compound auxiliary) + particípio is the future perfect subjunctive. *Tiver* alone (1st/3rd person sg of futuro do subj of *ter*) means simply "will have." Both forms use *tiver*, but only the compound has a particípio attached.
- **The compound is more common than the indicative future-perfect (terei feito).** Speakers reach for *quando eu tiver feito* far more often than for *terei feito X amanhã*. The subjunctive form has a clear conjunction trigger; the indicative form depends on context.
- **EP and BP usage are essentially identical** for this form — variant: shared.

---

## Unit 117 — Orações concessivas (embora, ainda que, mesmo que, apesar de)

*Slug: `b2-concessivas` · Sequence position: 85.5 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `concessive-clauses`, `subjunctive-triggers`, `subjunctive-present`, `subjunctive-imperfect`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-trigger-conjuncoes`, `b1-subj-imperfeito`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Construct concessive clauses ("although / even though") using the appropriate conjunction + subjuntivo
- Choose between **presente subjuntivo** (present/future hypothetical) and **imperfeito subjuntivo** (past hypothetical) based on time reference
- Use **apesar de + infinitivo** as the subjuntivo-free alternative
- Distinguish concessive subordination from adversative coordination (*embora* vs *mas*)

### Vocabulary

The concessive-conjunction inventory:

| Conjunction | Mood it triggers | Register |
|---|---|---|
| **embora** | subjuntivo | most common, neutral |
| **ainda que** | subjuntivo | common, slightly emphatic |
| **mesmo que** | subjuntivo | strongly hypothetical |
| **conquanto** | subjuntivo | formal / literary |
| **nem que** | subjuntivo | "not even if" |
| **por mais / muito que** | subjuntivo | "no matter how (much)" |
| **apesar de que** | subjuntivo | considered redundant by some prescriptivists |
| **apesar de** + infinitivo | infinitivo (no subj) | the subjuntivo-free alternative |

### Grammar

Concessive clauses contrast with the main clause: the speaker presents a fact or hypothesis that *would* normally block the main-clause action, but the action happens anyway. The subordinate clause carries subjuntivo because the speaker is not asserting the contrast as fact — they're acknowledging it hypothetically.

### Tense choice — present vs imperfect subjuntivo

Time reference of the concessive event determines the tense:

| Time | Subjuntivo tense | Example |
|---|---|---|
| Present / future hypothetical | presente | *Embora **chova** amanhã, vou sair.* — Even if it rains tomorrow, I'll go out. |
| Past hypothetical | imperfeito | *Embora **chovesse**, saímos.* — Even though it was raining, we went out. |
| Counterfactual past | mais-que-perfeito | *Embora **tivesse chovido**, saímos.* — Even though it had been raining, we went out. |

### Three primary patterns

**1. Conjunction + subjuntivo** (the canonical concessive pattern):

- *Embora **esteja** cansado, vou estudar.* — Although I'm tired, I'll study.
- *Ainda que **chova**, fazemos a festa no jardim.* — Even if it rains, we'll have the party in the garden.
- *Mesmo que ele **venha**, não vou ficar.* — Even if he comes, I won't stay.
- *Por mais que tu **tentes**, não vais conseguir.* — No matter how much you try, you won't manage.

**2. Apesar de + infinitivo** (the no-subjuntivo alternative):

This construction uses an infinitive (which can be personal — see [[b2-infinitivo-pessoal-uso]]) and avoids subjuntivo entirely:

- *Apesar de **estar** cansado, vou estudar.* — Despite being tired, I'll study. (same subject — bare infinitive)
- *Apesar de **eles virem**, não vou ficar.* — Despite their coming, I won't stay. (distinct subject — personal infinitive)

**3. Adversative coordination — NOT concessive subordination**

Coordinating conjunctions (*mas, porém, contudo, todavia, entretanto*) express contrast WITHOUT subordination — and take indicative:

- *Estou cansado, **mas** vou estudar.* — I'm tired, but I'll study. (mas + indicativo)
- *Estou cansado; **porém**, vou estudar.* — Same meaning, more formal.

The coordinative pattern is structurally simpler — two independent clauses joined by *mas*. The concessive pattern is more rhetorically marked — the subordinate clause is presented as a backgrounded fact that makes the main-clause action surprising.

### Exemplar set

- *Embora ele **seja** novo, é muito experiente.* — Although he's young, he's very experienced.
- *Ainda que **trabalhasses** mais, não terias passado.* — Even if you had worked more, you wouldn't have passed. (Type-3-like)
- *Mesmo que **chovesse** ontem, fizemos o piquenique.* — Even though it rained yesterday, we had the picnic.
- *Apesar de **chover**, fomos à praia.* — Despite the rain, we went to the beach.
- *Por mais que **estudasse**, ela não percebia a matéria.* — No matter how much she studied, she didn't get the material.
- *Conquanto a proposta **seja** interessante, não a aceitamos.* — Although the proposal is interesting, we're not accepting it. (formal register)

### Drills & artifacts

- Cross-link: see [[b1-subj-trigger-conjuncoes]] for the broader subjunctive-trigger framework that includes concessive conjunctions.
- Cross-link: see [[b2-infinitivo-pessoal-uso]] for the *apesar de* + (personal) infinitive alternative.

<!-- TODO: build a tense-choice drill (present vs imperfeito subjuntivo for concessives based on time reference). Build a concessive vs adversative discrimination drill (embora + subj vs mas + indic). -->

### Traps

- **Don't use indicativo with the concessive conjunctions.** *Embora chove* — wrong; *Embora chova* — right. The subjuntivo is mandatory.
- **Apesar de takes infinitive, NOT subjuntivo.** *Apesar de chova* is wrong. Use *apesar de chover* (bare infinitive, same subject) or *apesar de eles virem* (personal infinitive, distinct subject).
- **Embora ≠ porque.** Embora is concessive (subjuntivo); porque is causal (indicativo). *Embora chova* (even though it rains) vs *Porque chove* (because it rains).
- **Apesar de que** is heard but considered redundant by some prescriptivists — *apesar de* already does the conjunction work, so adding *que* + subjuntivo doubles the marking. Prefer the cleaner forms (*apesar de* + infinitivo OR *embora* + subjuntivo). Both alternatives are widespread in real usage; *apesar de que* won't be marked wrong but isn't elegant.
- **Mesmo se vs mesmo que.** *Mesmo se* (= "even if") takes indicativo or futuro do subjuntivo per Type-1/Type-2 conditional rules. *Mesmo que* takes subjuntivo (concessive). Different conjunctions, different syntactic behavior.
- **Tense alignment with main clause matters.** A past-time main clause (*saímos*) calls for past subjuntivo (*chovesse*) — not present subjuntivo. *Embora chova, saímos* is grammatical but mixes time references; *Embora chovesse, saímos* aligns the past hypothetical with the past main-clause action.

---

## Unit 118 — Orações finais (para que, a fim de que) + alternativa com infinitivo pessoal

*Slug: `b2-finalidade` · Sequence position: 85.6 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `purpose-clauses`, `subjunctive-triggers`, `subjunctive-present`, `personal-infinitive`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-trigger-conjuncoes`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Construct purpose clauses ("in order to / so that") using **para que / a fim de que + subjuntivo**
- Choose the **personal-infinitive alternative** (*para + infinitive*) when the subject of the purpose clause is the same as the main clause OR when distinct (with personal-infinitive inflection)
- Distinguish purpose clauses from result clauses (consecutivas) and concessive clauses (concessivas)

### Vocabulary

The purpose-conjunction inventory:

| Conjunction / structure | Mood / form | Register |
|---|---|---|
| **para que** + subj | subjuntivo | most common |
| **a fim de que** + subj | subjuntivo | formal |
| **a fim de** + infinitivo | infinitivo | formal, less common |
| **para** + infinitivo | bare or personal infinitive | most natural in BP/EP |
| **com a finalidade de** + infinitivo | infinitivo | very formal |
| **no intuito de** + infinitivo | infinitivo | formal/literary |

### Grammar

Purpose clauses express the GOAL of the main-clause action — what the action aims to bring about. Two structurally distinct paths exist:

1. **Conjunction + subjuntivo** (clause structure)
2. **Para + infinitivo** (cleaner, more common in spoken usage)

The choice between them is partly subject-determined and partly register-determined.

### Same subject — bare infinitive is the natural choice

When the subject of the main clause and the purpose clause is **identical**, the natural form is *para + bare infinitive*. Adding *que* + subjuntivo with a redundant subject sounds heavy:

- *Estudo muito **para passar** no exame.* — I study a lot to pass the exam. (natural)
- *~~Estudo muito **para que eu passe** no exame.~~* — Same meaning, but the *eu* is redundant; sounds bookish.

### Distinct subject — choose between *para que* + subj and *para* + personal infinitive

When the purpose clause has a **different subject** from the main clause, both options exist and are productive:

- *Estudo muito **para que os meus pais fiquem** orgulhosos.* — I study so my parents are proud. (subjuntivo)
- *Estudo muito **para os meus pais ficarem** orgulhosos.* — Same meaning. (personal infinitive)

The personal-infinitive form is **more economical and slightly more formal in writing**; the subjuntivo form is **more emphatic and slightly more conversational**. Both are correct.

See [[b2-infinitivo-pessoal-uso]] for the personal-infinitive details.

### Formal alternatives

For deliberately formal register (academic, legal, official) the longer conjunctions appear:

- *Trabalhamos **a fim de que** todos **tenham** acesso.* — We work so that everyone has access. (formal, with subjuntivo)
- *Trabalhamos **com a finalidade de proporcionar** acesso a todos.* — We work in order to provide access to everyone. (formal, with infinitivo)
- *Reformamos a lei **no intuito de proteger** os consumidores.* — We reformed the law in order to protect consumers. (formal/literary)

These are recognition targets in formal text; for production at B2, *para que* + subj and *para* + (personal) infinitivo cover almost all needs.

### Tense in the subjuntivo subordinate

The purpose-clause subjuntivo follows the main verb's tense:

- Main verb in present/future → presente subjuntivo: *Trabalho **para que ele tenha** uma vida melhor.*
- Main verb in past → imperfeito subjuntivo: *Trabalhei **para que ele tivesse** uma vida melhor.*

### Exemplar set

- *Saí cedo **para chegar** a tempo.* — I left early to arrive on time. (same subject, bare infinitive)
- *Saí cedo **para o João chegar** a tempo.* — I left early so João would arrive on time. (distinct subject, personal infinitive)
- *Saí cedo **para que o João chegasse** a tempo.* — Same meaning, subjuntivo path.
- *A professora explicou devagar **para que todos percebessem**.* — The teacher explained slowly so everyone would understand.
- *Estudamos juntos **a fim de termos melhores resultados**.* — We study together so we have better results. (formal, personal infinitive)
- *O governo aprovou a lei **no intuito de proteger** as crianças.* — The government passed the law to protect the children. (formal/literary)

### Drills & artifacts

- Cross-link: see [[b1-subj-trigger-conjuncoes]] for the broader subjunctive-trigger framework.
- Cross-link: see [[b2-infinitivo-pessoal-uso]] for the personal-infinitive alternative — the choice of subjuntivo vs personal infinitive in purpose clauses is one of the canonical contexts where both options compete.

<!-- TODO: build a same-subject vs distinct-subject choice drill (when does *para + bare inf* vs *para + personal inf* vs *para que + subj* apply?). Build a register-shifting drill (informal *para* / standard *para que* / formal *a fim de que* / very formal *no intuito de*). -->

### Traps

- **Don't use *para que* with the same subject.** *Estudo para que eu passe* sounds wrong/bookish. Same subject → *para passar*.
- **The subjuntivo path requires a *que*.** *Estudo para os meus pais fiquem* — wrong (no *que*). Either *para que os meus pais fiquem* (with *que* and subj) or *para os meus pais ficarem* (no *que*, personal infinitive).
- **A fim de vs a fim de que.** *A fim de* takes infinitive (often with same subject); *a fim de que* takes subjuntivo. Both are formal; the difference is the same as *para* vs *para que*.
- **Don't confuse with consecutive clauses.** Purpose: *Falo devagar **para que percebas**.* (subjuntivo, intent). Result: *Falo devagar **de modo que percebes**.* (indicative, consequence). The conjunction *de modo que* is genuinely ambiguous between purpose and result depending on the verb mood — see [[b2-consecutivas]] for the result-clause framing.
- **Tense agreement with main clause.** Past main verb forces past subjuntivo: *Estudei para que ele **passasse***. — not *para que ele passe*. The subordinate aligns to the temporal frame of the main clause.
- **Don't substitute *para* with *por* in purpose clauses.** *Por* expresses cause/exchange/duration, not purpose. *Estudo por passar no exame* is wrong — use *para passar*.

---

## Unit 119 — Orações consecutivas (tão / tanto … que — resultado, indicativo)

*Slug: `b2-consecutivas` · Sequence position: 85.7 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `result-clauses`

**Prereqs:** `a2-pret-vs-imp`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Construct result/consecutive clauses ("so X that Y") using **tão / tanto … que + indicative**
- Distinguish result clauses (consequence, indicative) from purpose clauses (intent, subjuntivo) — same surface conjunctions can read either way
- Recognize the formal-register alternatives (*de tal forma que, de tal modo que, de tal maneira que*)

### Vocabulary

The result-clause inventory:

| Structure | Pattern | Example |
|---|---|---|
| **tão + adjective + que** | intensifier + adj + que + indic | *tão alto que toca o teto* |
| **tão + adverb + que** | intensifier + adv + que + indic | *tão rapidamente que ninguém viu* |
| **tanto + noun + que** | quantifier + noun + que + indic (with agreement: tanto/tanta/tantos/tantas) | *tanto trabalho que não dorme* |
| **tanto … que** (verb intensity) | verb + tanto + que + indic | *trabalha tanto que está exausto* |
| **de tal forma / modo / maneira que** | manner + que + indic | *falou de tal forma que todos perceberam* |
| **de modo que** (ambiguous) | indicative → result; subjuntivo → purpose | see Traps |

### Grammar

Result clauses express the **consequence** of the main-clause action — the magnitude or manner of the main clause produces the subordinate-clause outcome. Because the consequence is asserted as fact, the subordinate clause takes **indicative**, not subjuntivo.

### Pattern 1 — tão + adjective/adverb + que

The intensifier *tão* (so, such) marks the main-clause adjective or adverb; *que* introduces the consequence:

- *A música está **tão alta que** não consigo dormir.* — The music is so loud that I can't sleep.
- *Ele falou **tão depressa que** ninguém percebeu.* — He spoke so fast that nobody understood.
- *A cidade era **tão bonita que** decidi mudar-me.* — The city was so beautiful that I decided to move.

### Pattern 2 — tanto + noun + que

The quantifier *tanto* agrees with the noun in gender + number (*tanto/tanta/tantos/tantas*):

- *Comeu **tanta comida que** ficou doente.* — She ate so much food that she got sick.
- *Tem **tantos livros que** não cabem na estante.* — He has so many books that they don't fit on the shelf.
- *Há **tanto trabalho que** preciso de ajuda.* — There's so much work that I need help.

### Pattern 3 — verb + tanto + que (verb intensity)

When *tanto* modifies a verb directly (no noun follows), it works as an adverb of intensity:

- *Trabalha **tanto que** está exausto.* — He works so much that he's exhausted.
- *Estudaram **tanto que** passaram com facilidade.* — They studied so much that they passed easily.
- *Chove **tanto que** as ruas estão alagadas.* — It's raining so much that the streets are flooded.

### Pattern 4 — de tal forma / modo / maneira que (formal)

A more formal way to introduce the consequence:

- *Explicou **de tal forma que** todos ficaram convencidos.* — He explained in such a way that everyone was convinced.
- *O concerto correu **de tal modo que** o público pediu repetição.* — The concert went so well that the audience asked for an encore.
- *Comportou-se **de tal maneira que** foi expulso.* — He behaved in such a way that he was expelled.

### The de modo que ambiguity

The conjunction **de modo que** is genuinely ambiguous between RESULT (indicative) and PURPOSE (subjuntivo). The verb mood disambiguates:

| Mood | Reading | Example |
|---|---|---|
| Indicative | result | *Estudo de modo que **aprendo**.* — I study in a way that I learn. (consequence) |
| Subjuntivo | purpose | *Estudo de modo que **aprenda**.* — I study so that I learn. (intent) |

Same surface conjunction, two distinct grammatical paths. Same applies to *de forma que* and *de maneira que*.

### Exemplar set

- *A casa é **tão grande que** se perde a gente lá dentro.* — The house is so big that you get lost inside.
- *Choveu **tanto que** o jogo foi cancelado.* — It rained so much that the game was cancelled.
- *O café estava **tão quente que** queimei a língua.* — The coffee was so hot that I burned my tongue.
- *Comprou **tantos presentes que** não conseguiu carregá-los.* — She bought so many gifts that she couldn't carry them.
- *Ele explicou **de tal forma que** todos ficaram a perceber.* — He explained in such a way that everyone understood.
- *A criança chorou **tanto que** a mãe teve que acalmá-la.* — The child cried so much that the mother had to calm her down.

### Drills & artifacts

- Cross-link: see [[b2-finalidade]] for the purpose-clause counterpart — the *de modo que* + subjuntivo path is taught there.

<!-- TODO: build a result-vs-purpose discrimination drill (de modo que + indic vs + subj). Build a tão / tanto pattern drill across adjective / noun / verb-intensity contexts. -->

### Traps

- **Don't use subjuntivo in result clauses.** *Estudou tanto que passe* — wrong (subjuntivo). *Estudou tanto que passou* — right (indicativo). The consequence is asserted as fact, not hypothetical.
- **De modo que + indicative = result; + subjuntivo = purpose.** Same conjunction, two functions. Choose the mood by intent. *Falo de modo que percebes* (you understand — fact) vs *Falo de modo que percebas* (so that you may understand — intent).
- **Tanto agrees with the noun.** *Tanto trabalho* (m sg), *tanta comida* (f sg), *tantos livros* (m pl), *tantas pessoas* (f pl). Only the verb-intensity use (*trabalha tanto*) is invariable.
- **Tão is for adjectives and adverbs only; tanto is for nouns and verbs.** *Tão livros* is wrong; *tantos livros* is right. *Tanta bonita* is wrong; *tão bonita* is right.
- **Don't conflate with comparative tão … como / tanto … como.** Comparative: *tão alto **como** o pai* (as tall as the father). Result: *tão alto **que** toca no teto* (so tall that he touches the ceiling). The conjunction tells you which is which (*como* vs *que*).
- **Causal vs result: porque vs tão … que.** *Não dormi **porque** estava barulhento* (causal — because). *Estava **tão** barulhento **que** não dormi* (result — so much so that). Same situation, different rhetorical framing — causal points back at the cause; result points forward at the consequence.

---

## Unit 120 — Conjunções condicionais além de *se* (caso, a menos que, contanto que, desde que)

*Slug: `b2-conj-condicionais` · Sequence position: 85.8 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `conditional-conjunctions`, `conditional-sentences`, `subjunctive-triggers`, `subjunctive-imperfect`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-trigger-hipotetico`, `b1-subj-imperfeito`, `b1-condicional`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Use conditional conjunctions beyond *se* — **caso, a menos que, a não ser que, contanto que, desde que** — with appropriate subjuntivo
- Distinguish the **conditional reading** of *desde que* (subjuntivo, "provided that") from its **temporal reading** (indicative, "since [time]")
- Choose between *se* and the more nuanced conjunctions based on the speaker's stance toward the condition (real vs hypothetical, restrictive, exclusionary, etc.)

### Vocabulary

The conditional-conjunction inventory beyond *se*:

| Conjunction | Meaning | Mood | Stance |
|---|---|---|---|
| **caso** | in case / if | subjuntivo | hypothetical, slightly more formal than *se* |
| **a menos que** | unless | subjuntivo | exclusionary |
| **a não ser que** | unless | subjuntivo | exclusionary, slightly more formal |
| **contanto que** | provided that | subjuntivo | restrictive, as a guarantee |
| **desde que** (conditional) | provided that | subjuntivo | restrictive |
| **desde que** (temporal) | since [time] | indicativo | temporal sequence |
| **salvo se** | except if | indicativo or subjuntivo | exclusionary, formal |
| **se acaso** | if by chance | subjuntivo | tentative |
| **na hipótese de** + infinitivo | in case of | infinitivo | formal |

### Grammar

These conjunctions extend the conditional system beyond plain *se*. Each carries its own pragmatic stance:

- **caso** — neutral conditional, slightly more formal than *se*
- **a menos que / a não ser que** — exclusionary ("unless")
- **contanto que / desde que** — restrictive ("provided that")
- **desde que** also has a temporal reading (indicative)

This unit builds on the conditional-sentence framework taught in [[b1-cond-real-bp]] / [[b1-cond-real-ep]] (Type 1), [[b2-cond-irreal-bp]] / [[b2-cond-irreal-ep]] (Type 2), and [[b2-cond-contra-bp]] / [[b2-cond-contra-ep]] (Type 3). The form-anchor for condicional simples is [[b1-condicional]].

### Caso — alternative to se

*Caso* is essentially "in case / if" — slightly more formal than *se* but pragmatically similar:

- *Caso **chova**, ficamos em casa.* — In case it rains, we'll stay home.
- *Caso **precises** de ajuda, liga-me.* — If you need help, call me.
- *Caso **tivesses estudado**, terias passado.* — If you had studied, you would have passed. (Type-3 with caso instead of se)

*Caso* always takes subjuntivo. It cannot replace *se* in Type-1 indicative-only contexts (no *caso chove* with present indicative).

### A menos que / a não ser que — unless

These exclusionary conjunctions take subjuntivo:

- *Vou à festa, **a menos que chova**.* — I'll go to the party, unless it rains.
- *Não saio, **a menos que tu venhas comigo**.* — I'm not going out unless you come with me.
- *Aceitarei o emprego, **a não ser que apareça** algo melhor.* — I'll accept the job, unless something better comes up.

The exclusionary stance: the main-clause action holds **except** in the case described by the subordinate. *A menos que* and *a não ser que* are interchangeable; the latter is slightly more formal.

### Contanto que / desde que (conditional) — provided that

These restrictive conjunctions establish a condition as a guarantee:

- *Vou contigo, **contanto que cheguemos** cedo.* — I'll go with you, provided that we arrive early.
- *Podes sair, **contanto que voltes** antes da meia-noite.* — You can go out, provided you come back before midnight.
- *Podes ficar, **desde que estudes**.* — You can stay, provided that you study.

The restrictive stance: the main-clause action holds **only on condition that** the subordinate clause is met.

### Desde que — conditional vs temporal

This is the highest-leverage trap in the unit. *Desde que* has two readings, distinguished by mood:

| Reading | Mood | Example |
|---|---|---|
| Conditional ("provided that") | subjuntivo | *Podes ficar **desde que estudes**.* — You can stay provided you study. |
| Temporal ("since [time]") | indicativo | *Conheço-o **desde que nasceu**.* — I've known him since he was born. |

The temporal reading anchors a starting point in time; the conditional reading establishes a restriction. Same surface conjunction, different moods, different meanings.

### Salvo se / a não ser que — except if

*Salvo se* mostly takes indicative when describing real exceptions, subjuntivo for hypothetical exceptions:

- *Vou **salvo se chove muito**.* — I'll go except if it's raining a lot. (real exception, indicative)
- *Vou **salvo se chovesse muito**.* — Same with hypothetical past framing, subjuntivo.

In practice, *a não ser que* + subjuntivo is more common and more flexible.

### Tense of subjuntivo follows the main clause

Standard tense agreement:

- Main verb in present/future → presente subjuntivo: *Vou contigo, contanto que **cheguemos** cedo.*
- Main verb in past → imperfeito subjuntivo: *Fui contigo, contanto que **chegássemos** cedo.*
- Counterfactual past → mais-que-perfeito subjuntivo: *Teria ido, contanto que **tivéssemos chegado** cedo.*

### Exemplar set

- *Caso ele **venha**, avisa-me.* — If he comes, let me know.
- *Saio à noite, **a menos que esteja** muito cansado.* — I go out at night, unless I'm very tired.
- *Vou ajudar-te, **contanto que sejas** honesto comigo.* — I'll help you, provided you're honest with me.
- *Podes usar o meu carro, **desde que devolvas** com gasolina.* — You can use my car, provided you return it with fuel.
- *Conheço a Maria **desde que era** criança.* — I've known Maria since she was a child. (temporal — indicative)
- *Conheço a Maria **desde que tu a apresentaste**.* — I've known Maria since you introduced her. (temporal — indicative)
- *Aceito o convite, **a não ser que apareça** algo urgente.* — I accept the invitation, unless something urgent comes up.

### Drills & artifacts

- Cross-link: see [[b1-cond-real-bp]] / [[b1-cond-real-ep]] (Type 1), [[b2-cond-irreal-bp]] / [[b2-cond-irreal-ep]] (Type 2), [[b2-cond-contra-bp]] / [[b2-cond-contra-ep]] (Type 3) for the conditional-sentence framework.
- Cross-link: see [[b1-subj-trigger-hipotetico]] for the subjuntivo trigger from the simple *se*-conditional.
- Cross-link: [[b1-condicional]] (shared form anchor) — this unit applies the locked architectural pattern from Cluster 9.

<!-- TODO: build a desde-que disambiguation drill (conditional vs temporal — given a sentence, identify the reading and the correct mood). Build a conjunction-choice drill (which of *caso, a menos que, contanto que, desde que* fits a given context?). -->

### Traps

- **Desde que is the highest-leverage ambiguity.** *Desde que cheguei* is temporal (indicative — "since I arrived"); *desde que chegues* is conditional (subjuntivo — "provided that you arrive"). The mood is the disambiguator.
- **Don't use indicative with caso.** *Caso chove* is wrong; *caso chova* is right. Caso always takes subjuntivo.
- **A menos que and a não ser que require subjuntivo.** *A menos que vens* is wrong; *a menos que venhas* is right.
- **Contanto que vs com tanto que.** Note the spelling: *contanto que* (single word for the conjunction) vs *com tanto que* (preposition + intensifier — different meaning entirely). Same pronunciation, different writing.
- **Salvo se can take either mood.** Indicative for real exceptions, subjuntivo for hypothetical. When in doubt, *a não ser que* + subjuntivo is more flexible and unambiguous.
- **Don't import *se* habits to other conjunctions.** *Caso chove* (wrong — caso requires subj) is a common error from importing the *se* + presente indicativo (Type 1 habitual) pattern into *caso* contexts. The two conjunctions don't share mood behavior.
- **Tense alignment with main clause matters.** Past main clause forces past subjuntivo: *Aceitei o emprego contanto que **pagassem** bem* (past hypothetical) — not *contanto que paguem*.

---

## Unit 121 — Colloquial Brazilian Portuguese Consolidated

*Slug: `b2-coloquial-bp` · Sequence position: 86.0 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: bp*

**Concepts:** `colloquial-speech`, `register-formal-informal`

### Outcomes

- Understand authentic Brazilian Portuguese conversations
- Recognize all major reductions and colloquialisms
- Know when to use formal vs informal speech
- Sound more natural in casual conversation (when appropriate)

### Vocabulary

- tá (está), tô (estou), tava (estava), tínha (tinha)
- cê (você), ocê (você - some regions)
- vô (vou), fazê (fazer), comê (comer)
- num (não), né (não é?), sabe (you know)
- pra (para), pro (para o), praquela (para aquela)
- tipo (like), assim (like), então (so)

### Grammar

- **Systematic overview of colloquial BP reductions and speech patterns**
- Recognition vs production: understand in listening, use in appropriate contexts
- Formal vs informal: knowing when each is appropriate

### Exemplar sentences

**Formal:** Você está indo para casa?
**Colloquial:** Cê tá indo pra casa?

**Formal:** Eu vou fazer isso amanhã.
**Colloquial:** Vô fazê isso amanhã.

**Formal:** Eu não sei.
**Colloquial:** Num sei. OR Não sei, não.

**Formal:** Você quer ir ao cinema?
**Colloquial:** Cê quer ir no cinema?

## Unit 122 — Condicional Tipo 2 — Irreal presente/futuro (se + imperfeito subj + condicional)

*Slug: `b2-cond-irreal-bp` · Sequence position: 86.5 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: bp*

**Concepts:** `conditional-sentences`, `subjunctive-imperfect`, `conditional-usage`

**Prereqs:** `b1-condicional-bp`, `b1-subj-imperfeito`, `b1-subj-trigger-hipotetico`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Construct **Type 2 (irreal present/future)** conditional sentences in BP using `se + imperfeito subjuntivo + condicional simples`
- Pair the subjuntivo clause and the condicional clause correctly (no indicativo in either slot)
- Use Type 2 to express imagined preferences, hypothetical plans, polite suggestions, and contrary-to-current-reality statements

### Vocabulary

- **se** — if (hypothetical reading)
- Common imperfeito subjuntivo forms (review from `b1-subj-imperfeito`): fosse, tivesse, estivesse, fizesse, pudesse, soubesse, viesse
- Common condicional simples forms (review from `b1-condicional-bp`): seria, teria, faria, poderia, gostaria, viajaria

### Grammar

Type 2 covers situations the speaker treats as **unreal at the moment of speaking** — imagined, hypothetical, or contrary to current circumstance.

The pattern is fixed in BP:

`se + [imperfeito subjuntivo] + [condicional simples]`

Both slots are required. The trigger-hipotetico unit (`b1-subj-trigger-hipotetico`) covers the subjuntivo side; this unit covers the **full sentence pairing** and the condicional side.

### Exemplar sentences

- *Se eu **fosse** rico, **viajaria** pelo mundo.* — If I were rich, I'd travel the world.
- *Se ela **soubesse** a verdade, **me contaria**.* — If she knew the truth, she'd tell me.
- *Se nós **tivéssemos** mais tempo, **terminaríamos** hoje.* — If we had more time, we'd finish today.
- *Se você **estudasse** mais, **passaria** com facilidade.* — If you studied more, you'd pass easily.
- *O que você **faria** se **ganhasse** na loteria?* — What would you do if you won the lottery?
- *Se eles **viessem** amanhã, eu **ficaria** muito feliz.* — If they came tomorrow, I'd be very happy.

### Order is flexible

Either clause can come first; the verb forms don't change:

- *Eu viajaria pelo mundo se fosse rico.*
- *Se fosse rico, eu viajaria pelo mundo.*

### Common error patterns

| Wrong | Right | Why |
|---|---|---|
| *Se eu **era** rico, viajaria...* | Se eu **fosse** rico, viajaria... | Type 2 needs imperfeito subj, not imperfeito indic |
| *Se eu fosse rico, **vou viajar**...* | Se eu fosse rico, **viajaria**... | Main clause needs condicional, not future |
| *Se eu fosse rico, **viajo**...* | Se eu fosse rico, **viajaria**... | Main clause needs condicional, not present |
| *Se eu **seria** rico, viajaria...* | Se eu **fosse** rico, viajaria... | *se*-clause needs subjuntivo, not condicional |

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: pair drill set with b1-subj-trigger-hipotetico (Cluster 2) — they share examples. The trigger unit drills the subjuntivo side; this unit drills the full sentence pairing. -->

### Traps

- **The subjuntivo trigger is *se* + hypothetical reading.** Type 1 *se* (real) takes indicativo or futuro do subjuntivo. The hypothetical reading is what triggers imperfeito subjuntivo. See `b1-cond-real-bp` for the contrast.
- **EP-BP divergence is sharp here.** EP commonly says *Se ela soubesse, dizia* (imperfeito indicativo as a condicional substitute). BP says *Se ela soubesse, diria* (condicional simples). When teaching EP, the imperfeito-as-cortesia pattern is the default — this BP unit's *diria* form would sound formal in EP. EP twin will cover this.
- **Polite-request overlap.** `b1-querer-aspect-bp` covers *eu queria um café* (polite-request imperfeito). The Type 2 condicional *eu gostaria de um café* is a more formal alternative. Both are correct; *queria* is more casual.
- **The two slots aren't interchangeable.** *Se eu fosse rico, fosse viajar* — wrong, you can't double the subjuntivo. *Se eu seria rico, viajaria* — wrong, you can't double the condicional. The pair is rigid: subjuntivo + condicional.

---

## Unit 123 — Condicional Tipo 3 — Contrafactual passado (se + mais-que-perfeito subj + condicional composto)

*Slug: `b2-cond-contra-bp` · Sequence position: 86.6 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: bp*

**Concepts:** `conditional-sentences`, `compound-tenses`

**Prereqs:** `b1-condicional-bp`, `b1-subj-imperfeito`, `b2-mais-que-perfeito-subj`, `b2-condicional-composto-bp`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Construct **Type 3 (counterfactual past)** conditional sentences in BP using `se + mais-que-perfeito subjuntivo + condicional composto`
- Recognize Type 3 as the past-time counterpart of Type 2 — the imagined situation is no longer reachable because the moment is gone
- Distinguish *Se eu tivesse estudado, teria passado* (counterfactual past) from *Se eu estudasse, passaria* (irreal present/future)

### Vocabulary

- **se** — if (counterfactual past reading)
- *mais-que-perfeito subjuntivo* forms (review from `b2-mais-que-perfeito-subj`): tivesse + particípio
- *condicional composto* forms (review from `b2-condicional-composto-bp`): teria + particípio

### Grammar

Type 3 covers situations the speaker treats as **counterfactual** — what *would have* happened *if* something *had been* different in the past. The past time anchor closes the door; the counterfactual is no longer reachable.

Pattern (rigid in BP):

`se + [mais-que-perfeito subjuntivo: tivesse + particípio] + [condicional composto: teria + particípio]`

### Exemplar sentences

- *Se eu **tivesse estudado** mais, **teria passado** no exame.* — If I had studied more, I would have passed the exam.
- *Se ela **tivesse vindo** ontem, **teríamos comemorado** juntos.* — If she had come yesterday, we would have celebrated together.
- *Se vocês **tivessem chegado** mais cedo, **teriam visto** o início do filme.* — If you had arrived earlier, you would have seen the beginning of the movie.
- *Se eu **tivesse sabido**, **teria avisado** todo mundo.* — If I had known, I would have warned everyone.
- *Se ele **tivesse dito** a verdade, ninguém **teria ficado** chateado.* — If he had told the truth, nobody would have gotten upset.

### Type 2 vs Type 3 contrast

The difference is the time anchor of the imagined situation:

- *Se eu **estudasse**, **passaria**.* — If I studied (now / in general), I'd pass. (Type 2 — present/future hypothetical)
- *Se eu **tivesse estudado**, **teria passado**.* — If I had studied (back then), I would have passed. (Type 3 — counterfactual past)

Both are unreal at the moment of speaking; Type 3 specifically anchors the unreality in the past.

### Mixed conditionals

A common variant: past condition → present consequence (mixing Type 3's *se*-clause with Type 2's main clause):

- *Se eu **tivesse estudado**, **estaria** trabalhando como engenheiro hoje.* — If I had studied, I'd be working as an engineer today.

The *se*-clause is mais-que-perfeito subjuntivo (past condition); the main clause shifts to condicional simples (present consequence) because the result is in the present.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a Type 1 / Type 2 / Type 3 contrast drill — same situation, three time-anchorings. Cross-link b2-mais-que-perfeito-subj and b2-condicional-composto-bp once Cluster 4 enriches those form-introduction units. -->

### Traps

- **Don't substitute mais-que-perfeito do indicativo (tinha estudado) for the subjuntivo form (tivesse estudado).** *Se eu tinha estudado, teria passado* — wrong in BP. The *se*-clause requires subjuntivo. (EP often allows *tinha estudado* in spoken usage, which is the source of EP-twin divergence — covered in the EP twin.)
- **Don't use the simple condicional in the main clause for past consequences.** *Se eu tivesse estudado, passaria* mixes Type 3's *se*-clause with Type 2's main clause — only acceptable when the consequence is genuinely present (mixed conditional, see above). For straightforward past consequence, use *teria passado*.
- **EP register substitution.** EP commonly says *Se eu tivesse estudado, tinha passado* (mais-que-perfeito do indicativo replacing condicional composto). BP keeps *teria passado*. Recognize the EP form when you hear it.
- **The form prereqs (`b2-mais-que-perfeito-subj` and `b2-condicional-composto-bp`) are sparse placeholders right now.** Cluster 4 will enrich them with full conjugation paradigms and contrast practice. For Type 3 sentence construction, the patterns above are sufficient — reach for the prereq units when you need to drill the forms in isolation.

- **Beyond physical proximity:** demonstratives have multiple uses
- **Three uses:** physical, discourse, temporal
