## Unit 125 — Infinitivo pessoal — formação

*Slug: `b2-infinitivo-pessoal-formacao` · Sequence position: 87.5 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `personal-infinitive`

**Prereqs:** `a1-vou-infinitivo`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Form the **personal infinitive** for any verb — regular and "irregular" alike (the personal-infinitive paradigm is highly regular)
- Recognize the difference between the bare infinitive (*falar*) and the inflected forms (*falares, falarmos, falarem*)
- Distinguish the personal-infinitive forms from the present-subjuntivo forms in same-form cells (1st-person sing and 3rd-person sing collide on form for many verbs)

### Vocabulary

The personal infinitive is a finite-like form of the infinitive that inflects for person and number. The endings:

- **eu** → no ending (bare infinitive)
- **tu** → -es
- **você / ele / ela** → no ending (bare infinitive)
- **nós** → -mos
- **vocês / eles / elas** → -em

(*vós* form *-des* is archaic and excluded from modern usage.)

### Grammar

### Regular paradigm

The personal infinitive of any -ar / -er / -ir verb is built by appending the personal endings to the **bare infinitive**. No stem change — just additions.

| Pessoa | falar (-AR) | comer (-ER) | partir (-IR) |
|---|---|---|---|
| eu | falar | comer | partir |
| tu | falares | comeres | partires |
| você / ele / ela | falar | comer | partir |
| nós | falarmos | comermos | partirmos |
| vocês / eles / elas | falarem | comerem | partirem |

### "Irregular" verbs follow the same pattern

Verbs that are highly irregular in other tenses (ser, ter, ir, vir, fazer, pôr) **become regular in personal infinitive** — just append the endings to the bare infinitive:

| Pessoa | ser | ter | ir | vir | fazer | pôr |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| eu | ser | ter | ir | vir | fazer | pôr |
| tu | seres | teres | ires | vires | fazeres | pores |
| você / ele / ela | ser | ter | ir | vir | fazer | pôr |
| nós | sermos | termos | irmos | virmos | fazermos | pormos |
| vocês / eles / elas | serem | terem | irem | virem | fazerem | porem |

Note: the circumflex on the bare *pôr* form drops in the inflected forms (*pores, pormos, porem*) because those forms are no longer monosyllabic.

### Same pattern for derivatives

Derivatives of pôr / ter / vir inherit:

- compor → compores, compormos, comporem
- manter → manteres, mantermos, manterem
- intervir → intervires, intervirmos, intervirem

### Distinguishing from subjuntivo presente

Several personal-infinitive forms are identical to subjuntivo presente forms — disambiguation is contextual, not formal.

For **-AR verbs**, the forms diverge cleanly:

| Pessoa | personal infinitive (falar) | subjuntivo presente (falar) |
|---|---|---|
| eu | falar | fale |
| tu | falares | fales |
| ele / ela | falar | fale |
| nós | falarmos | falemos |
| eles / elas | falarem | falem |

For **-ER / -IR verbs**, the eu and 3sg forms collide with subjuntivo presente — distinguished only by trigger context:

| Pessoa | personal infinitive (comer) | subjuntivo presente (comer) |
|---|---|---|
| eu | comer | coma |
| tu | comeres | comas |
| ele / ela | comer | coma |
| nós | comermos | comamos |
| eles / elas | comerem | comam |

Wait — these *don't* collide for -ER/-IR because subj-pres has its own endings. Let me re-check.

Actually the collision is at the **futuro do subjuntivo** for regular -er/-ir verbs:

| Pessoa | personal infinitive (comer) | futuro do subjuntivo (comer) |
|---|---|---|
| eu | comer | comer |
| tu | comeres | comeres |
| ele / ela | comer | comer |
| nós | comermos | comermos |
| eles / elas | comerem | comerem |

The forms are **identical** — only context (the trigger) tells them apart:

- *Quando comermos…* — futuro do subjuntivo (after temporal conjunction *quando*)
- *Para comermos…* — personal infinitive (after preposition *para* with subject)

This is the most common confusion point and is covered in the use unit (`b2-infinitivo-pessoal-uso`).

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a personal-infinitive paradigm drill across regular + "irregular" verbs (the "irregular" verbs are actually regular here). Pair with b2-infinitivo-pessoal-uso for application practice. -->

### Traps

- **Don't try to make the "irregular" verbs irregular here.** Personal infinitive of *ser* is *ser/seres/ser/sermos/serem* — no *seja-/foss-* stems. The verb's other-tense irregularity doesn't carry into personal infinitive.
- **The personal infinitive of pôr drops the circumflex in inflected forms.** *Pôr* (bare) but *pores, pormos, porem* (inflected). The circumflex marks contrastive stress on the monosyllable; once the form has additional syllables, the accent falls naturally without needing the diacritic.
- **Form collision with futuro do subjuntivo for -ER/-IR verbs is real.** *Comermos* is both personal infinitive and futuro do subjuntivo for *comer*. Disambiguation is by trigger: temporal/conditional conjunctions (*quando, se, assim que*) signal futuro do subjuntivo; prepositions or impersonal expressions signal personal infinitive. Covered in `b2-infinitivo-pessoal-uso`.
- **For -AR verbs, the form is unique** — no collision with subjuntivo or futuro do subjuntivo. *Falarmos* unambiguously means personal infinitive (futuro do subj would be *falarmos* — actually wait, futuro do subj of *falar* is also *falarmos*. Same collision!). Recheck: yes, the collision applies across all conjugations. Disambiguation is always by trigger context.
- **The personal-infinitive form of vir is *virmos*, NOT *vimos*.** *Vimos* is the present-indicative 1pl of *vir*. *Virmos* is the personal infinitive 1pl. The extra *r* matters.

---

## Unit 126 — Infinitivo pessoal — uso (sujeito distinto, preposições, expressões impessoais)

*Slug: `b2-infinitivo-pessoal-uso` · Sequence position: 87.6 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `personal-infinitive`, `register-formal-informal`

**Prereqs:** `b2-infinitivo-pessoal-formacao`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Choose **personal infinitive** vs **uninflected (bare) infinitive** based on subject distinctness
- Use the personal infinitive after prepositions (*para, sem, antes de, depois de, ao*) when the subject of the infinitive clause differs from or needs clarification
- Use the personal infinitive with impersonal expressions (*é importante, é necessário, é melhor*) as an alternative to the subjuntivo construction
- Recognize the register effect: personal infinitive is more economical and slightly more formal than subjuntivo equivalents

### Vocabulary

Common triggers / contexts for personal infinitive:

- **Prepositions**: para, sem, antes de, depois de, até, ao, por, em
- **Impersonal expressions**: é importante, é necessário, é melhor, é preciso, é bom, é pena
- **Conjunctions allowing infinitive substitution**: para que (→ para), antes que (→ antes de), sem que (→ sem)
- **Verbs of perception/causation**: ver, ouvir, sentir, deixar, mandar, fazer (with following infinitive clause)

### Grammar

The personal infinitive is **selected over the bare infinitive when the subject of the infinitive clause is distinct from the main-clause subject, or when subject identification needs clarification**. Three primary uses:

### 1. After prepositions, with a distinct subject

The most distinctive use. When the subject of the infinitive clause is different from the main clause's subject, the personal infinitive marks it explicitly:

| Bare infinitive (same subject) | Personal infinitive (distinct subject) |
|---|---|
| *Estudo **para passar** no exame.* — I study to pass the exam. | *Estudo **para os meus pais ficarem** orgulhosos.* — I study so my parents will be proud. |
| *Saí **sem comer**.* — I left without eating. | *Saí **sem eles me verem**.* — I left without them seeing me. |
| *Antes de partir, deixa um recado.* — Before leaving, leave a note. | *Antes de partires, deixa-me um recado.* — Before you leave, leave me a note. |

Even when the subject is the same as the main clause, personal infinitive is sometimes used for clarity, especially in plural contexts:

- *Saímos antes de chegarmos atrasados.* — We left before getting late. (the *-mos* makes plural-subject explicit)

### 2. With impersonal expressions

Personal infinitive competes with subjuntivo presente in impersonal-expression contexts. **Both are correct**; the personal infinitive is more economical and slightly more formal in writing:

| Subjuntivo (`b1-subj-trigger-impessoal`) | Personal infinitive |
|---|---|
| *É importante que eles **saibam** disso.* | *É importante eles **saberem** disso.* |
| *É necessário que vocês **cheguem** cedo.* | *É necessário vocês **chegarem** cedo.* |
| *É melhor que nós **fiquemos** em casa.* | *É melhor nós **ficarmos** em casa.* |
| *É pena que tu não **possas** vir.* | *É pena tu não **poderes** vir.* |

The subjuntivo version is more emphatic and feels more "complete" syntactically; the personal-infinitive version is leaner and reads as slightly more formal in written contexts. Choice is register-driven.

### 3. After verbs of perception and causation

With *ver, ouvir, sentir, deixar, mandar, fazer* + infinitive clause, the personal infinitive is used when the subject of the embedded verb is plural or distinct:

- *Vi **as crianças correrem** pelo parque.* — I saw the children run through the park.
- *Ouvimos **os pássaros cantarem** ao amanhecer.* — We heard the birds sing at dawn.
- *Deixei **os miúdos brincarem** mais um pouco.* — I let the kids play a bit longer.
- *Mandei **o mecânico arranjar** o carro.* — I had the mechanic fix the car.

For singular subjects, both bare and personal infinitive are acceptable:

- *Vi **o João correr**.* / *Vi **o João correr**.* — same form, no plural marking needed.

### When to keep the bare infinitive

When the subject of the infinitive clause is **the same as the main clause** AND **obvious from context**, use the bare infinitive — adding a personal ending sounds redundant:

- *Eu quero **comer**.* — not *eu quero eu comer*.
- *Posso **falar** contigo?* — not *posso eu falar*.
- *Gosto de **viajar**.* — not *gosto de eu viajar*.

After modal-like verbs (*poder, querer, dever, ir, vir*) and aspectual verbs (*começar a, acabar de, continuar a*), the bare infinitive is the natural choice — these verbs are aspectual extensions of the main verb, not clause introducers with their own subject.

### Form-collision disambiguation

Personal infinitive forms often collide with **futuro do subjuntivo** forms (especially -ER/-IR verbs). The trigger context disambiguates:

| Form | Trigger | Reading |
|---|---|---|
| *comermos* | after *para* / impersonal expression | personal infinitive |
| *comermos* | after *quando* / *assim que* | futuro do subjuntivo |

- *Para **comermos** bem, escolhemos um bom restaurante.* — Personal infinitive (preposition *para*).
- *Quando **comermos**, conversamos.* — Futuro do subjuntivo (temporal conjunction *quando*).

### Exemplar set (mixed)

- *Foi bom **tu teres vindo**.* — It was good that you came.
- *Para **eles entenderem**, é preciso explicar devagar.* — For them to understand, you need to explain slowly.
- *Antes de **sairmos**, vamos rever a lista.* — Before we leave, let's review the list.
- *É melhor **vocês ficarem** aqui.* — It's better for you all to stay here.
- *Sem **nós sabermos**, os planos mudaram.* — Without our knowing, the plans changed.
- *Vi **as crianças brincarem** no jardim.* — I saw the children play in the garden.
- *É importante **eles serem** honestos.* — It's important for them to be honest.

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a same-subject vs distinct-subject choice drill (when does personal vs bare infinitive apply?). Build a personal-infinitive-vs-subjuntivo drill for impersonal-expression contexts (cross-link to b1-subj-trigger-impessoal). -->

### Traps

- **Don't overuse personal infinitive in colloquial speech.** Spoken BP often defaults to the bare infinitive even where personal infinitive would be technically more precise. *É importante eles saber* (colloquial BP, with bare infinitive) is heard, though prescriptively *saberem*. Spoken EP and formal BP/EP both prefer the personal-inflected form.
- **The personal-infinitive vs subjuntivo choice is register, not error.** A B2 student writing an essay should generally prefer personal infinitive after impersonal expressions (more economical, more "writerly"). A student speaking informally with friends might use subjuntivo or even just bare infinitive. None is wrong.
- **Form collision with futuro do subjuntivo is the highest-error point.** Disambiguate by trigger word: *para / sem / antes de / é importante* → personal infinitive. *quando / assim que / se* → futuro do subjuntivo. The forms are identical for many verbs; the trigger is the only signal.
- **Don't use personal infinitive after modal verbs.** *Quero falares* is wrong (or marked); use *quero que tu fales* (subjuntivo with overt subject) or *queres falar?* (different question entirely). Modals take bare infinitive when subjects align, subjuntivo with *que* when distinct.
- **Bare-infinitive default in same-subject contexts is universal.** *Vou comer* (I'm going to eat) is right; *vou eu comer* is wrong (the personal ending is redundant when subject is identical to main clause). Personal infinitive's job is to mark distinctness or clarification — when there's nothing to mark, don't inflect.
- **The cross-link to subjuntivo is real, not just a footnote.** See [[b1-subj-trigger-impessoal]] for the subjuntivo path with impersonal expressions. Both paths exist for the same construction frame; mature B2 production includes both.

---

## Unit 127 — Conversational Strategies and Discourse Markers

- Organize ideas in conversation with discourse markers
- Sound more fluent with fillers

- então (so, well then), pois é (yeah, exactly)
- aliás (by the way, actually), além disso (besides, moreover)

- quer dizer (that is to say), ou seja (in other words)
- na verdade (actually, in fact), tipo (like - filler)
- assim (like, sort of), sabe? (you know?)

### Grammar

- **Discourse markers:** words that organize conversation and connect ideas
- **Fillers:** words that give time to think
- **Turn-taking:** how to enter and maintain conversation
- **Repair strategies:** how to clarify and rephrase

## Unit 128 — Conectivos textuais avançados (aditivos, contrastivos, causais, consecutivos, enumerativos, conclusivos)

*Slug: `b2-conectivos-textuais` · Sequence position: 88.5 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `textual-connectives`, `cohesion-coherence`

**Prereqs:** `b1-discourse-markers`, `b2-conj-condicionais`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Use higher-register textual connectives across six categories — additive, contrastive, causal, consecutive, enumerative, conclusive
- Choose connectives appropriate to the register (academic / journalistic / business / informal essay)
- Avoid repetition fatigue by varying connectives within a single text

### Vocabulary

The connective inventory, organized by category. Forms in **bold** are the most-used in formal writing; the rest are register/style alternatives.

### Additives — adding information

- **além disso** — in addition / moreover
- **ademais** — furthermore (more formal)
- **mais ainda** — even more so
- **igualmente** — likewise
- **do mesmo modo / da mesma forma** — in the same way
- **paralelamente** — in parallel
- **bem como** — as well as

### Contrastives — opposing information

- **contudo** — however
- **no entanto** — nevertheless
- **todavia** — yet
- **por outro lado** — on the other hand
- **em contrapartida** — in counterpart / on the other hand
- **ao invés de** — instead of
- **pelo contrário** — on the contrary

### Causals — introducing cause

- **visto que** — given that
- **dado que** — given that (slightly more formal)
- **uma vez que** — once / given that
- **na medida em que** — to the extent that
- **devido a / em virtude de** — due to / by virtue of (with noun phrase)
- **graças a** — thanks to

### Consecutives — introducing consequence

- **por conseguinte** — consequently
- **logo** — therefore (also temporal)
- **portanto** — therefore
- **assim sendo / assim** — thus
- **dessa forma / desse modo** — in this way
- **em consequência (disso)** — as a consequence

### Enumeratives — ordering points

- **em primeiro lugar / primeiramente** — firstly
- **em segundo lugar** — secondly
- **a seguir / em seguida** — next
- **por último / finalmente** — finally / lastly
- **por fim** — at the end / lastly

### Conclusives — summarizing

- **em suma** — in sum
- **em síntese** — in synthesis
- **em conclusão** — in conclusion
- **em resumo** — in short
- **enfim** — in short / finally (mid-discourse marker)
- **resumindo** — to summarize

### Grammar

These connectives operate at the **text level** — they organize multi-sentence or multi-paragraph flow rather than connecting single clauses. Most function as parenthetical adverbials and require comma punctuation.

### Standard punctuation pattern

A connective opening a sentence usually takes a comma after:

- *Além disso, é necessário considerar a opinião dos especialistas.*
- *Contudo, a evidência aponta noutra direção.*
- *Em primeiro lugar, devemos definir o problema.*

A connective inserted mid-sentence typically takes commas around:

- *A evidência, contudo, aponta noutra direção.*
- *Devemos, em primeiro lugar, definir o problema.*

### Register match

Connectives carry register weight. Mixing high-formal connectives with informal style sounds incongruous:

| Register | Typical connective set |
|---|---|
| Casual essay | mas, então, e, depois, no fim |
| Academic / formal | além disso, contudo, por conseguinte, em síntese |
| Journalistic | no entanto, por outro lado, em consequência |
| Business correspondence | adicionalmente, em contrapartida, por fim |

A formal essay reaching for *então* repeatedly sounds underdressed; a casual blog post over-using *por conseguinte* sounds pretentious.

### Avoiding repetition fatigue

Within a single text, vary connectives across categories. Don't stack three *contudo*s in three sentences — use *no entanto*, *por outro lado*, or restructure.

### Exemplar paragraph (mid-formal)

> *A inovação tecnológica trouxe enormes ganhos de produtividade. **Além disso**, criou novos mercados de trabalho que não existiam há uma década. **Contudo**, a transição também produziu perdas significativas em setores tradicionais. **Por conseguinte**, qualquer política pública nesta área deve equilibrar inovação e proteção social. **Em suma**, o desafio é económico e ético ao mesmo tempo.*

The five connectives mark text structure cleanly: addition (além disso) → contrast (contudo) → consequence (por conseguinte) → conclusion (em suma).

### Drills & artifacts

- Cross-link: see [[b1-discourse-markers]] for the foundation discourse-marker set (this unit extends it).
- Cross-link: see [[b2-conj-condicionais]] for conditional conjunctions (which overlap with contrastive/causal connectives at the clause level).

<!-- TODO: build a category-classification drill (given a connective, identify category). Build a register-matching drill (given a text register, pick appropriate connectives). Build a repetition-avoidance drill (rewrite a paragraph that over-uses one connective). -->

### Traps

- **Don't mix register.** *Então, podemos concluir que…* sounds informal in academic writing — use *Por conseguinte* or *Portanto*. Conversely, *por conseguinte* in a personal email sounds stiff.
- **Don't over-use one connective.** Three *contudo*s in three sentences signals a mechanical writer. Vary across category-mates (*no entanto, por outro lado, todavia*) or restructure to remove some.
- **Punctuation matters.** Connectives are parenthetical — comma after when sentence-initial, commas around when mid-sentence. *Além disso* (with the comma) signals "moving to a related point"; without the comma the reader stumbles.
- **Logo has two meanings — temporal and consequential.** *Logo depois* (right after — temporal). *Logo, podemos concluir* (therefore — consequential). Disambiguation by context.
- **Visto que / dado que / uma vez que are causal, NOT temporal.** All three mean "given that" or "since [as cause]" — they don't mark time. Don't substitute for *desde que* (temporal — covered in [[b2-conj-condicionais]]).
- **Bem como is not the same as e (and).** *Bem como* implies "as well as" with a parallel-listing flavor; *e* is the simple coordinator. *X bem como Y* sounds more formal and emphasizes the equivalent status of X and Y. Don't substitute *bem como* for *e* in casual lists.

---

## Unit 129 — Argumentação — estrutura, tese, evidência, refutação, conclusão

*Slug: `b2-argumentacao` · Sequence position: 88.6 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `argumentation`, `subjunctive-triggers`, `conditional-usage`

**Prereqs:** `b1-subj-trigger-impessoal`, `b1-condicional`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Build a structured argument in writing or speech: **thesis → supporting evidence → refutation → conclusion**
- Use formulaic phrases for each move (*defendo que, é evidente que, apesar disso, conclui-se que*)
- Apply appropriate hedging through impersonal subjuntivo and condicional to manage diplomatic tone
- Recognize argument structure when reading opinion pieces, essays, formal speeches

### Vocabulary

The argumentation toolkit, organized by rhetorical move:

### Thesis statement — stating your position

- **defendo que** — I argue that
- **sustento que** — I maintain that
- **considero que** — I consider that
- **na minha perspetiva / na minha opinião** — in my view
- **é minha posição que** — it's my position that
- **acredito firmemente que** — I firmly believe that
- **diria que** — I'd say that (hedged, condicional)

### Supporting evidence — justifying

- **como mostra / como demonstra** — as X shows / demonstrates
- **conforme aponta / segundo** — according to / as X points out
- **a evidência mostra que** — the evidence shows that
- **é evidente que** — it's evident that
- **convém notar que** — it's worth noting that
- **um exemplo claro disso é** — a clear example of this is
- **a este respeito** — in this regard
- **basta lembrar que** — one need only remember that

### Refutation — countering opposing views

- **apesar disso** — despite this
- **contudo** — however
- **é equivocado afirmar que** — it's mistaken to claim that
- **ao contrário do que se pensa** — contrary to what is thought
- **é falso supor que** — it's false to suppose that
- **não procede a ideia de que** — the idea that X is invalid
- **convém esclarecer que** — it's worth clarifying that

### Conclusion — closing the argument

- **em síntese** — in synthesis
- **portanto** — therefore
- **conclui-se que** — it is concluded that
- **podemos concluir que** — we can conclude that
- **em última análise** — in the final analysis
- **em suma** — in sum

### Grammar

Argumentation in Portuguese builds on three structural anchors:

1. **Impersonal subjuntivo** for hedged claims (*é evidente que, convém notar que* + subj)
2. **Condicional simples** for diplomatic positioning (*diria que, seria interessante, parece*)
3. **Textual connectives** (see [[b2-conectivos-textuais]]) for moving between rhetorical moves

### Impersonal subjuntivo — the hedging engine

Argumentation often uses impersonal subjuntivo expressions that present claims as worth-considering rather than asserted-as-fact:

- *Convém notar **que ele tenha** mostrado interesse pelo projeto.* — It's worth noting that he has shown interest. (subj — softer than *convém notar que ele mostrou*)
- *É possível **que isto seja** um erro de cálculo.* — It's possible this is a calculation error.
- *Importa salientar **que a economia esteja** a recuperar lentamente.* — It's important to emphasize that the economy is recovering slowly.

The indicative alternative (*convém notar que ele mostrou*) asserts the proposition as fact; the subjuntivo version (*tenha mostrado*) presents it as a noteworthy possibility. Both are correct; the choice is rhetorical.

See [[b1-subj-trigger-impessoal]] for the underlying subjuntivo-trigger framework.

### Condicional for diplomatic distance

Direct claims (*Acho que ele está errado*) can sound aggressive in formal argumentation. Condicional softens:

- *Diria que essa interpretação é problemática.* — I'd say that interpretation is problematic. (softer than *digo que*)
- *Seria interessante considerar uma perspetiva alternativa.* — It would be interesting to consider an alternative perspective.
- *Poderíamos argumentar que…* — We could argue that…
- *Seria pertinente perguntar se…* — It would be pertinent to ask whether…

Condicional gives the writer plausible deniability and signals openness to other views — essential for academic and policy discourse.

See [[b1-condicional]] for the form anchor.

### Argument structure — a typical paragraph

A well-structured argumentative paragraph typically follows: thesis → support → refutation → conclusion.

> *(Tese)* **Defendo que** a regulação ambiental deve incluir incentivos económicos, não apenas proibições.
>
> *(Apoio)* **A evidência mostra que** sistemas baseados em incentivos têm produzido reduções de emissões superiores às de regulações puramente proibitivas. **Conforme aponta** o relatório do IPCC, países com mecanismos de mercado para o carbono apresentam trajetórias mais sustentáveis.
>
> *(Refutação)* **Contudo**, alguns críticos sustentam que incentivos económicos legitimam a poluição. **Esta posição, no entanto, é equivocada**: o problema não é o mecanismo, mas a sua calibragem.
>
> *(Conclusão)* **Em síntese**, a regulação ambiental moderna deve combinar instrumentos económicos e legais — **diria que** abandonar qualquer dos dois compromete a eficácia da política.

The four moves are clearly marked by their connective frames; the condicional (*diria que*) at the conclusion adds diplomatic finish.

### Refutation patterns

Effective refutation acknowledges the opposing view before countering — agreement-then-pivot is more persuasive than dismissal:

- *É verdade que X tem mérito; **contudo**, Y revela uma limitação importante.*
- *Concordo com a observação inicial; **apesar disso**, a conclusão não se segue.*
- *Embora o argumento pareça plausível à primeira vista, **convém notar que** ele assume…*

The concessive opening (*É verdade que / Embora / Concordo*) signals fair engagement; the contrastive turn (*contudo / apesar disso / convém notar que*) carries the actual refutation.

### Exemplar phrases — production-ready

- *Defendo que esta política produz mais danos do que benefícios.*
- *Convém notar que existem alternativas viáveis.*
- *Apesar disso, a maioria das evidências aponta na direção oposta.*
- *Conclui-se que precisamos repensar a abordagem.*
- *Diria que a evidência ainda é inconclusiva.*
- *Seria pertinente investigar mais antes de tomar uma posição firme.*

### Drills & artifacts

- Cross-link: see [[b1-subj-trigger-impessoal]] for the impersonal-subjuntivo trigger set.
- Cross-link: see [[b1-condicional]] for the condicional form anchor.
- Cross-link: see [[b2-conectivos-textuais]] for the connective inventory used in argument structure.

<!-- TODO: build a rhetorical-move identification drill (given a sentence, identify whether it's thesis / support / refutation / conclusion). Build a hedging drill (rewrite assertive sentences with subjuntivo or condicional softening). -->

### Traps

- **Weak hedging in formal writing.** Direct assertions in argumentation sound aggressive: *Ele está errado* in academic writing reads as overstated. Use *parece-me que se equivoca* or *seria mais preciso afirmar que…*. Hedging signals scholarly humility.
- **Overstating evidence.** *Ficou provado que* (it was proven that) overcommits unless you have a definitive proof. Use *a evidência aponta que* (the evidence indicates that) for findings that are well-supported but not proof-level.
- **Refutation without acknowledgment.** Jumping straight to *Esta ideia é falsa* alienates readers. Effective refutation: *É compreensível pensar que X; contudo, a evidência aponta noutra direção.* Acknowledge first, refute second.
- **Wrong-register argumentation phrases.** *Eu acho que sim* in a formal essay sounds undergraduate; use *Considero que / Defendo que / Sustento que*. Same pivot in reverse: *Defendo que* in casual conversation is bombastic.
- **Connective monoculture.** A page-long argument using only *contudo* and *além disso* fatigues. Vary across category-mates and rhetorical moves.
- **Ad-hominem trap (universal pitfall).** Don't refute the opposing view by criticizing the person who holds it. *X afirma A, mas X é incompetente* is rhetorically and logically weak. Engage the argument, not the arguer.

---

## Unit 130 — Coesão e coerência textual (referência, substituição, encadeamento)

*Slug: `b2-coesao` · Sequence position: 88.7 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `cohesion-coherence`

**Prereqs:** `b1-relativo-que`, `b1-discourse-markers`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Use **pronominal reference**, **lexical chains**, and **demonstrative back-reference** to maintain text flow without repetition
- Apply **theme-rheme** progression (given-information first, new-information second) at sentence and paragraph level
- Write paragraphs with strong **topic sentences** and clear thematic progression
- Identify cohesion failures (pronoun ambiguity, paragraph drift, lexical repetition) in their own and others' writing

### Vocabulary

The cohesion toolkit:

### Pronominal reference

- Subject pronouns (often elided): ele, ela, eles, elas
- Object pronouns: o, a, os, as, lhe, lhes
- Reflexive: se
- Demonstrative back-reference: este, esse, aquele (closer ↔ farther in discourse distance)

### Lexical chains

- Synonyms: *casa / habitação / residência / lar*
- Hyponyms / hypernyms: *gato → animal → ser vivo*
- Periphrases: *o autor → o escritor → o nosso interlocutor*

### Discourse markers (transitional)

See [[b1-discourse-markers]] for the foundational set; see [[b2-conectivos-textuais]] for the extended formal-register set.

### Connectives flagging text moves

- **a este respeito** — in this regard
- **além do que foi dito** — beyond what's been said
- **voltando ao ponto** — returning to the point
- **como referido anteriormente** — as mentioned earlier

### Grammar

Cohesion is the **surface-level binding** of a text — the pronouns, connectives, and lexical relations that show which elements are "linked." Coherence is the **deep-level logical sense** — the underlying argument or narrative that makes the text feel like one thing rather than scattered sentences.

Strong texts have both. A text can be cohesive (lots of *este, ele, contudo*) without being coherent (the underlying logic doesn't hold). And a text can be coherent (clear logic) without being well-cohered (sounds like a list of disconnected facts).

### Pronominal reference — antecedent management

The first job of pronouns is to refer back to a previously mentioned entity. The reader must be able to identify the antecedent without ambiguity:

> *(Ambiguous)* O João visitou o Pedro. Ele estava cansado.
>
> Who was tired? Both *João* and *Pedro* are possible antecedents for *ele*. The reader has no way to choose.
>
> *(Disambiguated)* O João visitou o Pedro. **O João** estava cansado da viagem.
>
> Repeating the noun resolves ambiguity at the cost of repetition. Better:
>
> *(Restructured)* Cansado da viagem, o João visitou o Pedro.
>
> The structure puts cause and action in one clause, eliminating the ambiguous pronoun.

When a pronoun has multiple grammatically-possible antecedents and the discourse doesn't disambiguate, restructure the sentence — don't rely on context.

### Subject elision and recovery

Portuguese routinely drops subject pronouns when the verb form makes the subject clear (covered in [[a1-pro-drop]]). In long stretches of text, subject elision builds chains:

> *A Maria chegou cedo. Foi à cozinha. Preparou o café. Bebeu sentada à janela.*

Four sentences, one subject (Maria), explicitly stated only in the first. The verb forms (*chegou, foi, preparou, bebeu*) maintain the subject through morphology. This works when there's no competing subject in the discourse window.

When a competing subject enters, restate explicitly:

> *A Maria chegou cedo. **O João** já estava na cozinha. **Ele** preparou o café e **a Maria** bebeu sentada à janela.*

### Demonstrative back-reference

The three-way demonstrative system (este / esse / aquele) carries discourse-distance information:

- **este / esta / isto** — about to be mentioned, or just mentioned
- **esse / essa / isso** — already mentioned, perhaps not most recently
- **aquele / aquela / aquilo** — mentioned earlier in discourse, more distant

In writing:

- *A questão é a seguinte: **isto** é um problema técnico ou político?* (*isto* points forward to the upcoming clause)
- *Acabei de explicar a regra. **Isso** é o ponto principal.* (*isso* points back to what was just said)
- *Falávamos do projeto X há semanas; **aquele** projeto teve consequências imprevistas.* (*aquele* refers to a more distant discourse referent)

See [[a2-dem-avancados]] for the discourse-and-temporal use of demonstratives.

### Lexical chains — avoiding repetition

A well-cohered text varies its lexical references to the same entity:

> *O autor publicou o livro em 2020. **A obra** tornou-se um best-seller. **O texto** foi traduzido em vinte línguas. **Esta produção** consagrou **o escritor** internacionalmente.*

Five references to the same conceptual entity (the book and its author), each varied: *o livro → a obra → o texto → esta produção → o escritor*. The variation creates lexical density without exhaustion.

The opposite — repetition fatigue — wears the reader out:

> *O autor publicou o livro. O livro tornou-se best-seller. O livro foi traduzido. O autor ficou famoso por o livro.*

### Theme-rheme progression

Sentences typically follow a **given → new** information pattern. The theme (left side) is the known/given information; the rheme (right side) is the new information. Successive sentences chain by promoting the previous rheme to the new theme:

> *(Theme: a economia portuguesa) (Rheme: cresceu 3% em 2024). (Theme: Esse crescimento) (Rheme: foi liderado pelo turismo). (Theme: O setor do turismo) (Rheme: representa hoje 18% do PIB).*

Each sentence's theme picks up the previous sentence's rheme — the text walks forward by handing off topics in a relay.

### Paragraph topic sentences

A well-organized paragraph opens with a **topic sentence** that announces what the paragraph will cover, and closes with either a conclusion or a transition to the next paragraph. Middle sentences develop the topic.

> *O turismo tem sido o motor da recuperação económica nos últimos anos. Os dados mostram um crescimento de 12% no número de visitantes em 2024. Este aumento concentrou-se sobretudo em Lisboa, Porto e Algarve. Contudo, o setor enfrenta agora desafios de sustentabilidade.*

First sentence: announces topic (turismo as economic driver). Middle sentences: develop with evidence and detail. Final sentence: transitions to the next theme (sustainability challenges).

### Drills & artifacts

- Cross-link: see [[a1-pro-drop]] for subject-elision foundation.
- Cross-link: see [[b1-relativo-que]] for relative-pronoun back-reference.
- Cross-link: see [[a2-dem-avancados]] for demonstrative discourse use.
- Cross-link: see [[b2-conectivos-textuais]] for transitional connectives.

<!-- TODO: build a pronoun-ambiguity drill (given a sentence with potential ambiguity, restructure to disambiguate). Build a lexical-chain drill (rewrite a paragraph that over-repeats one term). Build a topic-sentence drill (given a paragraph body, write the topic sentence). -->

### Traps

- **Pronoun ambiguity is the most common cohesion failure.** When two grammatically-possible antecedents exist, the reader stalls. Restructure rather than relying on context.
- **Paragraph drift.** A paragraph that opens with one topic and ends with another loses readers. Each paragraph should hold one main idea; transitions to new ideas mark new paragraphs.
- **Lexical repetition fatigue.** Repeating *o livro* five times in a paragraph wears down the reader. Vary with synonyms (*a obra, o texto*), pronouns (*ele*), or demonstratives (*esta produção*).
- **Demonstrative confusion.** *Isto* (forward-pointing or just-mentioned), *isso* (mentioned earlier), *aquilo* (more distant) carry discourse-distance information. Substituting one for another shifts meaning. *Falei sobre isto* (this thing I'm about to discuss) vs *Falei sobre isso* (that thing I just discussed) vs *Falei sobre aquilo* (that distant matter from earlier).
- **Theme-rheme breaks.** When successive sentences fail to chain (each starts with brand-new information), the reader can't follow the thread. Promote the previous rheme to the next theme — or signal the topic shift explicitly.
- **Cohesion vs coherence — both required.** A text full of *contudo* and *além disso* but with weak underlying argument feels mechanically constructed. Conversely, a coherent argument with no transitional markers feels jumpy. Both layers need attention.

---

## Unit 131 — Registo académico — vocabulário formal, hedging, citação

*Slug: `b2-academico` · Sequence position: 88.8 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `academic-portuguese`, `argumentation`, `cohesion-coherence`

**Prereqs:** `b2-argumentacao`, `b2-conectivos-textuais`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Recognize the conventions of academic Portuguese: formal vocabulary, third-person convention, passive constructions, nominalization
- Apply **hedging** appropriate to academic claims (impersonal subjuntivo + condicional)
- Use citation phrases (*segundo X, conforme aponta Y, na perspetiva de Z*)
- Avoid informal contractions and personal-conversational register in academic writing
- Recognize BP/EP citation-style differences (Brazilian academic convention vs Portuguese academic convention)

### Vocabulary

### Formal vs informal vocabulary register

Academic Portuguese systematically prefers more Latinate, longer-syllable, lower-frequency vocabulary. A short list of common substitutions:

| Informal | Academic |
|---|---|
| usar | utilizar / empregar |
| ajudar | auxiliar / contribuir para |
| pôr | colocar / posicionar |
| dizer | afirmar / declarar / sustentar |
| achar | considerar / entender |
| começar | iniciar / dar início a |
| acabar | finalizar / concluir |
| mostrar | demonstrar / evidenciar |
| ver | observar / constatar / verificar |
| dar | conceder / atribuir / fornecer |
| pegar | obter / adquirir |
| muito | considerável / significativo / substancial |

Academic vocabulary isn't *better* — it's register-marked. A Master's thesis defending *cheguei à conclusão* sounds correct; the same phrase in a casual blog post would feel overweight. Match register to context.

### Citation phrases — introducing sources

- **segundo X** — according to X
- **conforme aponta X** — as X points out
- **conforme demonstra X** — as X demonstrates
- **na perspetiva de X / no entender de X** — in X's view / understanding
- **como argumenta X** — as X argues
- **X (ano) afirma que…** — X (year) states that… (with parenthetical year)
- **na obra clássica de X** — in X's classic work
- **citação direta**: aspas + (X, ano: pp.) — for direct quotations

### Hedging vocabulary — managing claim strength

- **parece que / aparenta-se que** — it seems that
- **é possível que / é provável que** — it's possible / probable
- **tendencialmente** — tendentially
- **em larga medida** — to a large extent
- **em geral / regra geral** — in general / as a general rule
- **com algumas exceções** — with some exceptions
- **talvez** — perhaps
- **eventualmente** (academic Portuguese: "possibly", not English "eventually") — possibly

### Grammar

Academic Portuguese has identifiable grammatical patterns beyond vocabulary register:

### 1. Third-person convention (no "eu" subject)

Academic prose typically avoids first-person *eu* in favor of:

- Impersonal constructions: *Conclui-se que / Verifica-se que / Constata-se que*
- First-person plural (the editorial "we"): *Argumentamos que / Verificamos que / Pretendemos demonstrar que*
- Nominalization: *Esta análise sugere que…* (instead of *Eu analiso e digo que…*)
- Passive: *Foi observado que…* (instead of *Eu observei que…*)

The *eu*-form sounds undergraduate or memoir-like in formal academic register.

### 2. Passive constructions for objectivity

Active voice: *Os investigadores observaram este fenómeno em 2020.*

Passive voice (academic preference): *Este fenómeno foi observado em 2020.* / *Este fenómeno foi observado pelos investigadores em 2020.*

The passive de-emphasizes the agent and emphasizes the affected entity (the phenomenon). In academic discourse, the entity is often the relevant focus; the agent (researchers) is secondary information.

See [[b1-passiva-ser]] for the full passive system.

### 3. Nominalization — verbs as nouns

Academic prose densifies meaning by converting verbs into nouns:

| Verbal version | Nominalized version |
|---|---|
| *Quando os preços aumentam, o consumo diminui.* | *O aumento dos preços provoca a diminuição do consumo.* |
| *Importa que se discuta o tema.* | *A discussão deste tema é importante.* |
| *Quando se observa o fenómeno cuidadosamente…* | *A observação cuidadosa do fenómeno…* |

Nominalization compresses information into noun phrases that can serve as subjects or objects. It sounds heavier but allows more precise relationships in fewer words.

### 4. Hedging through impersonal subjuntivo

Academic claims are typically presented as worth-considering rather than asserted-as-fact. The impersonal subjuntivo (covered in [[b1-subj-trigger-impessoal]]) is the workhorse:

- *É possível **que esta interpretação esteja** equivocada.* — Hedging the assertion
- *Convém notar **que existam** alternativas viáveis.* — Acknowledging without committing
- *Importa salientar **que o estudo apresente** limitações metodológicas.* — Self-criticism appropriate to academic register

### 5. Condicional for tentative formulations

Condicional (see [[b1-condicional]]) softens claims further:

- *Diria que esta abordagem é problemática.*
- *Seria pertinente investigar mais profundamente.*
- *Poderíamos considerar uma perspetiva alternativa.*
- *A teoria proposta beneficiaria de mais validação empírica.*

### Citation conventions — BP vs EP

Citation styles differ slightly between Brazilian and Portuguese academic conventions:

| Aspect | BP convention | EP convention |
|---|---|---|
| Author-date format | (Silva, 2020) | (Silva, 2020) — similar |
| Direct quote attribution | "..." (Silva, 2020, p. 15) | "..." (Silva, 2020: 15) |
| Footnote vs in-text | More in-text in BP | More footnote use in EP |
| Bibliographic style | ABNT (Brazilian) | various (often APA, ISO) |

For B2 production, follow whichever convention the institution requires. Recognize both when reading.

### Exemplar academic paragraph

> *A análise dos dados sugere que a relação entre crescimento económico e emissões de carbono é mais complexa do que sustenta a literatura clássica. **Verifica-se que** países desenvolvidos apresentam, em larga medida, uma estabilização das emissões mesmo com crescimento contínuo. **Conforme aponta** Silva (2022), este fenómeno deve-se à transição estrutural dos setores económicos, mais do que a políticas ambientais explícitas. **É possível que** a relação se altere em economias emergentes, **embora** os dados disponíveis ainda **sejam** inconclusivos. **Diria que** uma investigação longitudinal seria pertinente.*

The paragraph combines: nominalization (*A análise dos dados*), impersonal verbs (*verifica-se*), citation (*conforme aponta*), hedging subjuntivo (*é possível que se altere*, *embora sejam*), condicional (*diria que, seria pertinente*).

### Drills & artifacts

- Cross-link: see [[b2-argumentacao]] for argumentation toolkit (academic register builds on it).
- Cross-link: see [[b2-conectivos-textuais]] for the formal connective inventory.
- Cross-link: see [[b1-passiva-ser]] for the passive constructions central to academic register.
- Cross-link: see [[b1-subj-trigger-impessoal]] for the hedging subjuntivo.
- Cross-link: see [[b1-condicional]] for the tentative-formulation condicional.

<!-- TODO: build a register-elevation drill (rewrite a casual paragraph in academic register, swapping vocabulary, voice, and hedge level). Build a citation-formatting drill (BP vs EP conventions). -->

### Traps

- **Informal contractions sneaking in.** *tá / tô / pra* in academic writing immediately mark the register as inappropriate. Always *está / estou / para* in formal text.
- **Over-hedging or under-hedging.** Too many *é possível que / talvez / parece que* in succession sounds evasive — the reader can't tell what the writer believes. Too few sounds dogmatic — the writer overcommits to claims that should be qualified. Balance.
- **First-person *eu* in academic writing.** Generally avoid; use first-person plural (*argumentamos que*) or impersonal (*conclui-se que*). Some disciplines (especially in BP) increasingly accept *eu* in qualitative research; check journal conventions.
- **Eventualmente means "possibly", NOT "eventually".** *Eventualmente teremos uma resposta* in EP/BP academic prose means "we might possibly have an answer", not "in the end we'll have an answer." False friend with English.
- **Citation-style mixing.** A single text shouldn't mix Brazilian (Silva, 2020, p. 15) and Portuguese (Silva, 2020: 15) conventions. Pick one and apply consistently.
- **Nominalization overdose.** *A nominalização excessiva da expressão verbal causa a densificação da prosa académica para além do limite da legibilidade.* — Technically correct, but the cascade of noun phrases is exhausting. Use nominalization to compress, not to obscure.

---

## Unit 132 — Registo mediático e empresarial — convenções formuláicas, vocabulário, salutações

*Slug: `b2-registro-midia-empresarial` · Sequence position: 88.9 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `business-portuguese`, `media-current-events`, `register-formal-informal`

**Prereqs:** `b2-conectivos-textuais`, `b2-bp-ep-vocabulario-regional`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Read and produce **media texts** (news headlines, news ledes, opinion pieces) using the conventional reporting verbs and compressed-syntax patterns
- Read and produce **business correspondence** (letters, emails, reports) using formulaic salutations, sign-offs, and corporate vocabulary
- Recognize the **BP/EP divergences** in business-letter conventions (salutations, sign-offs, vocabulary)
- Avoid register-inversion errors (formal patterns in casual contexts and vice versa)

### Vocabulary

### News reporting verbs

The journalistic register has a stylized inventory of verbs for reporting speech acts:

| Verb | Connotation |
|---|---|
| **afirmar** | to state, assert |
| **declarar** | to declare (formal/official) |
| **sustentar** | to maintain / argue |
| **defender** | to defend a position |
| **anunciar** | to announce |
| **revelar** | to reveal (often with new-information undertone) |
| **garantir** | to guarantee / assure |
| **negar** | to deny |
| **rejeitar** | to reject |
| **refutar** | to refute / counter |
| **alertar para** | to warn about |
| **chamar a atenção para** | to draw attention to |
| **frisar / sublinhar** | to emphasize / underline |

These reporting verbs replace the bland *disse* / *falou* in formal news writing. *O ministro disse* sounds informal/casual; *O ministro afirmou* / *declarou* / *sustentou* sounds journalistically appropriate.

### Headline conventions — compressed syntax

News headlines compress syntax aggressively:

- **Articles dropped**: *(O) Presidente anuncia novas medidas* → *Presidente anuncia novas medidas*
- **Verb dropped (with implied "ser/estar")**: *(É) Crise económica em três frentes* → *Crise económica em três frentes*
- **Present-tense reporting of past events**: *Banco central sobe juros* (the rate hike happened today, but reported in present)
- **Colon to introduce attribution or topic**: *Crise: governo prepara plano de emergência*

These compressions are headline-specific. The article body returns to standard grammar.

### Business-letter formulas

Standard salutation and sign-off conventions for formal business correspondence:

#### Salutations (opening)

| Context | BP convention | EP convention |
|---|---|---|
| Generic formal | *Prezado(a) Sr.(a)…* | *Exmo.(a) Sr.(a)…* |
| Named recipient | *Prezado Sr. Silva* | *Exmo. Sr. Silva* |
| Less formal (known recipient) | *Caro(a) [nome]* | *Caro(a) [nome]* (shared) |
| Plural / unknown recipient | *Prezados Senhores* | *Exmos. Senhores* |

The BP *Prezado* and EP *Exmo. (Excelentíssimo)* differ — direct transfer between variants sounds odd.

#### Sign-offs (closing)

| Register | BP convention | EP convention |
|---|---|---|
| Standard formal | *Atenciosamente,* | *Com os melhores cumprimentos,* / *Atenciosamente,* |
| Slightly more personal | *Cordialmente,* | *Cordialmente,* (shared) |
| Letter close (informal) | *Abraço,* / *Um abraço,* | *Um abraço,* (shared) |

EP *Com os melhores cumprimentos* is the canonical formal sign-off; BP rarely uses this phrase in business letters (it would sound translated or stilted).

#### Body-text formulas

- **Opening reference**: *Em referência ao seu email de [data]* / *Reportando-me ao seu email…* (EP) / *Em resposta ao seu email…*
- **Attaching documents**: *Segue em anexo…* / *Anexo encontra…* (EP) / *Encaminho em anexo…* (BP)
- **Requesting**: *Solicitamos a gentileza de…* / *Agradecemos que…* / *Pedimos que…*
- **Confirming receipt**: *Confirmamos a receção do seu email* (EP) / *Confirmamos o recebimento do seu email* (BP)

### Corporate vocabulary

Modern business Portuguese has accumulated formulaic phrases — many translated from English management-speak:

- **alinhar expectativas** — to align expectations
- **agregar valor** — to add value
- **dar follow-up / fazer follow-up** — to follow up (often used in English even in Portuguese contexts)
- **brainstorming** — same in Portuguese
- **stakeholder** — usually kept in English; sometimes *parte interessada*
- **a curto / médio / longo prazo** — short/medium/long term
- **margem de manobra** — room to maneuver
- **prestar contas** — to be accountable / report back

These phrases are register-marked: they signal "I work in a professional environment" and would sound incongruous in casual conversation.

### Grammar

The media + business register doesn't introduce new grammar so much as it **selects** specific constructions from the standard inventory:

### 1. Passive voice for reporting

News-style reporting often uses passive constructions to depersonalize:

- *Foi anunciado que… / Foi confirmado que…*
- *O acordo foi assinado pelas duas partes.*
- *O projeto foi rejeitado pelo conselho.*

See [[b1-passiva-ser]] for the passive system.

### 2. Impersonal-se for generic reporting

The passive-se construction (see [[b1-passiva-se]]) appears in news-style generic statements:

- *Discutiu-se a proposta no parlamento.*
- *Procura-se solução para o impasse.*
- *Investiga-se a origem do incidente.*

### 3. Condicional for attributed claims (Conditional reporting)

When reporting unverified claims, journalistic Portuguese uses condicional to mark the claim as not-yet-confirmed:

- *Segundo fontes, o ministro **teria** participado da reunião.* — According to sources, the minister allegedly participated. (the *teria* signals attribution, not confirmation)
- *O presidente **teria** dito que…* — The president allegedly said that…

This use of condicional ("conditional reporting") is a well-defined journalistic convention. A reader interprets the *teria* as "according to the source, but unverified."

### 4. Subjuntivo for editorial / opinion register

Opinion-piece writing leans on impersonal subjuntivo for editorial commentary:

- *É lamentável que se tenha chegado a este ponto.*
- *Importa que o governo aja com rapidez.*
- *Convém recordar que existem alternativas.*

### Exemplar texts

**News headline:**
> *Banco central sobe juros: economia em retração no terceiro trimestre*

(Compressed syntax, present-tense reporting of recent events, colon introducing topic.)

**News lede:**
> *O Banco Central de Portugal anunciou ontem uma subida dos juros de referência em 0,25 pontos percentuais. A decisão, segundo o comunicado, visa controlar a inflação que se mantém acima da meta. Analistas alertam para o risco de retração do consumo.*

(Reporting verb *anunciou*, attribution *segundo o comunicado*, impersonal *se mantém*, journalistic verb *alertar para*.)

**Business email opening (BP):**
> *Prezado Sr. Silva,*
>
> *Em resposta ao seu email de ontem, confirmamos o recebimento dos documentos solicitados. Encaminhamos em anexo o relatório atualizado.*

**Business email opening (EP):**
> *Exmo. Sr. Silva,*
>
> *Reportando-me ao seu email de ontem, confirmo a receção dos documentos solicitados. Segue em anexo o relatório atualizado.*

(Note the salutation difference, the *recebimento* / *receção* vocabulary divergence, and the slightly different opening phrases.)

**Business email sign-off (EP):**
> *Com os melhores cumprimentos,*
> *[Nome]*

**Business email sign-off (BP):**
> *Atenciosamente,*
> *[Nome]*

### Drills & artifacts

- Cross-link: see [[b2-conectivos-textuais]] for the connective inventory used in news/business prose.
- Cross-link: see [[b2-bp-ep-vocabulario-regional]] for the BP/EP vocabulary divergences relevant to business writing.
- Cross-link: see [[b1-passiva-ser]] and [[b1-passiva-se]] for the passive constructions central to news reporting.
- Cross-link: see [[b1-condicional]] for the conditional-reporting convention.

<!-- TODO: build a salutation-translation drill (BP <-> EP business letter openings and sign-offs). Build a headline-decompression drill (given a compressed headline, write the full sentence). Build a register-classification drill (given a sentence, identify whether it fits news / business / casual). -->

### Traps

- **Don't translate English business clichés literally.** *Touch base* doesn't translate well; use *contactar* or *entrar em contacto*. *Reach out* is similarly awkward in literal translation; use *contactar* or *enviar uma mensagem a*.
- **Salutation register matters.** Using EP *Exmo.* in a BP business letter sounds pompous; using BP *Prezado* in an EP business letter sounds Brazilian-translated. Match the variant of the recipient.
- **Conditional reporting is not the same as personal hedging.** *O ministro teria dito* (he allegedly said — journalistic attribution) ≠ *Eu diria que* (I'd say — personal hedge). Both use condicional but in different rhetorical positions.
- **Headline compression doesn't transfer to body text.** *Presidente anuncia* in a headline is fine; in the article body, restore articles: *O presidente anunciou…*
- **Don't over-use management-speak vocabulary.** *Vamos alinhar expectativas para agregar valor às margens de manobra dos stakeholders* is technically grammatical but signals jargon-overload. Use formulaic phrases sparingly and substantively.
- **BP/EP vocabulary divergence is sharpest in business contexts.** *Recebimento* (BP) vs *receção* (EP), *encaminhar* (BP-leaning for forwarding) vs *enviar* (more shared). When writing for an audience of unknown variant, lean toward shared vocabulary.
- **Reporting verb register match.** *Disse* in news writing is too informal — use *afirmou, declarou, sustentou*. But also: don't overload one piece with stylized verbs (*o presidente sustentou, o ministro defendeu, o porta-voz declarou, o analista alertou para…*) — vary including occasional plain *disse* or paraphrase.

---

## Unit 133 — Advanced Por/Para and Idiomatic Expressions

*Slug: `b2-por-para-avancado` · Sequence position: 89.0 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `por-vs-para`, `preposition-collocations`, `idioms-proverbs`

### Outcomes

- Use advanced por/para expressions naturally
- Distinguish subtle meanings (estar por vs estar para)
- Use common idioms with por/para
- Understand regional BP/EP differences

### Vocabulary

- por acaso (by chance), por exemplo (for example)
- por enquanto (for now), por via das dúvidas (just in case)
- estar por (to be about to), estar para (to be about to)
- por aí (around there), por aqui (around here)
- para sempre (forever), para variar (for a change)
- de vez em quando (from time to time)

### Grammar

- **Advanced por/para:** idiomatic expressions and fixed phrases
- **Subtle distinctions:** estar por vs estar para
- **Regional variations:** BP vs EP usage differences

### Exemplar sentences

- Por favor, me ajude. (Please help me.)
- Estou estudando há duas horas, por isso estou cansado. (I've been studying for two hours, that's why I'm tired.)
- Ele não está nem aí para o trabalho. (He doesn't care about work at all.)
- Está para chover. (It's about to rain.)
- Estou por fazer isso ainda. (I still need to do that.)
- De vez em quando, eu viajo. (From time to time, I travel.)
- Vou embora por volta das 5. (I'm leaving around 5.)

## Unit 134 — BP vs EP — pronomes pessoais e formas de tratamento

*Slug: `b2-bp-ep-pronomes-tratamento` · Sequence position: 89.5 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `bp-vs-ep-distinctions`, `personal-pronouns`, `register-formal-informal`

**Prereqs:** `a1-pron-voce-bp`, `a1-pron-tu-ep`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Map any 2nd-person address form (*tu, você, o senhor, a senhora*) to its register and variant
- Read or write in either variant with appropriate pronoun choice for the social context
- Recognize the **register inversion** of *você* — informal/default in BP, formal/distant in EP — and avoid the resulting cross-variant errors

### Vocabulary

The 2nd-person address landscape in modern Portuguese:

| Pronoun | BP register | EP register |
|---|---|---|
| **tu** | rare (regional, far South / Northeast) | informal default |
| **você** | informal default | formal / distant |
| **o senhor / a senhora** | very formal | very formal |
| **vocês** | 2nd-person plural (all registers) | 2nd-person plural (all registers) |
| **vós** | extinct in modern speech | extinct in modern speech |

### Grammar

### The você inversion

This is the single highest-leverage BP/EP difference for any learner switching tracks:

- **In BP**: *você* is the **default informal** form. You use *você* with friends, family, peers, children, strangers your own age. *O senhor / a senhora* is reserved for formal/respectful contexts (older strangers, professional registers, very formal letters).
- **In EP**: *você* is **formal/distant**. With friends and family you use *tu*. *Você* enters when there's professional distance, age difference without intimacy, or a deliberate signal of respect-and-distance. *O senhor / a senhora* is super-formal.

Direct cross-variant transfer fails:
- A BP speaker using *você* with new EP friends sounds **cold/distant**, not friendly.
- An EP speaker hearing BP *você* may parse it as inappropriately formal — the BP intent of casual friendliness misreads.

### Conjugation correlate

Each pronoun selects a verb-form pattern:

| Pronoun | Verb form | Example |
|---|---|---|
| tu | 2nd-person singular (-s ending) | *Tu **falas** português?* |
| você (BP or EP) | 3rd-person singular | *Você **fala** português?* |
| o senhor / a senhora | 3rd-person singular | *O senhor **fala** português?* |

For a student writing in EP, the practical rule: switching from *tu* to *você* keeps the verb form same as switching to *o senhor*. The verb cues address-distance via grammatical 3rd person, while *tu* keeps you in 2nd person.

### Imperatives

Imperative forms diverge by pronoun choice:

| Address | Affirmative imperative | Negative imperative |
|---|---|---|
| tu (EP) | *Fala!* (bare 3sg pres ind) | *Não fales!* (subjuntivo presente 2sg) |
| você (BP and EP) | *Fale!* (subjuntivo presente 3sg) | *Não fale!* (subjuntivo presente 3sg) |

A BP speaker sees only the *você*-imperative form day-to-day; an EP speaker uses both depending on who's being addressed. See `a2-imperativo-bp` and `a2-imperativo-ep` for full paradigms.

### Vós is dead — historical note

Both modern variants have lost productive use of *vós* (the 2nd-person plural informal). Some grammar tables still list *vós* paradigms (*vós sois, vós tendes*) but no native speaker uses these in everyday speech. The 2nd-person plural is now *vocês* in both variants, regardless of register.

Encounters with *vós* in modern texts are typically:
- Liturgical / religious language (especially in Catholic prayers)
- Law / formal proclamations
- Literary or poetic register
- Quotations from older texts

### Exemplar contrasts

- BP: *Você quer um café?* (asking a friend) → EP equivalent: *Queres um café?* (tu, no pronoun shown — natural in EP)
- BP: *O senhor pode me ajudar?* (asking an older stranger) → EP equivalent: *(O senhor) pode ajudar-me?* / *Pode ajudar-me?* (similar register, similar form)
- BP: *Vocês vão à festa?* (asking a group) → EP equivalent: *Vocês vão à festa?* (identical — *vocês* shared)

### Drills & artifacts

- Cross-link: see [[a1-pron-voce-bp]] and [[a1-pron-tu-ep]] for the full per-variant pronoun introductions.
- Cross-link: see [[a2-imperativo-bp]] and [[a2-imperativo-ep]] for the imperative-system divergence.

<!-- TODO: build a register-inversion drill — given a context (friends / strangers / elders / professional) and a target variant (BP / EP), pick the appropriate pronoun. Especially target the você-register inversion. -->

### Traps

- **The você inversion is the #1 cross-variant error.** A BP-trained student moving to EP must consciously substitute *tu* for *você* in friend/family contexts. An EP-trained student moving to BP must accept that *você* is now warm and unmarked.
- **Don't over-correct toward *tu* in BP.** While some BP regions (Rio Grande do Sul, parts of the Northeast) use *tu* productively, the standard urban BP has lost it. A BP speaker hearing *tu* outside those regions parses it as either regional, archaic, or affected. Don't import EP *tu* habits into BP production.
- **The *o senhor / a senhora* form requires actually saying it.** Unlike *tu* / *você*, which can be dropped (verb agreement carries the reference), *o senhor / a senhora* is typically explicit — dropping it loses the register marker. *O senhor pode me ajudar?* (right) vs *Pode me ajudar?* (drops the senhor — register weakens).
- **Vós is a recognition target.** Recognize it in liturgy, law, literature. Don't produce it in conversation — it sounds either reverent (in religious contexts) or absurd (in casual ones).
- **Plural vocês is a register-flattener.** With a group of friends in EP, *vocês* is the natural form (no plural-tu equivalent in modern use). The intimacy that *tu* expresses is lost in plural — both variants are equally flat at the 2nd-plural level.

---

## Unit 135 — BP vs EP — colocação clítica e usos divergentes de tempos verbais

*Slug: `b2-bp-ep-clitica-tempos` · Sequence position: 89.6 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `bp-vs-ep-distinctions`, `object-pronouns`, `conditional-usage`, `register-formal-informal`

**Prereqs:** `a2-reflexivos-bp`, `a2-reflexivos-ep`, `a2-dop-bp`, `a2-dop-ep`, `a2-iop-bp`, `a2-iop-ep`, `a2-estar-gerundio-bp`, `a2-estar-a-infinitivo-ep`, `b1-condicional-bp`, `b1-condicional-ep`, `b1-pret-perfeito-composto-bp`, `b1-pret-perfeito-composto-ep`, `b2-cond-irreal-bp`, `b2-cond-irreal-ep`, `b2-cond-contra-bp`, `b2-cond-contra-ep`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Map the five major BP/EP grammatical-divergence dimensions side-by-side: clitic placement, progressive aspect, *tenho falado* register, Type-2 conditional substitution, Type-3 conditional substitution
- Read a passage and identify the variant from clitic placement and tense choice alone
- Switch production register between variants without carrying over wrong-variant patterns

### Vocabulary

The five divergence dimensions, with the canonical contrast pair for each:

| Dimension | BP form | EP form |
|---|---|---|
| Clitic placement (default) | proclisis (*me chamo*) | enclisis (*chamo-me*) |
| Progressive aspect | *estar + gerúndio* (*estou falando*) | *estar a + infinitivo* (*estou a falar*) |
| *Tenho falado* | requires recency anchor (*tenho ido ultimamente*) | free-standing (*tenho ido*) |
| Type-2 conditional | condicional simples (*viajaria*) | imperfeito do indicativo (*viajava*) — colloquial |
| Type-3 conditional | condicional composto (*teria passado*) | mais-que-perfeito do indicativo (*tinha passado*) — colloquial |

### Grammar

### Dimension 1 — Clitic placement

The single sharpest BP/EP divergence in syntax. **EP defaults to enclisis; BP defaults to proclisis** in spoken language. The trigger words that force proclisis (negação, conjunções subordinativas, advérbios de inclusão, pronomes interrogativos / relativos / indefinidos) are the same in both variants — but the unmarked default differs:

- BP: *Eu **me chamo** João.* (proclisis even with no trigger)
- EP: *Chamo-me João.* (enclisis is default)
- Both: *Não **me chamo** João.* (proclisis triggered by *não* in both variants)

Mesoclisis (*chamar-me-ei*) survives in formal EP, dead in BP.

See [[a2-reflexivos-bp]], [[a2-reflexivos-ep]], [[a2-dop-bp]], [[a2-dop-ep]], [[a2-iop-bp]], [[a2-iop-ep]] for full per-variant detail.

### Dimension 2 — Progressive aspect

Same meaning, two structurally different constructions:

- BP: *Estou **falando** com ela.* — I'm speaking with her.
- EP: *Estou **a falar** com ela.* — Same meaning.

The construction is identical across all tenses (estava + gerúndio / estava a + infinitivo, estarei + gerúndio / estarei a + infinitivo, etc.).

Geographic note: some EP regions (Alentejo, Azores) historically used the gerund; standard EP (Lisbon norm) uses *estar a + infinitivo*. BP universally uses the gerund.

See [[a2-estar-gerundio-bp]] and [[a2-estar-a-infinitivo-ep]].

### Dimension 3 — Pretérito perfeito composto register

Same form (*tenho + particípio*), divergent natural-usage pattern:

| Form | BP reading | EP reading |
|---|---|---|
| *Tenho falado.* | sounds incomplete; needs *ultimamente* | natural — "I've been speaking [recently]" |
| *Tenho falado ultimamente.* | habitual recent action | same meaning, adverb optional |

A BP speaker hearing free-standing *tenho falado* parses it as somewhat formal/EP-flavored. An EP speaker hearing *tenho falado ultimamente* finds the adverb redundant.

See [[b1-pret-perfeito-composto-bp]] and [[b1-pret-perfeito-composto-ep]].

### Dimension 4 — Type-2 conditional substitution

Type 2 (irreal present/future) main clause:

| Variant | Standard form | Substitute |
|---|---|---|
| BP | *Se eu fosse rico, **viajaria**.* | (no substitute) |
| EP formal | *Se eu fosse rico, **viajaria**.* | — |
| EP colloquial | *Se eu fosse rico, **viajava**.* | imperfeito do indicativo |

Both EP forms are productive native usage. The substitution is broad (applies across most verbs in colloquial EP) but specifically excludes the *se*-clause (which stays imperfeito subjuntivo: *se fosse*, never *se era*).

See [[b2-cond-irreal-bp]] and [[b2-cond-irreal-ep]].

### Dimension 5 — Type-3 conditional substitution

Same register split, different verb forms:

| Variant | Standard form | Substitute |
|---|---|---|
| BP | *Se eu tivesse estudado, **teria passado**.* | (no substitute) |
| EP formal | *Se eu tivesse estudado, **teria passado**.* | — |
| EP colloquial | *Se eu tivesse estudado, **tinha passado**.* | mais-que-perfeito do indicativo |

A BP speaker hearing *tinha passado* in this context parses it as past pluperfect (he had passed — strange) and may not recognize it as a conditional substitute. An EP speaker hears it as natural Type-3 result clause.

See [[b2-cond-contra-bp]] and [[b2-cond-contra-ep]].

### Dimension 6 (auxiliary) — Polite-request register

Smaller divergence, but real: EP uses imperfeito-de-cortesia substitution more pervasively than BP, especially for the high-frequency request set (*queria, gostava, podia, devia*).

- BP polite: *Eu **queria** um café.* (also *Eu **gostaria** de um café*)
- EP polite: *Eu **queria** um café.* (essentially mandatory; *quereria* is prescriptively correct but practically dead)

See [[b1-condicional-bp]] and [[b1-condicional-ep]].

### Identifying variant from a passage

Quick diagnostic: look for clitic placement first.

- *Eu te ligo amanhã.* → BP (proclisis with no trigger)
- *Ligo-te amanhã.* → EP (enclisis as default)
- *Estou trabalhando muito.* → BP (gerund)
- *Estou a trabalhar muito.* → EP (a + infinitive)
- *Se pudesse, ia.* → likely EP (Type-2 imperfeito substitution)
- *Se pudesse, iria.* → BP, or formal EP
- *Tenho lido este livro.* → likely EP (no recency anchor)
- *Tenho lido este livro ultimamente.* → could be either

### Drills & artifacts

- Cross-link: see all 16 prereq units for per-dimension detail.

<!-- TODO: build a variant-identification drill — given a paragraph, identify clitic placement, tense choices, and progressive form to determine variant. Build a same-content-different-variant drill — translate a BP passage into EP equivalents (and vice versa) using the divergence dimensions. -->

### Traps

- **Don't import wrong-variant clitic placement.** A BP-trained student writing EP and forgetting to switch to enclisis sounds Brazilian-on-paper. An EP-trained student speaking BP and using enclisis sounds bookish. Both errors are register-marked.
- **Gerund vs *a +* infinitive isn't optional.** *Estou falando* in EP sounds Brazilian; *Estou a falar* in BP sounds Portuguese. The forms aren't interchangeable for naturalness, only for grammar.
- **The Type 2/3 substitution applies ONLY to the main clause.** The *se*-clause stays imperfeito subjuntivo (Type 2) or mais-que-perfeito subjuntivo (Type 3) in both variants. *Se eu era rico* is wrong in any variant — substitution doesn't enter the *se*-clause.
- **The *tenho falado* register error.** Brazilian students writing EP-style *tenho falado* without an adverb sound stiff. EP students writing BP-style *tenho falado ultimamente* are correct but the adverb redundant.
- **Polite-request *queria* is shared, but EP relies on it more.** *Quereria* is dead in EP (real-session trap documented). *Gostaria* is sometimes substituted by *gostava* in EP. BP keeps both *queria* and *gostaria* alive in equivalent register.
- **Variant-identification is probabilistic, not deterministic.** A formal EP passage may use condicional simples (no Type-2 substitution) and look BP-like by tense. Use multiple cues — clitic placement is the most reliable single cue.

---

## Unit 136 — BP vs EP — vocabulário regional (catálogo por domínio)

*Slug: `b2-bp-ep-vocabulario-regional` · Sequence position: 89.7 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `bp-vs-ep-distinctions`, `false-cognates`

### Outcomes

After this unit, the student can:

- Recognize the most common lexical divergences across daily-life domains (transport, housing, food, technology, body, clothing, family, education)
- Choose appropriate vocabulary for either variant context — order coffee in Lisbon vs São Paulo, ask for a bus in Porto vs Rio, mention furniture in Coimbra vs Salvador
- Avoid the cross-variant vocabulary mishaps that mark a learner as variant-confused

### Vocabulary

The catalog is organized by domain. **The first column shows the BP form; the second shows the EP form.** Where forms are shared (used in both), they're noted as such.

### Transport

| BP | EP | English |
|---|---|---|
| trem | comboio | train |
| ônibus | autocarro | bus |
| metrô | metro | subway / metro |
| caminhão | camião | truck |
| trem-bala | comboio de alta velocidade | high-speed train |
| pedágio | portagem | toll |
| estacionamento | parque de estacionamento | parking lot |
| ponto de ônibus | paragem | bus stop |

### Housing

| BP | EP | English |
|---|---|---|
| banheiro | casa de banho | bathroom |
| geladeira | frigorífico | refrigerator |
| aluguel | renda / aluguer | rent |
| terno | fato | suit (clothing) |
| escritório | escritório (shared) | office |
| sala | sala (shared) | living room |
| privada / vaso sanitário | sanita | toilet |
| chuveiro | chuveiro (shared) | shower |
| pia | lavatório / pia | sink |
| cobertor | cobertor (shared) | blanket |
| sacada | varanda | balcony |
| apartamento | apartamento (shared) | apartment |

### Food and drink

| BP | EP | English |
|---|---|---|
| café da manhã | pequeno-almoço | breakfast |
| almoço | almoço (shared) | lunch |
| jantar | jantar (shared) | dinner |
| suco | sumo | juice |
| sorvete | gelado | ice cream |
| açougue | talho | butcher shop |
| padaria | padaria (shared) | bakery |
| bala | rebuçado | candy / sweet |
| chiclete | pastilha elástica | chewing gum |
| bacon | bacon / toucinho fumado | bacon |
| presunto | fiambre / presunto (cured) | ham |
| xícara | chávena | cup |
| copo | copo (shared) | glass (drinking) |
| garçom | empregado de mesa | waiter |
| conta (restaurante) | conta (shared) | bill / check |

### Technology

| BP | EP | English |
|---|---|---|
| celular | telemóvel | mobile phone |
| tela | ecrã | screen |
| arquivo (de computador) | ficheiro | file (computer) |
| mouse | rato | mouse (computer) |
| computador | computador (shared) | computer |
| fone de ouvido | auscultadores | headphones |
| caixa de som | coluna | speaker (audio) |
| internet | internet (shared) | internet |

### Clothing

| BP | EP | English |
|---|---|---|
| terno | fato | suit |
| meia (curta ou longa) | peúga | sock |
| calça | calças (always plural) | trousers / pants |
| tênis | sapatilhas | sneakers |
| camiseta | t-shirt / camisola | T-shirt |
| moletom | sweatshirt / camisola | sweatshirt |
| cueca | cuecas (always plural) | underwear |
| sutiã | soutien | bra |

### Body

| BP | EP | English |
|---|---|---|
| bunda | rabo | butt (informal) |
| barriga | barriga (shared) | stomach |
| panturrilha | barriga da perna / gémeo | calf (leg) |
| dedão | dedo grande do pé | big toe |

### Family

| BP | EP | English |
|---|---|---|
| vovô / vovó | avô / avó | grandfather / grandmother (BP forms more colloquial) |
| pai / mãe | pai / mãe (shared) | father / mother |
| irmão / irmã | irmão / irmã (shared) | brother / sister |
| neto / neta | neto / neta (shared) | grandson / granddaughter |

### Education and work

| BP | EP | English |
|---|---|---|
| escola | escola (shared) | school |
| faculdade | faculdade / universidade (shared) | college / university |
| professor / professora | professor / professora (shared) | teacher |
| sala de aula | sala de aula (shared) | classroom |
| prova | teste / prova | test / exam |
| aula | aula (shared) | class |
| nota | nota (shared) | grade |
| currículo | currículo (shared) | curriculum / résumé |
| emprego | emprego (shared) | job |

### Grammar

This unit is primarily a vocabulary catalog. There's no grammatical pattern beyond the lexical divergence itself.

### Same-form-different-meaning false friends

A few words exist in both variants with **different meanings** — a higher-stakes type of trap:

| Word | BP meaning | EP meaning |
|---|---|---|
| **propina** | bribe (illegal payment) | tuition (legal university fee) |
| **rapariga** | (regional, sometimes pejorative for a young woman) | girl / young woman (neutral, daily-use) |
| **bicha** | (slur — pejorative) | queue / line (neutral) |
| **camisola** | nightgown | T-shirt / sweatshirt |
| **fato** | event / situation / fact | suit (clothing) |

These false friends across variants are the most embarrassing errors. *Vou pegar a bicha* in EP means "I'm going to get in line"; in BP it's offensive.

### Same-form-same-meaning items

Most vocabulary is shared. The catalog above shows the divergent items; the unmarked majority of words (*água, casa, livro, comer, dormir, falar, gostar*…) work identically in both variants.

### Exemplar mini-paragraphs

Same content, BP vs EP:

**BP:**
> *Hoje de manhã peguei o ônibus para o trabalho. No café da manhã comi pão com presunto e bebi suco de laranja. Almocei na padaria perto do escritório.*

**EP:**
> *Hoje de manhã apanhei o autocarro para o trabalho. No pequeno-almoço comi pão com fiambre e bebi sumo de laranja. Almocei na padaria perto do escritório.*

(Note: *padaria* and *escritório* are shared; the change is mostly in *pegar/apanhar*, *ônibus/autocarro*, *café da manhã/pequeno-almoço*, *presunto/fiambre*, *suco/sumo*.)

### Drills & artifacts

<!-- TODO: build a domain-organized vocabulary drill (transport / food / housing / etc.) with BP↔EP translation prompts. Build a false-friend awareness drill specifically for propina, rapariga, bicha, camisola, fato. -->

### Traps

- **Asking for *trem* in Lisbon yields blank looks.** Use *comboio*. Same in reverse: *comboio* in São Paulo will be parsed as a Portuguese-from-Portugal usage.
- **Saying *casa de banho* in Brazil sounds formal/foreign.** Use *banheiro*. Same in reverse: *banheiro* in EP can be parsed as Brazilian or as referring to a baby's bath area.
- **The false friends are the highest-stakes errors.** *Propina* in EP context (asking about university fees) is fine; in BP context it accuses someone of accepting bribes. *Bicha* in EP is "queue" — neutral; in BP it's a slur. **Always check variant context before using these words.**
- **Some shared words have register asymmetry.** *Vovô / vovó* is universal in BP for grandparents; in EP, *avô / avó* is the standard form (vovô / vovó exists but reads as Brazilian-influenced or affectionate). Default to *avô / avó* when writing for an EP audience.
- **Plural-only clothing items.** *Calças* (trousers) and *cuecas* (underwear) are plural in both variants but BP often uses singular *calça* informally. EP keeps them rigorously plural.
- **The catalog above is starter content, not exhaustive.** Real working vocabulary divergence covers hundreds of items. Use this as a recognition framework; expand domain-by-domain as you encounter real text in either variant.
- **Don't conflate variant divergence with archaism.** Some BP/EP differences reflect older Portuguese forms preserved differently; others are recent neologisms diverging in real time. The catalog above is current standard; older texts may show different distributions.

## Unit 148 — Subjunctive in All Contexts

*Slug: `b2-subj-broad` · Sequence position: 500.02 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `subjunctive-broad`

### Outcomes

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 (sparse CEFR-only unit) -->

### Grammar

## Unit 149 — Conditional Sentences (Full System)

*Slug: `b2-condicionais-sistema` · Sequence position: 500.03 · CEFR: B2 · Variant: shared*

**Concepts:** `conditional-sentences`

### Outcomes

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 (sparse CEFR-only unit) -->

### Vocabulary

<!-- TODO: enrich in Phase 3 -->

### Grammar

- Real conditions: Se chover, fico em casa (future subj)
- Hypothetical present: Se eu fosse rico, viajaria (imperfect subj)
- Hypothetical past: Se eu tivesse estudado, teria passado
- Mixed conditionals
